The Self as Perception:
The Self as Perception 

Sheikh al Mishri (ra) said in Kitab al-Jami regarding Shaikh al-Tijani (ra): 

“I also asked him about the true reality of the human being: is it the spirit (rūḥ), or the body (jism), or both together?
He replied: “It is neither the spirit nor the body.”
I said to him: “We have written, following your words, that it is the spirit, and that it is the one addressed and intended by divine obligation.”
He (may God be pleased with him) said: “That was my view in the past—the view of the gnostics—and that is why I had replied as you recorded. But today it has been made clear to me otherwise: that the human being is neither spirit nor body, but rather the perception (idrāk) generated between them when they come together.”

I said: “If that is the case, then why is the spirit punished or rewarded?” He said: “Affliction or bliss befalls it by God’s decree, as with other created things—not because it disbelieved or disobeyed. For from the moment God created it, it has been knowing, aware, remembering, and has never ceased from the remembrance of God for even the blink of an eye. This contradicts the description of the disbeliever which God mentioned in His Book—ignorance, heedlessness, and other blameworthy traits. Likewise, the body constantly remembers God the Exalted and never ceases, for His saying: ‘There is nothing but that it glorifies Him with His praise.’ Thus, it is one of the things that glorify, and this is a praiseworthy quality that merits only bliss and praise—so how could it be punished?”

I said to him: “Then how do we understand the reports that speak of the reward or punishment of the spirit and the body?” He said: “That occurs to them only due to their association with the human being—meaning that perception which arises between them upon their union.”

Our master supported the truth of what he had said, saying: “If the human being were the spirit, as some claim, he would necessarily know all that his spirit contains of knowledges, secrets, and unveilings—but he does not. And it is known that a person knows what his own innermost self contains, as is experientially evident. Hence, it becomes clear that the human being is not identical with his spirit. There are further proofs, but mentioning them would take us too far.”

It was said to our master (may God be pleased with him): “Perception is a meaning, not a substance (jawhar), so how can we judge it to be a ‘thing’?” He replied: “That is only according to the limited circle of the human intellect. But in relation to God, all realities are equal—substances and accidents alike—as has been reported regarding the forms of deeds in the grave and beyond, which none can deny. Once this is established, there is no difference in addressing realities, whether substantial or accidental.”

“So, once you understand this,” he continued, “God the Exalted is fully able to create a perception at the conjunction of spirit and body, to name it ‘human being,’ and to address it—and there is no rational objection to this.

Then it was said to him: ‘If reason allows this, then why is that perception not independent on its own, apart from spirit and body, since divine power is capable of creating it separately, as you mentioned, and making it truly conscious in itself?’ He replied: ‘It has already been determined in God’s eternal knowledge that it would not exist except when they are joined, and none can contest His crafting. He is not questioned about what He does.’

I said: ‘If this is accepted, then to which does perception belong—spirit or body?’
He said: ‘It belongs to the spirit so long as it remains in the body, for perception is within it; and when the spirit departs, perception departs with it, leaving the body inert like a stone.’

I said: ‘This is with regard to the generality of creation. But as for God’s chosen elect among His servants, perception does not leave their bodies when the spirit departs, just as it remains with their spirits. For this reason, it is reported that they continue worshipping God after death just as they did before it—and this applies only to those in whom perception remains.’

Do not be misled by the Prophet’s saying (peace and blessings be upon him): ‘Whoever greets me, God returns my soul to me so that I may return his greeting.’ It does not mean that his noble body lacks perception—far from it! Rather, he is perceiving even as in worldly life. The return of the noble spirit to the blessed body at the moment of responding to the greeting is a distinction and an honor for the one who greeted him. That is the benefit of the spirit’s return to the pure body.“
---
The Ranks/Rows in the Hereafter:
The Ranks/Rows in the Hereafter 

مراتب الخلق في الآخرة

قال سيدنا رضي الله عنه : الخلق في الآخرة ثلاثة أصناف

الصنف الأول: سهم الرضا منه سبحانه وتعالى وهم الصديقون، والأقطاب، والنبيون، والمرسلون.

وصنف هم سهم الرحمة وفي هذا عموم الأولياء والصالحين والشهداء.

وصنف هم أهل العفو والمغفرة وهم عصاة المؤمنين.

ومعنى الرضا من الله هو إرادته للعبد غاية الترفيع والتعظيم والإجلال.

والرحمة هي التقلب في أطوار الشهوات والملاذ المطلوبات والنعم المتواترات.

وأهل العفو والمغفرة يعفو عنهم ويغفر أوزارهم.

وأما رضا العبد عن الله بالثبوت لما يجري عليه من البلايا والمحن فهذا مخصوص ببعض الصديقين.

ومعنى الصديق هو كمال صحوه من غرق المشاهدة حتى يصير كحالة العامة من يراه يقول هذا ليس بمدرك شيئًا ويعطي المراتب حقها من الحقية والخلقية.

قال بعض التابعين لابن سيرين رضي الله عنه، وهو من أكابر التابعين، صحب كثيرًا من الصحابة - قال له : كيف كانت الصحابة؟ قال: كالناس، ثم أنشد بيتا :

يحب الخمر من كاس الندامي

ويكره أن تفارقه الفلوس

وأما الصنف الرابع وهم الأعلون حيث قال تعالى في حقهم: ﴿ يُحِبُّهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ ﴾ [المائدة: ٥٤] وهم أكبر من أهل الرضا المخصوصين بمحبة الذات

العلية.

٤٧

Ranks of Creation in the Hereafter

Our master, may Allah be pleased with him, said: “Creation in the Hereafter consists of three categories.”

The first category: Those who are the share of Allah’s rida (satisfaction), and they are the truthful ones (siddiqoon), the poles (aqtab), the prophets (nabiyyoon), and the messengers (mursaloon).

The second category: Those who are the share of His rahma (mercy), and this includes the general ranks of the saints (awliya), the righteous (salihun), and the martyrs (shuhada).

The third category: Those who are the people of pardon (afu) and forgiveness (maghfira), and they are the disobedient believers.

The meaning of rida from Allah is His will for the servant to attain the utmost elevation, exaltation, and honor.
Rahma refers to the immersion in layers of pleasures, delights, and blessings that continuously flow.
As for the people of pardon and forgiveness, Allah pardons them and forgives their sins.

However, the rida of a servant with Allah—being steadfast in facing trials and tribulations—is specific to some of the truthful ones (siddiqoon).

The meaning of siddiq is someone who has perfected their clarity after emerging from the depths of spiritual witnessing, to the point where they appear like the common folk. Whoever sees them may think they perceive nothing extraordinary, yet they give each station its due, whether divine or created.

One of the followers of Ibn Sirin—may Allah be pleased with him, who was among the greatest of the followers (tabi’un) and had accompanied many companions—asked him: “How were the companions?” He replied: “Like ordinary people.” Then he recited a verse of poetry: “He loves wine from the cup of companions, Yet dislikes to part with his coins.”

As for the fourth category, they are the highest ranks, regarding whom Allah says:
“He loves them, and they love Him” [Qur’an 5:54]. They are greater than those of rida, being uniquely endowed with love of the divine essence (dhat al-‘uluw).

———————————————————————

 من الصديقين والأقطاب والنبيين والمرسلين فيه تسامح؛ وما ذكر قبل لأنهم أهل المحبة الذاتية.

فالناس حينئذ مذنبون، وموفون بعهود الله ، وخاصة، وخاصة الخاصة.

فالمذنبون معلومون، والموفون بعهد الله هم طوائف المؤمنين؛ من حفظ العهود، ورعي الحدود، إلا أنهم أصحاب حجاب.

فالمذنبون سهم العفو، والموفون بعهد الله سهم الرحمة، والخاصة هم الذين انكشفت لهم صفات الله تعالى من وراء سبحات الجلال فإذاقتهم لذة تلك المشاهدة وإن حملوا ما تطيقه الجبال من البلايا والمحن، فهم خاصة الله من خلقه، وهم أهل الدرجة العليا.

والطائفة الرابعة هم الذين انخرقت لهم جميع الحجب، حتى وصلوا إلى محبة الذات العليا، وهم خاصة الخاصة، فهم أكبر رتبة وأعلى منزلة من الذين قبلهم، وهم أهل شهود الصفات، هم أهل الرضا منه سبحانه وتعالى رضي الله

عنهم ورضوا عنه.

وأما خاصة الخاصة فقد قال في حقهم ﴿ تُحِبُّهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ فهم أهل الرتبة العالية، لا رتبة فوقهم، وفي هذه المرتبة الصديقون والأقطاب والنبيون والمرسلون؛ لأن الصديقية تجمع الجميع فكل نبي وولي ورسول صديق، ولا عكس، يقول سبحانه وتعالى في حق إبراهيم عليه السلام وهو من أكبر الرسل مقامًا قال فيه : إِنَّهُ كَانَ صِدِّيقًا نَّبِيًّا ﴾ [مريم : ٤١] فالصديقية جامعة ولا عکس.

وأما محبة الله لهؤلاء الأكابر فهو إرادته بهم غاية التعظيم والإجلال والتكريم والترفيع.

٤٨

Among the truthful ones (ṣiddīqīn), the spiritual poles (aqṭāb), the prophets (nabiyyīn), and the messengers (mursalīn), there is a distinction; what was mentioned before refers to those who possess intrinsic love (maḥabba dhātiyya).

At that time, people are divided into sinners, those who fulfill the covenants of Allah, the elect (khāṣṣa), and the most elect (khāṣṣat al-khāṣṣa).
	•	The sinners are known.
	•	Those who fulfill the covenants of Allah are groups of believers who safeguard the covenants and observe the limits, yet they remain veiled (aṣḥāb ḥijāb).

Thus,
	•	The sinners belong to the lot of divine pardon (ʿafw).
	•	Those who fulfill the covenant of Allah belong to the lot of divine mercy (raḥma).
	•	The elect (khāṣṣa) are those for whom the attributes of Allah have been unveiled beyond the dazzling lights of His Majesty (subuḥāt al-jalāl), allowing them to taste the sweetness of that vision. Even if they endure trials and tribulations that mountains themselves could not bear, they are the chosen ones (khāṣṣat Allāh) among His creation and the people of the highest rank.
	•	The fourth group are those for whom all veils have been torn away until they have reached the love of the Supreme Essence (maḥabbat al-dhāt al-ʿulyā). They are the most elect (khāṣṣat al-khāṣṣa), ranking higher than all others before them. They are the people of witnessing (ahl al-shuhūd) of divine attributes and the people of Allah’s pleasure, as He is pleased with them and they are pleased with Him.

As for the most elect (khāṣṣat al-khāṣṣa), Allah has spoken of them, saying:

﴿يُحِبُّهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ﴾
“He loves them, and they love Him.” (Qur’an 5:54)

They are the people of the highest station, beyond which there is no rank above. In this rank are the truthful ones (ṣiddīqīn), the spiritual poles (aqṭāb), the prophets (nabiyyīn), and the messengers (mursalīn), because ṣiddīqiyya (absolute truthfulness) encompasses all of them. Every prophet, saint, and messenger is a ṣiddīq, but not the other way around.

Allah Almighty says about Ibrahim (peace be upon him), who is among the greatest of the messengers in rank:

﴿إِنَّهُ كَانَ صِدِّيقًا نَّبِيًّا﴾
“Indeed, he was a truthful one (ṣiddīq) and a prophet.” (Qur’an 19:41)

Thus, ṣiddīqiyya is all-encompassing, but the reverse is not necessarily true.

As for Allah’s love for these great figures, it is His will to grant them the highest degree of honor, exaltation, veneration, and elevation.

—————

وهي

وأما محبتهم له سبحانه وتعالى فإنما يحبون ذاته العلية المقدسة لا لا تعقل ولا تكيف وإنما يعقلها من ذاقها.

وفي معنى هذا قال المرسي رضي الله عنه : إن الله عبادا يظهرهم في البداية، ويسترهم في النهاية، وإن الله عبادًا يسترهم في البداية ويظهرهم في النهاية، وإن الله عبادًا يسترهم عن العامة، ويظهرهم للخاصة، وإن الله عبادا ضن بهم عن الخاصة والعامة، فلا يظهر حقيقة ما بينهم وبينه حتى للحفظة فمن سواهم، حتى يتوفى أرواحهم بيده، فهم شهداء الملكوت الأعلى، وهم أهل الصف الأيمن من العرش، فهؤلاء خاصة الخاصة جعلنا الله منهم جميعا بمنه وكرمه. ما أملاه علينا رضي الله عنه. انتهى

معنى : ﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينَا مِمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ )

وسألته رضي الله عنه عن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِّمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنُ ﴾ الآية [النساء: ١٢٥].

فأجاب رضي الله عنه بقوله معناه : أنه لا أحد أحسن دينا ممن أسلم وجهه الله وهو محسن كما قال في الآية الأخرى: ﴿وَمَن يُسْلِمْ وَجْهَهُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ * الآية [لقمان: ٢٢].

والوجهة هنا التي يسلمها إلى الله هي توجه القلب إلى الله تعالى بالإدبار عن كل ما سواه.

١١ - يقول : إن الله لا ينظر إلى صوركم وأعمالكم ولكن ينظر إلى

(١١) م : ( ٤ / ١٩٨٧ رقم ٣٣ - ٣٤ / ٢٥٦٤) (٤٥) كتاب البر والصلة (١٠) باب تحريم ظلم المسلم - من حديث أبي هريرة.

ولفظه: «إن الله لا ينظر إلى أجسادكم ، ولا إلى صوركم ولكن ينظر إلى قلوبكم وأشار بإصبعه إلى صدره.

٤٩

And as for their love for Him, Exalted and Most High, they love His exalted and sacred essence—without rationalizing it or defining it in any particular way. Rather, only the one who has tasted it can truly comprehend it.

Regarding this, al-Mursi (may Allah be pleased with him) said:

“Indeed, Allah has servants whom He manifests in the beginning and conceals in the end. And He has servants whom He conceals in the beginning and manifests in the end. And He has servants whom He hides from the common people but reveals to the elect. And He has servants whom He has withheld from both the elect and the common people, so that the reality of what is between them and Him remains hidden—even from the recording angels and all others—until He Himself takes their souls. These are the witnesses of the highest dominion, the people of the right side of the Throne. They are the most elect of the elect. May Allah make us all among them by His grace and generosity.”

This is what he dictated to us (may Allah be pleased with him). End quote.

Meaning of the Verse:

﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾
“And who is better in religion than one who submits his face to Allah while being a doer of good?” (Qur’an 4:125)

I asked him (may Allah be pleased with him) about the meaning of Allah’s statement:

﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِّمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾ (Surah An-Nisa: 125)

He replied (may Allah be pleased with him), saying:

“Its meaning is that no one has a better religion than the one who submits his face to Allah while being a doer of good, as stated in another verse: ﴿وَمَن يُسْلِمْ وَجْهَهُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾ (Surah Luqman: 22).”

Here, the “face” that is submitted to Allah refers to the heart’s complete turning toward Allah and its turning away from everything else besides Him.

The Hadith:

The Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said:

“Indeed, Allah does not look at your forms or your deeds, but He looks at your hearts.”

(Reported by Abu Huraira, recorded in Sahih Muslim, Book of Righteousness and Relations, Chapter: The Prohibition of Wronging a Muslim, Hadith No. 1987 & 2564).

And in one narration:

“Indeed, Allah does not look at your bodies or your appearances, but He looks at your hearts,” and he (the Prophet) pointed to his chest with his finger.
---
Reality of Ma’iyya and Qurb:
Reality of Ma’iyya and Qurb 

“Here is an example to clarify something of this domain, if you grasp it—it is in the created (ḥādith), not in the Eternal (qadīm): a man from among the people of Paradise, for instance, has from among the houris a number that surpasses by multiples the number of angels, and yet he couples with all of them at one and the same moment, tasting the pleasure of each one individually according to her own specificity in that very same moment.

He couples with each of them fully, in his single bodily place and his singular essence, without any multiplication in his essence nor in his locus. There is no multiplicity of the moment, no before or after, and no confusion among their bodies in a single place. However, comprehension of this in this worldly abode is beyond the capacity of reason and sense—but within the expanse of divine power, it is entirely possible.

And although the adherents of rational limitations may not accept this, it is supported by sound reports in the traditions, which have been established in the ḥadīth” (622, Kitab al-Jami )

إِلَيِّهِ لِلعَفْلِ وَالفِكْرِ، كَذَلِكَ تَعَقُّلُ هَاتَيْنِ الصِّفَتَيْنِ مَعِيَّةً وَقُرْباً لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ مِن الْمَوْجُودَاتِ، تَعَلُّقُهُمَا مِنْ وَرَاءٍ طَوْرِ العَفْلِ وَالحِسِّ، فَلَا اتَّصَالَ وَلَا الْغِصَالَ وَلَا مَسَافَةً لِلقُرْبِ وَالبُعْدِ، وَلَا أَيْيَّةَ وَلَا حُلُولَ وَلَا مَكَانا وَلَا دُخُولاً وَلَا خُرُوجا ، وَلَا تَتَعَدَّدُ الذَّاتُ بِتَعَدُّدِهَا بِالمَعِيَّةِ.
وَدُونَكَ وَجْها يُوَضِّحُ لَكَ شَيْئا مِنْ هَذَا المَيْدَانِ إِنْ عَقِلْتَهُ، فَهُوَ فِي الحَادِثِ فَقَطْ دُونَ القَدِيمِ، فَإِنَّ الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الجَنَّةِ عِنْدَهُ مَثَلاً مِنَ الحُورِ مَا يَتَضَاعَفُ عَلَى عَدَدِ المَلَائِكَةِ بِأَضْعَافٍ مُضَاعَفَةٍ، وَمَعَ ذَلِكَ يُجَامِعُهُنَّ فِي الآنِ الوَاحِدِ، وَيَذُوقُ لَذَّةَ كُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ بِانْفِرَادِهَا عَلَى اخْتِصَاصِهَا فِي ذَلِكَ الآنِ الوَاحِدِ، وَيُجَامِعُ كُلَّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُنَّ جِمَاعاً مُتَمَكِّناً بِمَحَلِّهِ الوَاحِدِ وَذَاتِهِ الوَاحِدَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَعَدُّدٍ فِي ذَاتِهِ وَلَا فِي مَحَلّهِ، وَلَا تَعَدُّدَ لِلآنِ وَلَا تَقْدِيم وَلَا تَأْخِيرَ وَلَا اشْتِبَاكَ فِي ذَوَاتِهِنَّ فِي مَحَلَّ وَاحِدٍ، إِلَّا أَنَّ تَعَقُّلَ هَذَا فِي هَذِهِ الدَّارِ مِنْ وَرَاءٍ طَوْرِ العَقْلِ وَالحِسِّ، لَكِنَّهُ فِي سَعَةِ القُدْرَةِ الإِلَمِيّةِ وَاقِعٌ.
وَهَذَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يُسَلَّمْهُ أَرْبَابُ الحُدُودِ العَقْلِيَّةِ فَقَدْ دَلَّتْ عَلَيْهِ الأَخْبَارُ الصَّحِيحَةُ بِمَا تَقَرَّرَ فِي الحَدِيثِ أَيْ مَعْنَاهُ مِنْ أَنَّ الرَّجُلَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الجَنَّةِ يُجَامِعُ نِسَاءَهٌ فِي مِقْدَارِ

---
“On the Neglect of Prophetic Tawḥīd and the Rise of Kalām: A Statement…:
“On the Neglect of Prophetic Tawḥīd and the Rise of Kalām: A Statement by Shaykh Aḥmad al-Tijānī”
(from al-Mishrī, Kitāb al-Jāmiʿ, pp. 66–67)

“I know the ailment, so I have no need for the remedy. That is all.”

As for your question, “if what is intended is not the tawḥīd (monotheism) of the mutakallimūn (theologians)—which someone like Ibn al-Mubārak (may Allah be pleased with him) and his likes certainly could not be ignorant of—then why did they not make this tawḥīd manifest in books and treatises so its benefit could become widespread, and so on…?”

The answer:
They did not conceal it. Indeed, that is the tawḥīd with which all the messengers were sent. It is the very tawḥīd that they used to proclaim to the masses of creation. However, the path to it was abandoned and eventually effaced only because the general public turned away from it, inclining instead toward the rhetorical embellishments of kalām theology and engaging with its rational proofs and epistemological gradations. They assumed that this was the ultimate goal in drawing near to God and in attaining complete knowledge of Him—whereas in truth, that path is the furthest one from God and leads only to misguidance.

The reason the common people fell into this was their mingling with the sciences of the early philosophers. They found that these philosophers had defined “true knowledge of tawḥīd” as the study of divine matters through rational principles and logical preliminaries. So Allah diverted them, through that path, away from knowledge of the Truth and its fruits, and away from the nearness that draws one close to Him and to knowledge of His majesty.

As for the Companions, since they did not mix with these philosophical sciences, they remained steadfast upon the tawḥīd of the messengers, whose ripe fruit they harvested, and whose sweet taste they personally experienced. This tawḥīd stemmed from the clear and divine revelations found in the Books of God, which He sent to His creation along with His messengers, and from the words of the messengers as they taught the people knowledge of God’s grandeur and majesty.

But when, in the third generation (the tābiʿ al-tābiʿīn), the sciences of the philosophers entered into the ummah, and they heard within those sciences strange and dazzling flourishes in the field of tawḥīd, which appealed to the curious hearts of those disinclined toward God—then whoever among them acquired such knowledge began to wield it against the commoners and the unlearned, claiming that the level he had reached was the ultimate end of knowledge of God and of His majesty. They even began to proclaim among the masses that whoever was ignorant of these things was essentially ignorant of all knowledge.

So the souls of the people followed them, out of their strong inclination toward novelty and wonder. They saw how these individuals were held in the utmost esteem by the masses, by kings, and by princes. And so, as generations passed—one following another—without any challenger or critic, the knowledge of tawḥīd brought by the messengers was forgotten. Those who continued to walk the path of the messengers’ tawḥīd and turned away from the philosophers’ tawḥīd came to be known as Ṣūfīs and ʿārifīn (gnostics). Those who followed the philosophers’ tawḥīd came to be called theologians and scholars of kalām.

As for those among the gnostics who engaged with the science of kalām—like al-Ashʿarī, al-Sanūsī, and others (may Allah be pleased with them)—they only did so out of gentleness and mercy toward the common folk. When they saw that the people would not accept the tawḥīd of the messengers except by the sword, they instead descended to their level by formulating rational arguments that the people could grasp within themselves, so they might choose to obey God of their own volition. They saw that this was better than the sword, since one who enters religion by compulsion and coercion does so without sincere faith.

This, then, is the reason they descended into the science of kalām.

أَعْرِفُ الدَّاءَ فَلَيْسَتْ بِيَ حَاجَةٌ إِلَى الدَّوَاءِ. انْتَهَى.
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُكَ: إِذَا كَانَ غَيْرَ تَوْحِيدِ المُتَكَلَّمِينَ الَّذِي لَا يَجْهَلُهُ ابْنُ المُبَارَكِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَأمْثَالَهُ، فَمَا بَالُهُمْ لَمْ يُظْهِرُوهُ فِي الكُتُبِ وَالدَّوَاوِينِ حَتَّى يَعُمَّ نَفْعُهُ. إِلَخْ..
الجَوَابُ: إِنَّهُمْ مَا كَتَمُوهُ، وَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ التَّوْحِيدَ هُوَ الَّذِي بُعِتَتْ بِهِ الرُّسُلُ كُلُّهَا، وَهُوَ الَّذِي يُظْهِرُونَهُ لِعَامَّةِ الخَلْقِ، وَإِنَّمَا تُرِكَ وَدُرِسَتْ طَرِيقُهُ لإِعْرَاضِ عَامَّةِ النَّاسِ عَنْهُ، لِمَيْلِهِمْ إِلَى شَقَاشِقٍ عِلْمِ الكَلَامِ وَالبَحْثِ فِي قَوَاعِدِهِ وَأُصُولِهِ بِالحُجَجِ العَقْلِيَّةِ وَالمَقَامَاتِ اليَقِينِيَّةِ ظَنَا مِنْهُمْ أَنَّ تِلْكَ هِيَ الغَايَةُ القُصْوَى فِي التَّقَرُّبِ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَكَمَالِ العِلْمِ بِهِ، وَجَهِلُوا أَنَّ ذَلِكَ هُوَ غَايَةُ البُعْدِ عَنِ اللَّهِ وَالضَّلَالِ.
فَإِنَّ السَّبَبَ الَّذِي أَوْقَعَ العَامَّةَ فِي هَذَا هُوَ مُخَالَطَتُهُمْ لِعُلُومِ أَوَائِل الفَلَاسِفَةِ، فَوَجَدُوهُمْ قَرِّرُوا فِي عُلُومِهِمْ : عِلْمُ التَّوْحِيدِ الحَقِّي هُوَ البَحْثُ فِي العِلْمِ الإِلَهِيِّ بِالقَوَاعِدِ العَقْلِيَّةِ وَالمُقَدِّمَاتِ المَنْطِقِيَّةِ، فَصَرَفَهُمْ اللّهُ بِذَلِكَ عَنْ مَعْرِفَةِ الحَقِّ وَمَآلِهِ، وَعَنِ التَّقَرُّبِ بِمَا يُقَرَّبُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَمَعْرِفَةِ جَلَالِهِ، وَحَيْثُ كَانَ الصَّحَابِةُ لَمْ يُخَالِطُوا هَذَا العِلْمَ، كَانُوا قَائِمِينَ عَلَى تَوْجِيدِ الرُسُلِ الَّذِي كَانَ جَنَاءُ ثُمَارِهِ، وَذَوْقُ حَلَاوَةٍ يَانِعِهِ مِنْ صَرِيحِ الأَحْبَارِ الإِلَهِّةِ

فِي كُتُبِ اللَّهِ الَّتِي بَعَتَهَا إِلَى خَلْقِهِ مَعَ رُسُلِهِ، وَمَا نَطَقَتْ بِهِ رُسُلُهُ فِي تَعْلِيمِ العَامَّةِ مِنَ العِلْمِ وَمَعْرِفَةِ عَظَمَتِهِ وَجَلَالِهِ.
فَلَمَّا دَخَلَ عَلَى الصَّدْرِ الثَّالِثِ عُلُومُ الفَلَاسِفَةِ وَسَمِعُوا فِيهَا فِي فَنّ التَّوْحِيدِ شَقَاشِقَ غَرِيبَةً تَسْتَحْلِيهَا نُفُوسُ أَهْلِ الفُضُولِ المُعْرِضِينَ عَنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَكُلُّ مَنْ حَصَّلَهَا مِنْهُمْ صَالَ بِهَا عَلَى العَامَّةِ وَالجَاهِلِينَ بِهَا مُدَّعِياً أَنَّ الَّذِي وَصَلَ إِلَيْهِ فِي رُتْبَةِ العِلْمِ هُوَ الغَايَةُ القُصْوَى فِي العِلْمِ بِاللَّهِ وَمَعْرِفَةِ جَلَالِهِ، وَيَصْرُخُونَ عَلَى العَامَّةِ : إِنَّ مَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُهَا كَأَنَّهُ لَا يَعْلَمُ شَيْئاً مِنَ العِلْمِ، فَتَبِعَتْهُمْ نُفُوسُ العَامَّةِ لِشِدَّةِ مَيْلِهَا إِلَى الفُضُولِ، حَيْثُ رَأَوْا لَهُمْ التَّعْظِيمَ البَالِغَ الغَايَة فِي قُلُوبِ العَامَّةِ وَالمُلُوكِ وَالأُمَرَاءِ، فَبِسَبَبِ تَتَابُع الأَعْصَارِ عَلَى هَذَا سَلَفاً عَنْ خَلَفٍ مِنْ غَيْرِ مُعَارِضٍ وَلَا زَاجِرِ نُسِيَ عِلْمُ التَّوْحِيدِ الَّذِي بُعِثَتْ بِهِ الرُّسُلُ، وَصَارَ السَّالِكُونَ عَلَى تَوْحِيدِ الرُّسُلِ المُعْرِضُونَ عَلَى تَوْحِيدِ الفَلَاسِفَةِ هُمْ المُسَمُّونَ بِالصُّوفِيَةِ وَالعَارِفِينَ، وَصَارَ السَّالِكُونَ عَلَى تَوْحِيدِ الفَلَاسِفَةِ هُمْ المُسَمُّونَ بِأَهْلِ عِلْمِ الكَلَامِ.
وَأَمّا مَنْ تَنَزَّلَ إِلَى فَنّ عِلْمِ الكَلَامِ مِنَ العَارِفِينَ كَالأَشْعَرِيِّ وَالسَّنُوسِيِّ وَأَمْثَالِهِمَا رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ إِنَّمَا أَرَادُوا الرَّفْقَ بِالعَامَةِ لَمَّا كَانَ تَوْجِيدُ الرُّسُلِ لَا يَسْتَجِيبُونَ لَهُ إِلَّا بِالسَّيْفِ، تَنَزَّلُوا لَهُمْ بِتَقْرِيرِ حُجَجٍ عَقْلِيَّةِ يُدْرِكُونَهَا فِي نُقُوسِهِمْ، لِيَسْتَجِبُوا بِذَلِكَ لِأمْرِ اللَّهِ بِاخْتِيَارِهِم، رَأَوْا أَنَّ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌ مِنَ السَّيْفِ، لِكَوْنِ صَاحِبِهِ لَا يَدْخُلُ فِي الدِّينِ إِلَّا قَهْراً وَجَبْراً . فَهَذَا السَّبْبُ الَّذِي حَمَلَهُمْ عَلَى التُّزَّلِ إِلَى فَنْ عِلْمِ الكَلَامِ.
---
The Tijānī Path of Giveness:
The Tijānī Path of Giveness
In many Sufi traditions influenced by Akbarian metaphysics, maʿrifa is primarily seen as an ascent through levels of Being—a journey through tajalliyāt toward the realization of unity. While Tijānī thought certainly affirms these dimensions, it inverts the direction of the journey: rather than climbing beyond the world toward the Divine, it emphasizes the immanence of the Divine in all things. Maʿrifa is thus not only a matter of recognizing the oneness of the Real in a metaphysical sense, but relating to the Real in every circumstance, moment, givenness, and encounter.

The Tijānī preference for the term maẓāhir (sites of manifestation) over tajalliyāt (disclosures) reflects a metaphysics grounded in encounter rather than transcendence. The world is not a veil over the Real, but a medium of constant Divine encounter. This aligns maʿrifa with the ethics of responsiveness, presence, and receptivity. Hence, maʿrifa becomes something lived. SheikhTijānī and Sheikh Ibrahim speak not only of recognizing God as the sole, essential Reality, but of experiencing nearness, companionship, and intimacy (uns) with Him. God is the neighbor. 

In Sum:
Tijani thought is:
Experiential, not speculative
Immediate, not merely transcendent
Emphasizes human mediation,  especially through the Prophet ﷺ and the Shaykh
World-affirming, rather than world-negating 
It avoids the pitfalls of metaphysical abstraction while preserving the depth of mystical insight. And it aligns with the Tijānī emphasis on ṣuḥba. One simply takes up the orientation of the ʿārifīn and beloveds through osmosis. Maʿrifa for the Tijānīya is ʿurf, and perfected through companionship—not intellectual ascent or assent.

The Tijānī preference for the term maẓāhir—sites of manifestation—over tajalliyāt, or divine disclosures, is more than a lexical distinction. It marks a metaphysical orientation: one that affirms immediate encounter over transcendence, intimacy over distance, and giveness over ascent. In this vision, the world is not a veil that obscures the Real, but a site of encounter for those with hearts gifted with the requisite constitution (I.e., Jud).

In the Tijānī path, maʿrifa is is a gift, a grace given to those whom God wills. The seeker does not transcend the world to reach God; the arif— to encounter Him perpetually through—jūd)— and to respond with ḥamd. 

There is no metaphysical shift from Names to Essence, no progression from theophanies to some hidden kernel. God does not change. The Real is not veiled. The only shift is in the sight of the one who witnesses—the opening of the inner eye, and the vision made hadid. What was always there is now seen as it is.

The Tijānī Re-reading of Tajallī and Maẓhar
In the classical Islamic metaphysical tradition, tajallī has long been central to understanding the dynamic relationship between the One (al-Ḥaqq) and the manifold forms of the cosmos. In the thought of Ibn ʿArabī, tajallī refers to the theophanic process through which the Divine unveils Itself in various forms, each of which both reveals and conceals the Real. These forms, or ṣuwar, are seen as veils that the gnostic must transcend in order to witness the Unity of the Divine Essence behind them. Tajallī is, therefore, a metaphysical unveiling, an epistemological and ontological movement that leads the seeker from multiplicity back to the singularity of the One.

However, the Tijānī tradition, particularly in the teachings of Shaykh Ibrāhīm Niasse, reorients this metaphysical understanding by shifting from tajallī to maẓhar (plural: maẓāhir). The term maẓhar literally means a “place” or “site” of appearance or manifestation, but it carries with it a deeper sense of positionality and embodiment. In the Tijānī framework, a maẓhar is not merely a form or appearance; it is the place where and how one encounters the Divine. Unlike tajallī, which directs the ‘arif to transcend appearances, maẓhar emphasizes the importance of encountering the Divine as these very appearances—in all their manifold expressions, whether as friend, enemy, trial, or joy. The focus shifts from seeing through the veil to receiving the Divine in the encounter itself, for those who can do so. 

This distinction is crucial in understanding the Tijānī approach to maʿrifa. In Ibn ʿArabī's model, the goal is to pierce through the multiplicity of forms to unveil the singular, unified Essence of the Divine. The emphasis is on metaphysical knowledge, where forms are ultimately seen as veils concealing the One. However, in the Tijānī tradition, particularly under Shaykh Ibrāhīm Niasse’s influence, maẓāhir signal a move toward an intimate and direct mode of gnosis. The goal is not to transcend forms, but to meet God within them—to witness and respond to the Divine in all its expressions.

The implications of this shift are profound. Ma’rifa, in this sense, becomes not only an intellectual ascent toward the Divine, but a lived experience of endless giveness. This reorients the seeker’s path from abstract knowledge to gifted, embodied intimacy. The Divine is not merely an abstract Essence to be conceptualized but even the Essence is given as madhhar.

As such, the Tijaniyya understand Prophet Harun’s statement, “Whoever fails to know God in one of His levels has decreased his maʿrifa,” as emphasis of the importance of engaging with the Divine in every circumstance and situation— immediately, not as a veil to overcome. Each level of experience  is a maẓhar, a site where God is present and encountered. To truly know God is to be able to encounter Him in all of His sites of appearance—to see Him directly—not to cognizant that He lies behind the veils.

This is where the Tijānī tradition offers a unique contribution to Islamic metaphysics: it presents a theology of encounter, where the Divine is not only to be known abstractly, but to be met in the lived reality. God is given. This meeting is not deferred to the unseen, nor abstracted into a distant Essence. It is given— and that is not difficult for God. The maẓāhir invite the ‘arif to respond to God’s giveness. The encounter with God is not something distant to be transcended, but something immediate, present, and to be received as part here and now, for those graced with the ability to receive the gift. 

In sum, the Tijānī understanding of maʿrifa as relational gnosis calls for a radical rethinking of the relationship between the seeker and the Divine. It challenges the notion of a gnostic journey that ascends beyond the world in search of an abstract Essence, proposing instead a path of radical immediacy and attentiveness to the sites of Divine encounter. The maẓāhir are not veils to be transcended, but sites to be entered, encountered, and responded to. This reconfiguration offers a path of intimacy with the Divine, where the giveness of God is encountered—where the world is not a veil, but a potential setting of continuous Divine Giveness. Neither this world or the next than contain or conceal His Presence and presencing. 

Before Wujud — in alastu bi rabbikum, which occurred with Jud — the people of Allah were gifted insight about these maratib, such that when Wujud occurred, which is the Salah (tajali), He was not denied. 
---
The vision of the knower vs the veiled::
The vision of the knower vs the veiled:

“The result of what has been said is what we said originally and that is that all creation are levels (marātib) of the Truth. One must submit to His decision and what He establishes in His creation. One cannot oppose anything in it. The legal ruling (ḥukm ash-sharʿi) is behind it. He operates in it outwardly and inwardly. This [understanding]  is only for one who knows the unity of existence. He witnesses the distinction (al-faṣl) and the connection (al-waṣl) in it. There are no parts made in it despite the plentitude of its various genera and species. Its unity does not remove it from the bifurcation of its individuals (ashkhāṣihā) in rulings and properties. The Knowers (al-ʿārifīn) remark on this saying: ‘Multiplicity is the essence of unity and unity is the essence of multiplicity.’ 

The gaze of whoever looks at the multiplicity of existence and the bifurcation of its parts is upon one essence in all its multiplicity. The gaze of whoever looks at its unifying essence is infinitely diversified. This gaze is only for the knower and for none of the people of the veil (aṣḥāb al-ḥijāb). This [vision] is for the one who sees the unity(dhawqan), not theoretically (rasman). 

This is beyond expression. (However) the meaning is that the distinction is the connection. Unity is the connection. Multiplicity is the distinction. ( al-Mishrī 2013, 246-247)
---
Al-Mishry documented Shaikh al-Tijānī’s having mentioned the following…:
Al-Mishry documented Shaikh al-Tijānī’s having mentioned the following verses attributed to some of the Seniors (al-akābir) and the Shaikh’s commentary on them:

“A Reality whose ability has manifested in the universe/existence (al-kawn).
	Thus, It manifested these beings (al-akwān) and veils.
The essences of the worlds disguised it just as it is
	Known by the hearts of the Erudite Knowers (al-ʿurrafa al-udabāʿ).
All creatures are the veils of Its appearance.
	Most of the affair (jumlat l’amr) became Its leaders (al-nuqabāʿ).
There is nothing wondrous hidden in existent things,
	Rather, their being Its essence [is wondrous] thus you have not seen anything amazing.”

Our master said (ra) regarding their meaning:

‘The ‘Reality’ here is Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) termed the Essence of Obliteration (ʿayn al-ṭams) and the Cloud (al-ʿamā). There is nothing relative to it, it is unimaginable nor intellected. It has no location, how, trace, or fantasy (wahm). All relationships with it have been annihilated. The ability that the Reality manifests is the first veil of Obliteration and the Cloud. The Attributes and Names are completely inconceivable there. It is primary in the treasured veil wherein He said: ‘I was an unknown hidden treasure, and I loved to be known.’ He meant that He loved to appear to other than Himself. ‘Thus, I created the creation and made Myself known to them, thus, they knew Me through Me.’ This ability is what He expanded in the existent things since He caused the existent things to appear through this ability. (pg.213)

‘[The essences of the world] disguised it,’ etc., The act of disguising here is to be veiled from the other, for in the essence of its existence, it is in the zenith of appearance and clarity because when it manifested ‘other’ and ‘otherness’ is obliterated. The one who sees It has no doubt nor delusion regarding It. It is in the epitome of manifestation in that [case]. It is then disguised by the appearance of existent entities (al-mawjūdāt). This is the meaning of ‘It was disguised’ after having been in the zenith of experiential knowledge, it was then obliterated in ‘other’ and ‘otherness.’ It was disguised by existence when the latter manifested. In other words, It was veiled by existence through the forms of existent things.

His words ‘the essences of the world’s entities disguised it’ here means that the ʿayn of something is its essence. It is called an ʿayn due to its specification from the Lordly Cloud (al-ʿamā al-rabbānī). They are called essences here and are the essences of existent entities.

His words:  ‘…just as it is Known by the hearts of the Erudite Knowers’ means: experiential knowers (al-ʿurrāf) is the plural of experential knower ʿ(ārif). The term here implies those experiential knowers who have become acquainted with the etiquettes of the Divine Presence (al-ḥadra al-ilāhiyya), and as a result, the Reality acquainted Itself with their hearts. The veil of the universe has been lifted from the hearts of the experiential knowers. Thus, they can designate the Holy Presence (al-ḥaḍra al-qudsiyya) directly, just as one drowned in the ocean does not require someone else to inform them about it.

His words: All creatures are the veils of Its appearance means they appropriate them. In other words, Absolute Existence through the forms of the existential events (al-akwān) and all of creation are the veils of Its appearance.

His words: ‘The bulk of the affair,’ etc., Linguistically, leaders means those who bear a responsibility. As the Prophet (s.a.w.s.) took the allegiance of the Helpers in Makkah and they pledged their allegiance to him to carry out all of his provisions with a condition that anyone who refused to do so would be in a state of dishonor and degradation, he was not convinced until he had taken some leaders. Leaders were responsible for making sure any tribe member who refused would be dishonored, incapable of rebelling or fighting and to assist his enemies against him. He appointed leaders amongst them due to this burden. They are those who bear the responsibility placed upon them in this issue. He said (s.w.t.) to the Children of Israil after having taken their oath from them: ‘and We delegated twelve leaders amongst them.’ (5:12)

His words: ‘The bulk of the affair,’ etc., here are all the forms of existent things. Each of them, one by one have become Its leaders. Their purpose is that they all bear the burden of the weight of their experiential knowledge. This is the heaviest of affairs. They bear the burden of their glorification, worship, and prostration to It, meaning the Absolute Essence. Each individual existent thing is a leader in this sense. All of them praise Him. Thus, the Truth is an Essence and a Level. The Essence is unseen and inconceivable. He has not manifested in His Existence but through a level. This level is Divinity (al-ulūhiyya). (pg.215) The meaning of the verses, then is that all of existence is focused on Him with submssive worship, abasement, experiential knowledge, glorification, and prostration. No atom is outside of this place.

His words: ‘There is nothing wondrous hidden in existent things’, etc, refers to it being nothing wondrous to be hidden in them. His words: ‘Rather, their being Its Essence, meaning the Essence of Absolute Existence. The meaning of ‘His being their Essence’ is that the universe has a mirror that they appear in only some people’s light is strong so they witness the mirror and the One manifesting in it. Whoever’s light is weak sees the One manifesting in the mirror but the Existence of the One who manifests veils them from the mirror. Thus, they don't see other than Him, meaning other than the Truth, may He be glorified. One in this state says: The entire universe is Allah (t.w.t.) there is nothing in it but Him due to the weakness of his light. The poet says:

So none remains but Allah, nothing other than Him
	There is no arrival nor one who arrives

The one whose light is strong witnesses the mirror and the One who manifests therein. He gives every level its right of reality (ḥaqiyya) and creation (khalqiyya). One does not veil him from the other.

As for His words ‘thus you have not seen anything amazing,’ the word mā here means  ‘that which’ (al-ladhī). When Ibn ʿArabī al-Ḥatimī met Aaron (a.s.s.) he said that he said to him, ‘O Prophet of Allah! Your words: ‘...so let not the enemies rejoice over me…’ (7:150) where are the enemies (pg.216)  that you indicate? Is there anything outside of Allah?’ or however it was that he said it. ‘We Knowers see that everything is Allah. How can one imagine there be enemies? Our master Aaron (a.s.s.) said: ‘All that you see is Him simultaneously.'  He said: ‘No.’ Aaron said to him: ‘To the extent that you do not know this experientially is the degree to which you have failed to witness of Him.’1 (Al Mishry N.d, Vo1.  213-217).

---
A Section on the Responses of Our Master, may God be pleased with…:
A Section on the Responses of Our Master, may God be pleased with him, Amen, regarding Some Ecstatic Utterances of the Saints, may God be pleased with them:

Among these, he was asked about the statement of Abū al-ʿAbbās al-Mursī, may God be pleased with him: "If the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) were veiled from me for even the blink of an eye, I would not consider myself among the Muslims." And about the statement of Abū Yazīd, may God be pleased with him: "We have plunged into a sea, while the prophets stood on its shore." He replied, may God be pleased with him: “As for verifying the statement of al-Mursī: ‘For forty years, I have not been veiled from God for even the blink of an eye, and if the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) were veiled from me for even the blink of an eye, I would not consider myself among the Muslims.' 

Know that this particular distinction is not unique to al-Mursī alone; it is for the Pole of Poles (quṭb al-aqṭāb) in every era. Since he has been seated on the throne of spiritual leadership (quṭbāniyya), there has never been any veil between him and the Messenger of God (peace be upon him). Wherever the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) moves—from the Divine Presence of the unseen or the Divine Presence of witness—the eye of the Pole of Poles is always able to gaze upon him, never veiled from him for even a moment.

As for the statement of Abū Yazīd, may God be pleased with him: "We have plunged into a sea, while the prophets stood on its shore," know that the fundamental principle from which one cannot deviate, and which every believer must uphold—whoever deviates from it has deviated from the foundation of faith—is that God, exalted and glorified, manifests Himself in His supreme majesty, grandeur, and holiness, encompassing all His high attributes and names in both their general and specific forms.

 Such a manifestation is not the same for everyone, nor is it governed by a single rule or uniform method. Rather, insights into it vary, and the secrets of creation regarding it differ greatly, both in abundance and scarcity. Thus, He manifests Himself to each person according to their capacity and according to the extent of what their spiritual essence can accommodate of the sacred beauty’s manifestation, which has no limit that can be grasped or end that can be comprehended.

And if you understand this, then know that what is in the rank of the Messenger (peace be upon him), of manifestations of attributes, names, and realities, cannot be attained by anyone, not even the greatest of the resolute messengers, let alone those who are below them among the messengers and prophets, peace be upon them. 

And what is in the rank of the resolute messengers cannot be attained by anyone from the generality of the messengers. And what is in the rank of prophethood cannot be attained by anyone from the generality of the poles, and what is in the rank of spiritual leadership (quṭbāniyya) cannot be attained by anyone from the generality of the truthful ones (ṣiddīqīn).

If this is the case, and you understand this distinction, then know that the ecstatic utterances (shaṭaḥāt) that have come from the greatest knowers—those that might give the impression or imply that they have a superiority or elevation over the ranks of the prophets and messengers, such as the statement of Abū Yazīd al-Bisṭāmī: 'We have plunged into a sea, while the prophets stood on its shore,' or the statement of Shaykh ʿAbd al-Qādir al-Jīlānī: 'O assembly of prophets, you were given the title, and we were given what you were not given,' and the statement of Ibn al-Fāriḍ, may God have mercy on him: 'There is before you a sea we have plunged into, while the foremost stood on its shore, preserving the sanctity of my station.'

And his statement also: ‘And even though I am in the image of Adam, I have a meaning from Him, a witness to prophethood.’


And also his statement:  

Live in the gathering of the Eternal, through which   
I found the old men of life to be children of my youth.  
And from the favor of what I left behind for my contemporaries to drink,   
And those who came before me, the virtues are my bounty."  

And his statement in the "Kāfiya":  

"Everyone in your sanctuary loves you, but   
I alone love all who are in your sanctuary."  

The response to these ecstatic utterances (shaṭaḥāt) is that there is a time when the knower (ʿārif) undergoes annihilation (fanāʾ) and immersion (istighrāq), until he exits the sphere of his senses and witnessing and transcends all his faculties and existence. 

This may sometimes be in the Essence of the Truth, glorified and exalted is He, where He manifests to him from His divine holiness some of His secrets, overflowing upon him, necessitating that he witnesses his own essence as identical with the Essence of the Truth due to his dissolution in it and his total absorption by it.

 In this state, he might declare, "Glory to me; there is no god but I alone!" and similar statements, like "Exalted is my greatness, and sanctified is my majesty." In such instances, he is excused because the rational faculty, which distinguishes signs and customs and grants the differentiation of ranks through knowledge of what each deserves of the attributes, is lost to him, vanishing and dissipating. When this rational faculty is lost and gone, and the holy secret overflows upon him, he speaks as he does.

The speech that occurs in such a state is created by the Truth within him as a representation on His behalf. Thus, he speaks with the tongue of the Truth, not his own tongue, and expresses the Essence of the Truth, not his own essence. An example of this is the statement of Abū Yazīd al-Bisṭāmī: "Glory to me, how great is my rank!" and the statement of al-Ḥallāj: "I am the Truth, and there is nothing in this cloak but God," and the statements of other great knowers, such as al-Tustarī:  

"Look, I am a wondrous thing to behold;   
I am the lover and the beloved; there is no second."

The sayings of Ibn al-Fāriḍ similar to these are many. This is what immersion in the Essence of the Truth bestows, and this cannot be understood by words and discourse but is comprehended by taste (dhawq) and the purity of spiritual states. No one knows its reality except those who have tasted it. Sometimes, the immersion for the knower and annihilation (fanāʾ) occurs in the Essence of the Prophet (peace be upon him), where he declares: "Glory to me; there is no god but I alone!"

When his essence is enveloped in that secret, he does not witness his own essence, but only the Essence of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And God Most High informs him of some of the great special qualities given to His Prophet (peace be upon him), qualities that elevate him above all ranks of the prophets and messengers. Thus, he speaks of what God has granted His Prophet (peace be upon him), not about himself. Whoever hears him may think he attributes this to himself, but he actually attributes it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) due to his state of annihilation in his essence.

When he separates from this annihilation and immersion and returns to his senses and witnessing, he disavows such statements due to his knowledge of his rank. Apply this understanding to everything you hear from the masters, which might suggest they have superiority over the ranks of the prophets and messengers.  

Like the statement of al-Dusūqī, may God be pleased with him:  

"I was with Noah when the world witnessed   
The seas and the flood, under my hand of power.  

I was in the vision of the sacrifice of the one who was ransomed   
And the ram was sent down only due to my chivalry.  

I was with Job in the time of tribulation,   
And his trial was not cured except by my supplication."

There are many more statements like this, may God have mercy on him and be pleased with him. All of this is due to his annihilation in the Essence of the Prophet (peace be upon him), translating about his rank (peace be upon him), and this suffices as a response.

Beyond this is what the intellect cannot grasp, what words cannot express, and what cannot be mentioned due to its remoteness from understanding. This annihilation of the knower in the Essence of God Most High and in the Essence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is not for all knowers, nor at all times for those who have experienced it; rather, it is specific to certain times for some knowers only. And peace.

Addendum: The sea into which the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) plunged, while the prophets stood at its shore, is the sea of realities that God revealed to him, to the exclusion of the greatest messengers and prophets. Had even a little of this been revealed to them, they would have become pure non-existence quicker than the blink of an eye. They only stood on the shore of these manifestations, which are the manifestations that are specific to them. God revealed them from the effulgences of majesty, beauty, grandeur, and supremacy. Those realities are, for them, in relation to his rank (peace be upon him), like the shore is to the sea. They spoke with his tongue (peace be upon him) due to their state of absence and annihilation in him. Peace.



Among the questions posed to our Master, may God be pleased with him, was about the words of the Greatest Shaykh (Ibn al-ʿArabī), who stated that if God takes a saint (walī) and chooses him through His love, He may grant him knowledge that has not been disclosed to the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them. He also said, reflecting upon himself: "God has disclosed to me knowledge that has not been revealed to Adam and those who came after him." This is the verbatim statement.

The response, and God grants success in achieving what is correct, is that Ibn al-ʿArabī al-Ḥātimī, may God be pleased with him, said something to this effect: The ranks of those close to God are divided into the Truthful (al-Ṣiddīqīya), the Absolute Prophethood (Nubuwwa Muṭlaqa), and the Legislating Prophethood (Nubuwwa Tashrīʿiyya). He, may God have mercy on him, said: "Each of these three groups has exclusive knowledge that the other two groups do not possess." He also mentioned that he read to a group of prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, and listed their names, the science of letters. He said: "And I recited it to ʿAlī, may God honor his face, and I did not find among them anyone more knowledgeable than him in the science of letters." 

Among these events is the incident involving Khidr with our Master Mūsā, peace be upon him and upon our Prophet. Khidr said to him when they were about to part: "Had you been patient, you would have seen a thousand marvels that your apparent law would reject." After this, he said to him: "I am upon a knowledge from God's knowledge which you do not know, and you are upon a knowledge from God's knowledge which I do not know."

All of this is concerning others than the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him. As for him, peace and blessings be upon him, he is the encompassing one, gathering everything, as he said, "I am only a distributor, and God is the Giver." This is witnessed by the saying of Abū ʿAbdullāh Sayyidī Muḥammad al-Bakrī, may God have mercy on him, in his poem:

"[O God] What the Most Merciful sent or will send  
Of mercy ascending or descending  
In God's dominion or kingdom  
Of everything specific or comprehensive,  
Except that the Prophet, His servant, His chosen Prophet and Messenger,  
Is an intermediary in it and its foundation,  
This is known to every person of reason."

A question arises for us: If we say that Khidr is a saint and not a prophet, how is it permissible for him to kill the boy, given that all the laws of the messengers prohibit the killing of children? Even if they had committed something that warranted death, killing them would be corruption on earth. Killing a person is only permissible if they committed an act warranting death after reaching maturity and accountability; before this, it is not permissible to kill a child under any circumstance, unless the killer is a prophet, for prophets are protected from error and mistake. If we assume a prophet killed a child, no objection would be raised against him, for such an act would stem from divine command.

If we say that the laws of the messengers all agree on the prohibition of killing children, how could it be permissible for this prophet to allow what the laws agree on prohibiting? The answer to this is that God Almighty, through prophethood, can forbid whatever He wills and permit whatever He wills, whether the ruling from Him, glorified and exalted be He, is always continuous and never ceases or whether it is a specific ruling from Him in one or two cases, then He lifts the ruling.

This is not denied concerning the rights of the Creator, glorified and exalted be He, for the Prophet, peace be upon him, said about his fighting in Mecca: "It was only made lawful for me for an hour of the day, then it reverted to being prohibited." He meant the prohibition of allowing fighting therein, and that it was forbidden before and after him, peace be upon him. So, the Prophet, peace be upon him, knew that those who transgress in fighting within it would say, "He fought therein, peace be upon him, so we have a precedent." When he realized this, peace be upon him, he countered their argument by saying: "It was only made lawful for me for an hour of the day, then it reverted to being prohibited." This is a specific ruling from God, fulfilled and not extended to all times.

Similarly, the case with our Master Mūsā, peace be upon him, and the Samiri who openly disbelieved in God. In his law, whoever openly disbelieves in God must be killed, and there is no way to leave him. So, when he intended to kill the Samiri, God, glorified and exalted, forbade him from killing him and commanded him to let him be due to his abundance of generosity and kindness to creation.

This command from God, glorified and exalted, to Mūsā is a specific command for a particular time and a particular person, not to be generalized to every disbeliever in God. This is used as proof because this is a specific ruling for a specific time on a particular individual. Then God, glorified and exalted, lifted this ruling and returned the law to its original state, requiring the killing of anyone who openly disbelieves in God. From this, it becomes clear to you the perfection of knowledge about God Almighty, that He decrees whatever He wills and lifts whatever He wills.

If a consistent ruling from God is issued in a law concerning a prophet, and then it is lifted in one or two specific cases, it is accepted as His ruling, and no objection is raised against Him, saying, "How did He rule with something and then rule with its opposite?" There is no objection against Him in anything because of His complete knowledge and exalted rank, glorified and exalted be He.

Moreover, the knowledge of legal rulings is exclusive to prophethood, and it is not within the capacity of the Truthful (al-Ṣiddīqīya) to comprehend knowledge of legal rulings without transmission from another, unlike prophethood, for knowledge of legal rulings is an inherent quality of it, meaning within prophethood. This is not the case with the Truthful; the Truthful do not have knowledge of legal rulings except through reception via prophethood.

A warning for those who claim to have reached and understood the realities: Among the sayings of our Master, may God be pleased with him: There is a consensus that the ruling established by prophethood cannot be lifted or altered except by prophethood. As for sainthood, it has no access to this matter because God Most High conveys knowledge to the saints as He conveys it to the prophets equally. However, what He conveys to the saints does not dissolve the binding covenants of prophethood. This is inconceivable and unimaginable.

From this perspective, Shaykh ʿAbd al-Qādir, may God be pleased with him, became aware of the words of the accursed: "I am your Lord; I have permitted for you the forbidden." He replied: "Get away, you accursed!" Then the demon fell, disfigured, and the cloud turned dark. The devil said: "O ʿAbd al-Qādir, you have escaped from me by your knowledge of your Lord's judgement and your understanding of the rules of your station.  With such an incident, I led seventy men of the Way astray. It was asked of the Shaykh: "How did you know it was the devil?" He replied: "By his statement to me, 'I have permitted for you the forbidden,' because what has been forbidden by his law, peace be upon him, cannot be lifted except by prophethood, and prophethood has been sealed and concluded.This is his verbatim statement.

I said: It is understood from his words here, may God be pleased with him, that declaring something permissible for oneself or others, which the law has forbidden, from someone who claims to follow the path, should not be heeded, for such a person is deluded and wandering in the valleys of error. 

In another phrase of his, he said, may God be pleased with him: A principle: Know that all the messengers expressed themselves with truthful statements that no falsehood approaches, neither from before nor from behind. Whoever claims that it is permissible to deviate from them or believes that such is permitted for him by God Most High has indeed disbelieved in God.

The evidence of this is His saying, where He mentioned the prophets, peace be upon them, in Surat al-Anʿām: "Those are the ones whom God has guided, so follow their guidance." And peace; this is his verbatim statement. Among his sayings, may God be pleased with him, is: God Almighty will say to His servants on the Day of Resurrection: "How long I listened to you, so listen to Me. Indeed, I have made a lineage for Myself and made a lineage for you. My lineage is piety: 'Indeed, the most honored of you in the sight of God is the most righteous of you.' As for your lineage, I have made you into peoples and tribes that you may know one another."

As for the prophet, knowledge of legal rulings is an inherent attribute within him. Suppose we assume two prophets, for example, in the same time period but in two distant lands, and one prophet sees the other ruling contrary to what he knows as law in his own law. In that case, he would not think ill of him nor disbelieve him. If you understand this and say that Khidr's status is that of sainthood (wilāya) and not prophethood (nubuwwa), then what justifies his permission to kill the boy while all divine laws prohibit killing him? He is not among the prophets for us to say that God permitted him to kill the boy in a specific instance. However, the answer lies in examining his statement: "I did not do it of my own accord."

We said that Khidr does not have access to the ruling directly from God Almighty as a prophet does, and he said, "I did not do it of my own accord." The answer is that he received this from another prophet, not Mūsā, peace be upon him, either at that moment or at a previous time. This prophet informed him of God’s command regarding the killing of the boy and clarified the reason for it, telling him that God commands him to kill him to make clear the matter in his statement, "I did not do it of my own accord."

Al-Shāmī, may God have mercy on him, said: I and a group of the Truthful (Ṣiddīqīn) who had knowledge of outward (exoteric) science met with him, and he had no apparent knowledge. He said: They delved into the meaning and interpretations of this hadith, which is his saying, peace be upon him, "The righteous vision of a righteous man is a part of forty-six parts of prophethood." Al-Shāmī, may God have mercy on him, said: I told them what appeared to me was contrary to what you are saying. They asked, "How so?" He replied:

"I see in every waking person the image of the spirit like a rising sun, whether that person is a believer or a disbeliever, as long as they are awake. When people sleep, I see every essence from which the sun has departed during sleep, leaving the essenc3 without anything. Then I see in each essence, when the spirit departs from it, forty-six jewels. In the selves of the disbelievers, I see them as black nigella seeds, all of them. As for those in the selves of sinful believers, I see them as yellow grains like the sun at dusk. As for those in the selves of the righteous, I see them brighter than that. I see a jewel or grain of them rising from the essence of the righteous until it reaches just below the sky, remaining there for as long as it takes to recite Sūrat al-Fātiḥa, then it returns to its body. 

I see in the selves of righteous saints three grains or jewels that ascend from their essence after sleep to above the first heaven, where they remain for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then they return to their essence. I see in the selves of the saints known as martyrs five grains or jewels that ascend to above the second heaven, remaining for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then they return to their body. 

In the essence of every knower (ʿārif) among the general knowers, I see seven grains or jewels rising from each essence, reaching above the third heaven, remaining for as long as it takes to recite Sūrat al-Fātiḥa, then returning to their essence. I see in the essence of each man of authority (ahl al-taṣrīf) nine jewels or grains ascending from his essence to above the fourth heaven, remaining for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then returning to their essence. 

In the essence of the encompassing help (ghawth al-jāmiʿ), I see eleven grains or jewels rising above the sixth heaven, remaining for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then returning to their essence. I see in the essence of each of the four individuals (afrād al-arbaʿa) thirteen grains or jewels ascending above the seventh heaven, remaining for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then returning to their essence. 

I see in the essence of each of the treasures' keys (mafātiḥ al-kunūz) fifteen grains or jewels, seven or eight of them going to the paradise where their station is, and the others going to the world of command, remaining for as long as it takes to recite al-Fātiḥa, then returning to their bodies."

When I informed them of this, they denied it and did not believe me, so we went, disputing, to Khidr, peace be upon him. He responded to us by saying: "All revelation is divided into forty-six parts." Khidr, peace be upon him, said: "One part of it is for the righteous, three parts for the Truthful Saints (awliyāʾ al-ṣiddīqīn), five for the Martyr Saints (awliyāʾ al-shuhadāʾ), seven for each of the general knowers (ʿārifīn), nine for each of the general authorities (ahl al-taṣrīf), eleven for the encompassing help (ghawth al-jāmiʿ), thirteen for each of the four individuals (afrād al-arbaʿa), fifteen for each of the treasures' keys (mafātiḥ al-kunūz), eighteen for each of the general prophets, and twenty-one for each of the general messengers, excluding Adam, Idrīs, Mūsā, ʿĪsā, Ilyās, and another man, meaning himself. For these six, there are twenty-three portions, half of what the Prophet, peace be upon him, has. And for our Prophet, peace be upon him, there are forty-six parts."

From this, it is established for us that Khidr was given from the division of revelation what was given to the greatest of the messengers, peace be upon them. It becomes clear to us that the people of outward knowledge cannot claim that a non-prophet can be more knowledgeable than a prophet. They should instead say, "This is a matter we do not know; God decides in it as He wills, so we do not pass judgment on it." Moreover, with all this, if Khidr were to enter the presence of the messengers, he would burn as a hair burns in fire. This is because our Master Mūsā, peace be upon him, has with God a thousand councils, and every council has overflowing knowledge from God without end, of which Khidr has no knowledge. However, when he was asked, "Is there on the face of the earth anyone more knowledgeable than you?" he said, "No." Then the Truth, exalted be He, reproached him and said, "Rather, I have a servant on earth who is more knowledgeable than you." From this, it is learned that God grants what He wills to whom He wills, so do not pass judgment on Him regarding anything, and peace be upon you.

He, may God be pleased with him, also answered this question with another expression, stating: "Know that Khidr is only a saint (walī) and not a prophet according to the majority. Shaykh al-Akbar (Ibn al-ʿArabī), may God be pleased with him, said: 'The difference in this matter is concerning his prophethood according to the people of outward knowledge, not according to us, for we are certain that he is among the saints and not the prophets.' And likewise, others among the notables hold this view, even though some outside the majority believe in his prophethood."

Shaykh Zarrūq, may God be pleased with him, said: "Some scholars have narrated that Khidr, peace be upon him, was a messenger sent to a group in the sea, and whoever does not acknowledge his prophethood has disbelieved." Shaykh Zarrūq responded to this statement: "We accept the validity of what he claims but do not accept the statement that whoever does not believe in his prophethood is a disbeliever because that is an addition to faith and a compulsion for it, and the community has not agreed upon it."

The evidence against his prophethood is the statement of our Master Mūsā, peace be upon him, to him during the incident of the ship: "You have indeed done a grave thing" (Qur'an 18:71), and regarding the killing of the boy: "You have done a deplorable thing" (Qur'an 18:74). Had he been a prophet, Mūsā, peace be upon him, would not have been ignorant of it because he was a complete knower. How could he be unaware of the status of a prophet present with him, thinking him not to be a prophet? This is inconceivable for the prophets, peace be upon them. 

It is also mentioned that Ibrāhīm al-Taymī, may God be pleased with him, one of the Abdāl (substitutes), in his narration of receiving the ten septuples from Khidr, said: "I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, and I asked him about Khidr, peace be upon him. He said to me, 'Khidr has spoken the truth.' Until he said to him at the end of the hadith: 'He is the master of the saints.' This is the strongest evidence against his prophethood."

205

 Regarding the Second Question: Can Non-Prophets Surpass Prophets in Knowledge?

The answer, and God knows best, is that it is possible for non-prophets to surpass prophets in knowledge in certain respects; there is no inherent impossibility in this. However, this does not diminish the rank of a prophet. There is a distinction here: when it comes to knowledge of God, His attributes, names, manifestations, and what these encompass in terms of gifts, talents, and divine outpourings, it is impossible for a non-prophet to surpass a prophet. This is because prophethood possesses a greater degree of knowledge, a wider scope, and a more profound perception in these matters. If a non-prophet were to reach or exceed a prophet in these aspects, they would either be equal in virtue or superior to him, which is not possible.

However, in terms of knowledge of the various levels of the universe, what occurs therein in both general and detailed terms, the vicissitudes of its changes, and the unveiling of what is yet to come in the future, which is the unveiling of cosmic mysteries, a non-prophet might surpass a prophet in this domain. This is precisely the case with the example of Khidr. The reality is that the insight of prophets and messengers is always directed towards the Divine Presence, intensely focused and dedicated to it. Their hearts are forever turned to God, without any diversion towards created beings. Because of the intensity of their focus on God, they are constantly engaged with His manifestations and do not turn their gaze to anything else. Each one of them has no concern or care except for what emerges from the Divine Presence at every moment in terms of manifestations, gifts, talents, and inspirations to give everything its due from the etiquettes and responsibilities of service, without ever being distracted from it, even for a single moment.

Due to this deep absorption, they do not pay attention to the created beings, nor do they know what occurs within them. Moreover, their engagement in conversing with the Divine in His sacred presence prevents them from diverting their focus. Without a doubt, anyone who tastes this cannot turn to anything other than God, even for a single moment. Therefore, they are unaware of what transpires in the cosmos or its fluctuations because they are occupied with God, the Exalted. Non-prophets, however, do not have the capacity to maintain this state perpetually; they experience it at times and not at others. Hence, they have more frequent unveilings regarding the cosmos and its affairs because they lack the ability to be in constant absorption as the prophets are.

If you understand this, you will understand why Khidr was specifically granted the knowledge of hidden things, unlike Mūsā, peace be upon him, because these are cosmic mysteries. Therefore, Khidr's superiority in this regard over Mūsā is not negated, as Mūsā was preoccupied with what we mentioned, and Khidr could not attain the absorption of Mūsā in the Divine Presence. Despite this, there is no restriction on God in His dominion or in His decree that a non-prophet might surpass a prophet in knowledge, as there are no limitations imposed upon Him. He grants what He wills to whom He wills, and He possesses absolute choice and effective will. His knowledge is not bound by constraints or governed by laws, and no one can encompass His knowledge. He, the Exalted, said: "And He creates that which you do not know" (Quran 16:8). This is one of His manifestations.

Therefore, what scholars have settled in their hearts as being impossible — that a non-prophet could surpass a prophet in knowledge — should not lead to judgments against God, the Exalted. This would be akin to imposing restrictions upon Him and encompassing His knowledge, which is beyond the scholars' grasp. It is merely a firmly established principle in their hearts that is not supported by evidence, neither from the Book (Quran) nor from the Sunnah concerning God, the Exalted.

Shaykh al-Akbar (Ibn al-ʿArabī), may God be pleased with him, said: "God gave me knowledge that neither Adam nor anyone else possessed," as has been mentioned earlier, referring to the prophets and messengers. And as for His, blessed and exalted be He, saying about Khidr: "And I did not do it of my own accord" (Quran 18:82), the answer is that God, blessed and exalted be He, commanded him in his secret with definitive knowledge that he knows is from God, the Exalted, without any intermediary between him and God. Just as He said, "We gave him a mercy from Us and taught him from Us a knowledge" (Quran 18:65). This is the state of the great Truthful ones (al-Ṣiddīqīn), and it does not contradict the fact that a prophet informed him about the matter as previously mentioned.

This is the strongest evidence that he (Khidr) is not a prophet, for if he were, he would not have been described in this manner. It would have sufficed to say that "they found one of Our prophets" instead of saying, "they found one of Our servants." This is because the rank of prophethood itself is sufficient to imply knowledge from God without an intermediary. Since he was not a prophet, it was said about him, "We taught him from Us a knowledge" (Quran 18:65). That is why he said, "I did not do it of my own accord" (Quran 18:82), indicating that God, the Exalted, commanded him inwardly and definitively, and he was certain that it was from the Truth, exalted be He. Just as He said regarding the bees, which are dumb and appear as though they do not reason: "And your Lord inspired to the bee, 'Take for yourself among the mountains, houses'" (Quran 16:68). The Exalted informed that He gave the bees knowledge from Himself, and they did not doubt that what they did was by His command. Likewise is the case with Khidr, peace be upon him. This is the end of his words.

And from the meaning of what has been mentioned earlier, one of the great scholars said:

“I concealed myself from my time by the shadow of His majesty,  
So I came to see my time while it could not see me.  
If you asked the days my name, they would not know,  
And if you asked my place, they would not know my location.”

He responded, may God be pleased with him, : The rank being referred to here is that of the Supreme Caliph (al-khalīfat al-ʿuṭmā), a spiritual rank or station that does not have a specific name attributed to it. All the names of existence are his names due to his realization of their respective levels, and because he is the spirit present within all beings.

In this metaphysical framework, the Supreme Caliph is considered the spirit that governs, animates, and sustains all existence. There is not a single entity within the cosmos except that he (the Supreme Caliph) is the regulating and moving force within it, the one that establishes its reality. Similarly, there is not a place within the sphere of the world except that he is present there, maintaining and holding it.

Due to this perspective, he (the Supreme Caliph) does not distinguish himself with any particular existence, nor does he have a specific location that sets him apart from others. For this reason, it was said in the poetic lines:

"If you were to ask the days..." (iimplying a state of omnipresence that transcends particularization).

207


Shaykh al-Mursī said: “If the reality of the walī (saint) were unveiled, he would be worshipped instead of God because his attributes are from God’s attributes and his qualities are from God’s qualities.” Here, the term walī refers to the "Perfect Man," who is the greatest deputy (khalīfa al-aʿẓam). This is the meaning of His saying, exalted be He: “Or is one who was dead, and We gave him life” (Quran 6:122).

Muhayyi al-Dīn said: “The human who is veiled is not truly human; he is merely like a human, like a dead body that has no spirit in it. It is the form of a human, but there is no spirit within it.” Wherever it is heard in the speech of the Sufis that the spirit is uncreated but rather ancient and eternal, they are referring to this spirit, which is the purity of gnosis after the spiritual opening. Its possessor does whatever he wills in whatever he intends. He brings the dead back to life if he wishes and calls out to them, and they respond quickly, even if they are in decay. He makes the dry trees flourish instantly if he wishes, and other such wonders. Nothing is difficult for him in terms of breaking the natural order, except that he is bound by the utmost etiquette with the Divine Presence. This is what prevents him from displaying such miracles.

If he displays any wonders that the moment does not permit, he is punished immediately, or he is expelled, or his spiritual station is stripped away. This is because he is absorbed in the Divine Presence, dead to all his own desires; his existence is sustained only by the sustenance of the Truth. If he were asked, “What do you want?” he would reply, “I only want what the Truth, exalted be He, wills.” He is thus annihilated in his desires, standing by the will of the Truth in all his movements, stillness, fluctuations, and desires.

This is the end of what he, may God be pleased with him, dictated to us.

And peace be upon you.

**Translation of the Verses:**

"And I have not sat with a group to whom I spoke  
Except that You were my conversation among those sitting.  
And I have not taken a drink of water from thirst  
Except that I saw an image of You in the glass."

**Main Text:**

"This is what is referred to by total immersion in God the Exalted (al-istighrāq fī Allāh taʿālā), which is the meaning of his statement 'Ayā sirrī yā jahrī wa baʿḍī wa jumlatī,' meaning: there is nothing apart from You; You are my part and my whole, and O all of my parts. Thus, I am not other than You, nor are You other than me. And his statement, 'wa maknūn khufiyyī,' means: what I conceal and hide of all hidden things, You are that. This refers to God’s seizing of the servant (muʾākhadhat Allāh taʿālā lil-ʿabd). They express this seizing with their saying: It is God's snatching of the servant from the valley of separation (wādī al-tafriqah) and casting him into the ocean of divine unity (baḥr al-jamʿ), in such a way that he no longer distinguishes in any way, shape, quantity, quality, image, thought, perception, imagination, sensation, otherness, or separateness. Thus, there is nothing but the Real (al-ḥaqq) with the Real, in the Real, for the Real, from the Real. This seizing is termed 'the annihilation of annihilation' (fanāʾ al-fanāʾ). And from here, the servant's life comes with his immersion in this ocean, emerging to distinguish the attributes, names, affairs, and considerations, by giving each rightful person his due."
