**Main Text:**

"Therefore, there is no paradise nor anything other than it. For the one who is immersed (fī Allāh), when he is cast into the sea of unity and distinguishes the ranks, his delight is in the existence of the Truth. If all the bliss of paradise were gathered together and compared to this delight, it would be like a drop in a sea.

It was said to (Prophet) Mūsā, peace be upon him, 'In what state were you when the discourse took place?' He said, 'As for the awe, imagine lightning bolts striking around you continuously; there is no description of the fear of someone in this situation. And as for the pleasure, it is indescribable. 

It has been said that the pleasure of intimacy in It has been said that the pleasure of intimacy (ladhdhatu al-jimāʿ) in that state is nothing compared to that matter, for pleasure has its ultimate limit and awe has its ultimate limit.


And his saying, 'And the light of my essence (anwār muhjatī)' — muhjah here is the soul (al-rūḥ) and the vision of the eye, and its light by which one sees is You. As for the eye, it is the soul (al-rūḥ), and his saying, 'and the coolness of my heart (bard fu’ādī)' — the coolness here refers to the cold sweet water which quenches the burning thirst; there is no pleasure for its taste. This is understood to mean that the heart burned with longing, and there is no coolness that can extinguish that burning except the vision.

Ibn al-Fāriḍ, may Allāh be pleased with him, says:

'I desire, even if the span of time is prolonged, a glance from you;  
And how much blood, besides mine, has been shed to reach my goal!'

And it has been narrated about him that when he was in the throes of death and some saints were present with him, the veil was lifted for him from paradise. And it was said to him: 'This is your station,' so he cried and said:

211

'If my rank in love is what I have seen, then I have wasted my days;  
It is a wish my soul has attained for a while, but today I count it as nothing but a dream.'"


The narrator said that it was said to him from the Divine Presence: "What do you wish for, O ʿUmar?" He recited: "I desire, even if the duration is prolonged, a glance from you. And how much blood has been spilled in pursuit of my aim!" The narrator said: "I looked at him for a while and saw him smiling, then his soul departed. I knew that he was given his desire."

His saying: "Bestow upon me the vision of You," is what was narrated about Ibn al-Fāriḍ, may Allah be pleased with him, in the verse that ended.

Our master, may Allah be pleased with him, answered concerning the meaning of Shaykh al-Akbar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he said:

"The Lord is the Lord and the servant is a servant. Oh, how I wish I knew who is responsible!  
If you say, 'a servant,' then the servant is dead, or if you say, 'the Lord,' how could He be responsible?"

The knower of Allah, Sayyidi ʿAbd al-Raḥmān al-Fāsī, may Allah be pleased with him, replied:

"Yes, by the truth of affirming a servant with the rule of separation, he is responsible."

Our master, may Allah be pleased with him, said about its meaning that the truth, exalted is He, created the servant and bestowed upon him the outpouring of existence, and provided him with the secrets of His seven self-attributes, which are: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, and speech. With these, his life, the continuity of his existence, his movements, 
 212

and made him responsible amidst these attributes.Thus, the Real (al-Ḥaqq) manifested within him through His own attributes of essence, so that the servant, by means of those attributes, became as if he were the very essence of the Real, capable of many things, willing, and managing many matters. When He manifested in him through these seven attributes, He charged him with responsibilities.And these seven attributes emerge from being merely essential, and this is the distinction he mentioned, by which He charged him. These are the end of his words.

And truly, it appeared in the universe through its essence, * revealing these worlds and veils. 

It became veiled from the eyes of the worlds as * it became known to the hearts of the knowledgeable, the courteous.

 All of creation are veils for its emergence, and the entirety of the matter has become its deputies (nuqabā).

There is nothing astonishing in the concealment within the cosmos; rather, its existence is its very essence, so what you see is not surprising.



Our master, may Allah be pleased with him, said regarding its meaning: "The Reality here is the absolute existence which is called the essence of erasure and blindness; within it, there is no attribution, no delusion, no rational comprehension, no 'where,' no 'how,' no form, and no imagination. All relations are negated within it. The power that the Reality manifested was initially within the veil of erasure and blindness; there is no rational comprehension of the attributes and names there in terms of appearance, not in terms of existence. It manifested its power through what it revealed of the cosmos. For, at first, it was within the veil of the hidden treasure where it said: 'I was a hidden treasure and I loved to be known,' meaning that it loved manifestation for others, so it created creation, and through them, I became known. And this power is what it has spread within the cosmos, where it manifested the cosmos through this power.”

### Translation with Key Terms Transliterated

**His saying: "Tanakkarat..."** 

"Tanakkarat" (تَنَكَّرَتْ) here means "to be veiled" (al-iḥtijāb) from anything other (al-ghayr). For in its very essence (māhiyyat wujūdihā), it is in the utmost state of manifestation (ẓuhūr) and clarity (wuḍūḥ). For whenever it appears, otherness (al-ghayr) and separateness (al-ghayriyyah) are obliterated. There is no doubt (shakk) or illusion (wahm) in the realm of the one who beholds it. It is, in this manifestation (tajallī), in the utmost state of appearance. Then, it veiled itself (iḥtijab) through the appearance of existing things (ẓuhūr al-mawjūdāt).

This is the meaning of his saying "Tanakkarat," after it was in the utmost state of knowledge (ma‘rifah) at the time of its manifestation (tajallī), otherness (al-ghayr) and separateness (al-ghayriyyah) were obliterated. And when existence (al-wujūd) appeared, it veiled itself (iḥtijab) by it, meaning it veiled itself by the forms of existents (ṣuwar al-mawjūdāt). And what is veiled here is the Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) by the forms of existents.

**His saying: "bi-‘uyūn al-‘ālamīn..."** 

The "eye" (‘ayn) of a thing here is its essence (dhāt). It is named an eye (‘ayn) to distinguish it from blindness (al-‘amā) and ignorance (jahl). For in the eternal knowledge (‘ilm al-azalī), they were fixed essences (a‘yān thābitah), thus here they are called "eyes" (‘uyūn), the essences (dhawāt) of the existents (al-mawjūdāt).

**His saying: "kamā ta‘arrafa bi-qulūb al-‘urraf al-adabā..."** 

Meaning: The term "al-‘urafā" (العُرَافُ) is the plural of "‘ārif" (عَارِف), and what is meant by them here are those who are knowledgeable (‘ārifūn) of the etiquettes (ādāb) of the Divine Presence (al-ḥaḍrah al-ilāhiyyah). It has made itself known (ta‘arrafa) to their hearts (qulūb), for the veils of the cosmos (ḥijāb al-kawn) have been lifted from their hearts. They have directly witnessed (mu‘āyanah) the Holy Presence (al-ḥaḍrah al-qudsiyyah), not by report (khabar), like a person drowning in the sea does not need anyone to inform him about it.

**His saying: "al-khalq kulluhum astār ṭal‘atihā..."** 

Meaning: "They are veils (astār) of its emergence." Meaning the Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) has made itself manifest through the forms of the worlds (ṣuwar al-akwān). All of creation (al-khalq) is veils of its emergence.

**His saying: "wa-jumlat al-amr ilā kh..."** 

The meaning of "al-naqīb" (النَّقِيب) in language is the one who bears the burden of something. For when the Ansār (helpers) pledged allegiance (bāya‘at) to the Prophet, peace be upon him, at Mecca, they pledged to uphold all of his decrees (matūnati).




" that whoever refused among their people would remain in humiliation (dhull) and disgrace (hawān). So when they pledged allegiance (bāya‘ūhu) to him on this, he was not satisfied with just that until he appointed from among them chiefs (nuqabā’), each chief (naqīb) carrying the responsibility over his tribe, [stipulating] that whoever refused among them would remain in humiliation and could neither openly oppose him nor engage in battle against him, nor could they assist his enemies against him. For this burden, he took chiefs from them, and they were those who bore the responsibilities assigned to them concerning the matter (al-amr). This is the meaning of the naqīb (chief). Allah, the Exalted, said to the Children of Israel after mentioning their taking of covenants (mithāqātihim): 'And We raised among them twelve chiefs' (Qur'an 5:12).""His saying: 'The entirety of the matter...' The entirety of the matter (jumlat al-amr) here refers to the forms of all existing things (ṣuwar al-mawjūdāt bi-asrihā). They have all become chiefs for it, each one individually (fardan fardan). And what is meant by them is that they all have taken upon themselves the weight of knowing it (ma‘rifatihā), for it is the most challenging of matters. They have also borne the burden of glorifying it (tasbīḥihā), worshipping it (‘ibādatihā), and prostrating to it (sujūdihā), meaning to the Absolute Essence (al-dhāt al-muṭlaqa). In this field, the entire universe (al-akwān) is made up of chiefs, each one individually, all glorifying Him. The Truth (al-ḥaqq) is an essence (dhāt) and a rank (martabah); the Essence is unseen (ghayb), not rationally understood (lā tu‘qalu) nor comprehended (lā tudraku), and nothing appeared in existence except by the rank (martabah), which is Divinity (al-ulūhiyyah)."


"And the direction of the entire existence (tawajuh al-wujūd kullihi) towards Him is with worship (‘ibādah), submission (khudū‘), humility (tadhallul), knowledge (ma‘rifah), glorification (tasbīḥ), and prostration (sujūd). There is not a single atom within it that is outside this domain. His saying: 'There is no wonder in what is hidden.' The meaning of the verse is that there is no wonder in its concealment within the universes. His saying: 'Rather, its existence is its very essence,' meaning that the entire universe is its very essence, which is the absolute existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq). The meaning of 'its existence being its very essence' is that the universe has become a mirror in which it [the Divine] reflects.""This assertion is true, except that among people, some have a strong light (nūr), so they witness the mirror and witness the manifestation (al-mutajalli) within it. And whoever's light is weak sees only the manifestation within the mirror, and the presence of the manifestation covers the mirror, so they see nothing else but the True (ḥaqq), may He be exalted. Such a person says: 'The entire universe is Allah (al-kawn kulluhu huwa Allāh), and there is nothing within it but Him,' due to the weakness of their light. The poet says:'So nothing remains except Allah; there is nothing other than Him, There is no connection nor anything connected.'""But whoever's light is strong witnesses both the mirror and the manifestation within it, giving each rank its due of reality (ḥaqīqiyyah) and creation (khalqiyyah), so nothing veils one from the other. His saying: 'You see no wonder': 'what' here is a relative pronoun meaning 'that which.'

Ibn al-‘Arabī al-Ḥātimī said when he met our master Hārūn, peace be upon him, 'I said to him, “O Prophet of Allah (yā nabī Allāh): your saying ‘Do not make the enemies rejoice over me,’ where is the enemy you are referring to?'”….

Quotes Kitab al-Jami:
Quotes Kitab al-Jami 

The most approximate statement about the difference between absolute oneness of existence (al-aḥadiyya), relative oneness (al-waḥda), and monism (al-wāḥadiyya) is that the absolute oneness of existence is an ontological level (martaba) of the Truth’s nature (s.w.t.) (kunh al-ḥaqq) which is His manifestation through His Essence to HIs Essence through all of His Attributes (ṣifātih) and Names (asmāʿih) for all the commensurate requisites (al-lawzim) and necessities (al-muqtaḍiyāt) therein. None but He has access to it. Relative oneness is His manifestation to His Messenger (s.a.w.s.) through some of His Attributes and Names. Much of what occurs in the absolute oneness of existence is kept from him. Monism is His manifestation to all of the prophets, messengers, the righteous, and knowers through His Divine Attributes and Names (bi ṣifātih wa asmāʿih al-lahūtiyya). This [ontological level] is what the creation seeks [its needs from]. He hides much of what He reveals to His Messenger, our master Muḥammad (s.a.w.s.), regarding His Attributes and Names. 

The difference between these two levels is only understood experientially. Mere statements do not reveal anything about them. Instead, such statements are mere approximations for the sake of conceptual understanding. No one knows the meaning of these expressions but those who have experienced them. As for [the statement above regarding one who] wanted to drown in oceans of relative oneness, relative oneness is the previously mentioned manifestation to the Prophet (s.a.w.s.). The essence (al-ʿayn) of relative oneness is the Muhammadan Reality (al-ḥaqīqa al-muḥammadiyya). To be drowned in it is to view it without veils. This perspective is from amongst those undefined and limitless virtues, gifts, secrets, and wisdom. As for drowning in the essence of the ocean of relative oneness without veils-none but he (s.a.w.s.) can do so. (Al-Mishry n.d., 174)

Work Cited

Al-Mishry, Muḥammad. n.d. Al-jāmiʿli-durar al-quṭb al-maktūm. Rabāṭ: dar al-imān. 

The distinctions between essence and accidents is only mental but otherwise unreal:

It was said to Sayyidinā (i.e., Shaikh at-Tijānī), may God be pleased with him, 
‘Perception (idrāk) is one of the meanings. It is not an essence (jawhar) that can be decided upon.’ He said: ‘That [definition] is with regard to the limited intellect. As for its relationship to God, the realities (al-haqaaiq), their essences and accidents are all the same. This is as it has come in the tradition about the forms of actions in the grave and what is afterward regarding the states of the hereafter all of which cannot be denied. If this has been affirmed then there is no difference in the discourse of the realities regarding essence or accident. Kitab al jaam’i pg 251


Shaikh at Tijani on the Unknowability of the Essence of the Essence:

All those of experiential knowledge, may God be pleased with them, know, without exception know it (ie, the name ‘Allah’) is the essence of the level (ayn al martaba) not the essence of  the Essence (ayn al dhat) as the Truth’s level, glorified is He, is the Divnity. The Essence is in utter hiddenness. No one other than Him knows It, glorified is He. Nothing has appeared in existence but the level. The Essence is hidden. None can perceive it. It is in utter hiddenness. The level is the epitome of manifestation. Whatever you hear of the words of the experiential knowers, may God be pleased with them, [say] that He is the Manifest (ath thaahir) and that nothing has existence but He, they only intend the level in that [expression], not the manifestation of the Essence. 
(Kitaab al jaami 346)

Shaikh at Tijani on the relationships (an nisb):

“Know that the “unique presence” (hadrat al ahadiyya) is the first relationship emerging from the essence of the Essence (ayn adh dhat) because the Truth in the presence of Its Essence knows no relationship (nisba). The presence of the Naive Essence (adh dhat as saadhij) (348) is the ocean of blindness (bahr al a’maa), oblivion (at tams). No attribute, name, essence, trace, otherness, imagination, quantification, qualification, jurisdiction, or property can be thought of in It. When Its Essence emerges It is categorical to every consideration. Thus, no relationship can be intellected for It. The manifestations of relationships are located after departing from Essential naïveté. 
[Kitab al jami 347]


During an explanation on the nature of Divine Love Shaikh at Tijani mentioned:

Neither inclination nor infatuation occur in the His High Essence (dhātihī al ‘aliyya) as in the level of His Essence is in the epitome of Essential Loftiness, Essential Pride, Perfect Honor, and Majesty. Undescribed,  unqualified. All these Attributes as such in the Essence require that nothing be found alongside Him in existence for these Attributes necessitate jealousy toward the co-existent, glorified is He, much less that He should look at it with love or bend toward it with inclination due to the aforementioned Attributes. 473 

Shaikh at-Tijānī on the Oneness of Existence (waḥadat al-wujūd) includes its bifurcations (iftirāq):

“It is only the relationships of existence (nisb al-wujūd) that differ according to the manner in which the Will of the Truth has divided them within it between the honored and the inferior, elevated and suppressed, despised and (243) precious, the celebrated and the despicable, until the final relationship in it. The relationship’s separations do not remove them from its single essentiality. This is similar to the human essence. Its unity does not negate the different relationships of its parts and the particulars of each part in its properties. The hand’s properties are not like that of the foot. Their properties are not like that of the eye. All properties, limbs, and parts are like this. The exaltation of his face out of  the epitome of respect, and the lowliness of his position in the most severe form of loss and insult does not remove him from his essence’s unity despite all the differing properties. The same is said regarding the oneness of existence. Its unity does not remove it from its having various parts and specifics as we have said regarding the human’s essence. ( al-Mishrī 2013, 244) 

He used ink to exemplify his intentions stating:

“....The various letters are contained in the ink and the miscellaneous words, the various meanings the ink’s forms indicate do not remove it from the unity of its inkness.

There is nothing there but ink formed in their shapes indicating variant meanings, individual letters, miscellaneous non-harmonious nor similar properties. Were you to look at the essence of these forms whose letters and words differ you only see ink manifesting in their forms. Nonetheless,they are just ink. They unite in inkness and differ in form, shape, words, and meanings. Just as the ink in those letters is their essence, and the letters in that ink are the essence of that ink and they are composed of varying shapes, secrets, properties and meanings ad nauseum. Likewise, existence in the essences of existence is the essence of those essences. 

Those essences in that existence are the essence of that existence. They are also of various shapes varying shapes, secrets, properties and meanings. Its unity in the essence of that existence does not remove it from the difference of its shapes, secrets, meanings, and properties. Nor does its bifurcation (iftirāq) via those secrets, properties, and meanings remove it from the oneness of that existence as it is with letters and ink. Likewise the unity of the ink does not remove it from the difference of its forms, secrets, meanings, and properties. Nor does its bifurcation in these affairs remove it from its unity in that ink. [...] The truth (of the matter) has been made clear for the one who understood.” ( al-Mishrī 2013, 245) 

in conclusion, he speaks on the matter further, clarifying what the vision of the knower as opposed to the one who is veiled is:

“The result of what has been said is what we said originally and that is that all creation are levels (marātib) of the Truth. One must submit to His decision and what He establishes in His creation. One cannot oppose anything in it. The legal ruling (ḥukm ash-sharʿi) is behind it. He operates in it outwardly and inwardly. This [understanding]  is only for one who knows the unity of existence. He witnesses the distinction (al-faṣl) and the connection (al-waṣl) in it. There are no parts made in it despite the plentitude of its various genera and species. Its unity does not remove it from the bifurcation of its individuals (ashkhāṣihā) in rulings and properties. The Knowers (al-ʿārifīn) remark on this saying: ‘Multiplicity is the essence of unity and unity is the essence of multiplicity.’ The gaze of whoever looks at the multiplicity of existence and the bifurcation of its parts is upon one essence in all its multiplicity. The gaze of whoever looks at its unifying essence is infinitely diversified. This gaze is only for the knower and for none of the people of the veil (aṣḥāb al-ḥijāb). This [vision] is for the one who experiences  the unity (dhawqan), [does] not [merely consider them] theoretically (rasman). This [i.e., the above]  is beyond expression. (However) the meaning is that the distinction is the connection. Unity is the connection. Multiplicity is the distinction. ( al-Mishrī 2013, 246-247) 


al-Mishry, Muḥammad bin. 2013. Rawḍ al-muḥib al-fānī fimā talaqaynā min Sīdī Abī al-ʿAbbās aṭ-Ṭijānī. Beirut: Lebanon.  

Ibn Arabi’s view seems to be based upon maintaining the bifurcation:

“God possesses Nondelimited Being, but no delimitation prevents Him from delimitation. On the contrary, He possesses all delimitations, so He is nondelimited delimitation” (Ibn ‘Arabî, al-Futûhât, 1911 edition, 3:162.23).

Ibn al-ʿArabī in the preface of al-Futūḥāt al-makiyya:

All praise is due to God who generated things from non-existence and His non-existence and conditioned their existence on His Speech’s directive that we may realize the secret of their occurrence and pre-eternity from His Pre-eternity. We realize His Pre-eternity is true as He has taught us. So, He manifested, glorified is He, and manifested and exhibited and did not hide. However, He hid and veiled. The existence of the slave’s essence confirmed the Name “The First” (al-awwal)  and He was [thus] confirmed. Annihilation (al-fanāʿ) and absences’ (al-faqd) decree confirmed The Name “The Last” (al-ākhir) and He was confirmed before that. 

Were it not for always (al-ʿaṣr) and now (al-mʿāṣir), and the ignorant and the informed, no one would know His Name “the First and the Last”, nor “ the Manifest and the HIdden” even though they are His Beautiful Names and [extant] in this radiant way. However, there is a distinction between their (i..e, the Names) dwellings (manāzil) that becomes evident once the circumstances surrounding their lodgings are considered. The slave of the Clement (al-ḥalīm) is not like the slave of the Wise (al-ḥakīm). The slave of the Forgiver (al-ghafūr) is not like the slave of the Thankful (ash-shakūr). Every slave has a Name that is His Lord. He is the body of that reversed Name. Thus, He is “the Omniscient” (al-ʿalīm), glorified is He, who taught (ʿallama) and was instructed (ʿullima). He is the Judge (al-ḥākim) who ruled (ḥakkama) and was ruled (ḥukkama). He is ‘the Overpowering’ (al-qāhir) who overpowered (qahhara) and was oppressed (uqhira). He is ‘ the Able (al-Qādir) who apportions (qaddara), and [also] acquired (kassab) and was not enabled (lam yuqaddar). He is the ‘the Remainder’ (al-bāqī) who cannot carry the quality of remaining (al-baqāʿ). He is “the sanctified” (al-Muqaddas) above confrontation and avoidance during witnessing. Rather, in that most remote place, transcendence attaches to the slave, but not because semblance clings to Him in that praiseworthy station. 

As a result, the slave becomes unaware of the [various] directions in that presence (al-ḥaḍra). His attention disappears as soon as he observes. He praises Him the praise of one who knows that He, glorified is He, ascended via His attributes and elevates, was majestic in His Essence and revealed, that the veil of power outside His majesty is drawn, and that the door anticipating knowledge of Him is locked. The one who speaks to His slave is the ear of the hearer. The action of the act He is ordered to perform is the One Obeyed by the obedient. Once this reality confused me, I recited upon the rule of the caliph’s path (aṭ-ṭarīqa li’l khalīfa):

The Lord is truth (ḥaqq). The slave is truth. 
	Would that I know who is responsible?  
If you say the slave, the slave is dead.
	Or, if you say the Lord then who does He make responsible? 

It is He, glorified is He, who obeys Himself through His creation whenever He desires. He pays Himself of what His right’s obligations deserve. He is naught but spectors devoid of Him, on their thrones devoid of Him. For those who have been guided, the return echo holds a secret. I thank Him the thanking of one who has realized that responsibility is the outward (aspect) of the Name of the Worshiped. With the existence of the reality of ‘there is no ability nor power but through God the reality of generosity (jūd) manifests. Otherwise, were you to make paradise a reward for what you did, then where is the divine generosity (al-jūd al-ilāhī) which you understood. You know that you have been bestowed your essence and that you are primarily veiled from knowledge. Thus, if what you are seeking compensation for what is not yours, how do you see your action? Therefore leave things and their Creator, the sustained and their Sustainer. He is the Bestower who never bores. He is the King whose power is glorified (15) and sublime. He is the Subtle who is aware of His slaves. He is the one who has no likeness. And He is the Hearer and Seer’ (ash-Shūrā: 11). (Ibn al-ʿArabī 1992, 15-16) 
  

Pre-eternity is post-eternity. Post-eternity is pre-eternity and is the presence of the continuity of the secret of the presences. The unseen world is the bisection of the witnessed world. Perhaps the explanation of them both is contained in my words responding to your question about the world of creation and (that of) the affair. The Universe (al-kawn) is the place of manifestation (mathhar) of Divinity (al-ulūhiyya), or that which is divined over or metaphorical existence (al-wujūd al-majāzī) whose realizer is the actual existence (al-wujūd al-ḥaqīqī) or the slave (al-ʿabd). That is to say, before the slave existed he was Allah. Once He made him, He remained as He was. This is why it is said: 

The Lord is a truth (ḥaqq). The slave is a truth. 
	Would that I know who is responsible?  
If you say the slave, the slave is dead.
	Or, if you say the Lord then who does He make responsible? 

However, the truth of the matter is the Lord is not a slave and the slave is not a lord. That which is correct to be a slave is the universe (al-kawn). Shaikh Ibrāhīm Niasse, Jawāhir ar-Rasāʿil vol.1, 116. 

Perhaps Ibn ʿArabī wasn’t quite confused enough, relaying between and depending on the binary between Lord and slave. By contrast, all such arrangements collapse in Niasse's non-structure.


The 21st Chapter of the Verdicts:

A clarification of Hārūn’s response, upon whom be peace, to Muḥyid-dīn b. al-ʿArabī al-Ḥātimī is that the level of Divinity gathers the perfections and encompasses all the Names, Attributes, and Affairs (shuʿūn). Whoever fails to know God in one of His levels [of manifestation] has decreased his experiential knowledge (maʿarifa) [from completion]. The knower (al-ʿārif) is one for whom the secrets of the Names and Attributes with respect to their varying structures and differing manifestations has been uncovered. The entirety is His manifestation. In fate’s manifestations (tajalliyāt ad-duhūr), at times the Truth manifests as a friend and sometimes as a foe: ‘ God is the Ally of the God fearing.’ (45:19), ‘Your only friend is God and His Messenger.’ (5:55), Verily God is the Foe of the Disbelievers.’ (2:98). This [meaning the friendship above] is the manifestation of His Beauty (jamālihi) and this [meaning the enmity above] is the manifestation of His Sublimity (jalālihi). Absolute Perfection (al-kamāl al-muṭlaq) is after these two. Peace. 

Written by Ibrāhīm b. al-Ḥajj ʿAbd Allāh at-Tijānī (Niasse nd, 121)

Jawāhir ar-rasāʿil, Vol. 1, 121


Ibn ʿArabī on the concurrent  understanding of philosopher’s and the people of experiential knowledge:

O examiner! Do not fail to observe that this kind of knowledge which is the prophetic knowledge inherited from them, may God send salutations upon them. If you encounter a matter of theirs that a philosopher, theologian, or the perspicacious in any knowledge mentions, and you then say that the speaker who is a realized Sufi (aṣ-ṣūfī al-muḥaqqiq) is a philosopher because the philosopher mentioned that matter, and he (i.e., the former) said it,  believed it, and that he transmitted it from them or that he has no religion because the philosopher said it and he has no religion, so therefore, do not do it, oh brother!’ This is an empty statement. Not all the philosopher’s knowledge is false. Perhaps this matter he has is from the truth especially if we found that the Messenger, peace be upon him, said it. In particular, if they revealed ascetic wisdom regarding the desires and schemes of the ego, and what evil they intend for the hearts. We should verify the philosopher's words in this specific matter and confirm that they are accurate if we do not know the realities for the Messenger, peace be upon him, said it or the Companion or Mālik, or ash-Shāfīʿ, or Sufyān ath-Thawrī. As for your statement, ‘If you heard it from a philosopher or read it in their books then perhaps you will fall into lies and ignorance,’ as for lies, your statement, ‘he heard it or read it’ and you did not witness him do tha [is enough]. As for ignorance, your inability to distinguish between the truth or falsehood of this matter [is enough]. Your statement, ‘ the philosopher has no religion’ does not mean that because he has no religion that everything he has is false. (56) This is perceived by the basic intelligence of every intellectual. Through your aversion to this Sufi, you have existed from knowledge, sincerity, and religion. You have taken up the path of the ignorant, lies, slander, the deficient intellect and religion, deteriorated observation, and deviation. 

What would you do if he presented it to you in a vision that you saw? Would you do anything but interpret it and seek its meanings? In the same manner, for you to take what this Sufi said and to guide your ego a bit, clearing your mind until its meanings appear to you is better than for you to say on the Day of Judgement: ‘ We were unaware of this. Rather, we were oppressive.’ (21:97) Knowledge is good if it is conveyed clearly and its meanings are understood, approximate, or are sweet to the listener. If he can understand it then it is theoretical knowledge. It would be loathsome and repugnant to [people's] understanding if you articulated that which could only be considered through knowledge of the secrets. Perhaps the weak intolerant mind incapable of managing the insight and researchable realities God placed in it would reject it. For this reason, a knowledgeable person is usually educated through examples and legal discourse. Knowledge of the states is between knowledge of the secrets and intellectual knowledge. The people of [spiritual] experience usually believe in knowledge of the states which is closer to it than intellectual-theoretical knowledge. Rather it approaches necessary intellectual knowledge. Rather it is the same. However, the intellect cannot understand it without a report from its knowledge base or a testimony from a prophet or saint. Due to this reason, it differs from the necessary, but it is essential to its witness. If it pleases you and you accept and believe it, then be happy for it is unveiled to you. You have no other option because nothing cools the chest but what it finds totally correct. The intellectual has no access to it unless a sinless individual presents it. In such a situation, the intellectual is content. No one appreciates the speech of the one capable of sin but the one who has experiential knowledge.  Ibn ʿArabī, al-Futūḥāt al-makiyya Vol.1, 56-57 

Chittick on Ibn ʿArabī’s knowledge of God:

In Chittick's view, Ibn ʿArabī’s view of God has  “no limited, dogmatic definition, but rather [He is] the unknowable Reality that discloses Itself in all things. This Reality is the foundation of all reality, and it is called by many Names.”  (Chittck 2002, 49) This “unmediated knowledge becomes the wellspring for knowledge of everything.”  (Chittck 2002, 49 “He is exposing what sees, and what he witnesses.”   (Chittck 2002, 49)
He states: 
“The overall picture of realized knowledge as Ibn ʿArabī presents it can be summarized like this: From one standpoint, God (49) is infinitely beyond understanding, and only the proper response to Him is silence. From another standpoint, He discloses Himself to creation, and He does so in two basic ways: First HE discloses His undisclosability, and thereby we come to know that we cannot know Him. Second, He discloses himself through scripture, the universe, and the human soul. To the degree that He does so, people can and do come to know Him, but only to the extent their own capacity to understand.”  (Chittick 2002, 49) 


The binary: 1) infinitely beyond understanding (and thus non-disclosure) and silence 2) He discloses Himself to creation (thus engendering understanding). The second is further bifurcates: a) He discloses His undisclosability, and there is understanding b)that we do not understand to whatever capacity they can.


“Ibn al-ʿArabī calls the modality of awareness that discerns God’s undisclosability ‘intellect’ or reason (ʿaql) and he calls the modality of understanding that grasps God’s self-disclosures ‘imagination’ (khayāl). He refers to fully actualized and realized imagination as ‘unveiling,’ which is of course one of the most common terms Sufi texts for the unmediated and privileged knowledge of God that the Sufis strive to acquire. (Chittck 2002, 50) 
The modes of awareness are binary: 1) intellect, 2) imagination. Imagination has two sides: a) When fully realized one is unveiled. b.Thus, the unmentioned corollary is that when one is not fully realized they are veiled.
“Unveiling allows the seeker to recognize the Divine Reality in the images through It discloses itself, and these images are the universe in its entirety, embracing all time and space and all dimensions of reality, such as the spiritual (or intellective) world and the corporeal (or sensory) world. In other words, unveiling allows the people to discern the ‘face’ (wajh) of God in all of the cosmos (ʿālam), which is defined as ‘everything other than God’ (mā siwaʿallāh). It provides experiential knowledge of the meaning of the Quranic verse, ‘Wherever you turn, there is the face of God.’ (Q.2:115)  (Chittck 2002, 50) 
Thus, for Ibn al-ʿArabī, at least per Chittick’s account there are essentially two sides of realization, 1) seeker and the Divine Reality, either 2) recognizing or not recognizing the latter through 3) unveiling as opposed to veiling. 4) There are images and a universe. 5) The former disclose (as opposed to conceal) in a universe of 6) time and space in a further binary of the either 7)spiritual or corporeal cosmos. The latter is defined as 8) ‘everything other than God’ as opposed to “just God.” All of the above provides the cognizance intended in the Quranic verse, 9) ‘Wherever you turn, there is the face of God’ as opposed to not finding Him, where you do not turn, or otherwise. 
“Reason has the natural and innate function of pushing God far away. Left to its own devices, it will abstract God from the world and leave it bereft of His presence. In contrast, imagination has the ability to perceive God’s appearance in the created realm. REason discerns God as absent, but imagination and unveiling see Him as present. When reason grasps God’s distance and inaccessibility it ‘asserts His incomparability’ (tanzīh), that is, it declares God’s transcendence. When imagination sees God present in all things, it ‘asserts His similarity’ (tashbīh), that is, it acknowledges His immanence.Long before Ibn al-ʿArabī, asserting God’s incomparability (or transcendence) had been normative for most versions of Islamic theology, and asserting His similarity (or immanence) was often found in Sufi expressions of Islamic teachings, especially poetry. Ibn al-ʿArabī’s contribution here was to stress the need to keep a balance between the two ways of understanding God. People do this by seeing with the ‘two eyes’ of the heart, that is, reason and imagination. If we fail to see God, the world, and ourselves with the full vision of both eyes, we will not be able to see things as they truly are. The beating of the heart symbolizes the constant shift from one eye to the other.” (Chittick 2002, 50-51) 


The 1) human has two internal epistemological forces from the 2) heart: 1) Reason and Imagination, representing the two eyes above regarding God who is either 1) present or 2) absent either through 1) abstraction ( 2 as opposed to insertion) in the realm that is  1) created (2 as opposed to uncreated). Prior to Ibn al-ʿArabī the Sufis simply stuck to one side of the binary over the other, for the most part. Ibn al-ʿArabī for his part insisted on their simultaneity. Maintaining the binary allows to see Reality (as opposed to non-Reality) as it truly is as opposed to how it truly is not, etc. The human heart’s binary between its two chambers is the 1) material binary representing the 2) metaphysical binary whose continual (as opposed to non-continual) alteration is required to bear witness to Reality. 
“According to Ibn al - ' Arabi , the specific characteristic of our humanity is not that we are rational animals , but that we are made in the divine form . To be a divine form is to be a self - disclosure of God within which every divine name that is ,every real quality found in the cosmos , every attribute of the absolutely Real - can become manifest and known . The human form is both different from God ( incomparable ) and identical with Him ( similar ) . Those who achieve realization differ from ordinary human beings in the clarity of the vision of the two eyes (i.e, 1) reason and 2) of their hearts and the appropriateness of their activity . They have realized the form in which they were created , so they grasp the realities of things in proper balance and respond to every situation as God Himself would respond were He to assume. human form.”   (Chittick 2002, 51) 


Humanity is 1) rational animal and 2) divine form. Divine form is 1) self-disclosure 2) within a Name itself a)  a real quality b) in the cosmos. Every quality (every attribute of the absolutely Real) a.1) manifest and known (a.2 as opposed to concealed and unknown) The human form is 1) is different and 2) identical to God. There are 1)those who realize and 2)those who do not realize this. The realization occurs with 1) two eyes (a. reason, b. imagination) and 2) appropriateness of their activity.   

Chittick relays Ibn al-Arabi's cognizance (ma'arifa) as a thoroughly binary structure. Beginning with the unknowable vs knowable, disclosure vs conceals, Reality vs non-Reality, Reality vs reality, Reality vs things, reality vs non-things, things vs non-things etc and ending with The binary realization occurring with 1) two eyes (a. reason, b. imagination) and 2) appropriateness of their activity. 


Chittick, William C. “Realized Knowledge According to Ibn Arabi .” Journal of the Muhyiddin Ibn ʿArabi Society 71 (2022): 42–61. 


Shaikh Ibrāhīm on the metaphor (al-majāz):

The place of suspension/ anchor (manāṭ) of the Sacred Law is the metaphor (al-majāz). [The latter] is comportment with the presences (al-ḥaḍrāt)... Jawāhir ar-rasāʿil (Inyās n.d Vol. 1, 122) 

“So who is Gabriel such that you would know his reality? “Gabriel” ( lit. ‘the slave of God’ʿAbd Allāh) until you know this slave, let go of any root (ʿaṣl) or which presence (ḥaḍra). We will make the secret of the metaphorical means (sirr al-wāsiṭa al-majāziyya). Thus, the affair is metaphorical without reality (fa al-ʿamr mujāz lā ḥaqqa).” Jawāhir ar-rasāʿil (Inyās n.d Vol. 1, 127) 



Shaikh Ibrahīm on the reality of experiential knowledge (al-mʿarifa):
“Chapter 30 of the Verdicts

“For me the cognizant is someone who has been annihilated once in the essence, two or three times in the attribute, and once in the name.” (Inyās nd Vol. 1, 136; Seesman 2011, 67) 



The constructivist agenda of Western Philosophy aims to build a reality based upon the duality of conceptual distinctions to form a metanarrative i.e., the final word, the thesis. 

Western philosophy has tried to capture the truth through words, even though words are nothing more than differences without essence. In themselves, words indicate things that do not belong outside of the association of words they are found in. The structure they are found in is dualistic in nature. 


Thought is dualistic working in binary opposites for conceptual distinction assigning an arbitrary privilege to one side of the binary over the over.: man vs animal, reason vs intuition, reason vs emotions, inner vs outer, a priori vs posteriori, epistemology vs metaphysics, subjective vs objective, mundane vs divine, material vs immaterial, existence vs non existence. As opposites are defined against one another. Derrida holds that one necessarily implies the other i.e., the juxtaposition between the two justifies them. 

For Derrida, because reality is non-dual, the words used to describe it are also reducible.  

Non duality is to break all these dualities down leading to non-definition. 


Shaikh Ibrāhīm’s proof of his own cognizance in“ A dialogue and conversation between my secret and my lord :

….’Are you cognizant of Allah (t.w.t.)?’ I said: ‘Yes. My proof is my witnessing the essence in other [than Allah] and my realization through my Lord in every designated thing (mutaʿayyun) without designation…” (wa dalīlī ʿalā thālik shuhūdī al-ʿayn fī’l ghayr wa taḥqīqī bi rabbī fī kullī mutaʿayyun bi lā taʿayyun…) Jawaahir (Inyās nd Vol. 2, 125)




Shaikh Ibrāhīm himself warning and guardian against the misappropriated admiration of spiritualists outside the companions of at-Tijānī and their spiritual rank with regard to the latter from the Pearls of Letters (Jawāhir ar-rasāʿil): 

“All praise is due to God. The end of the spiritual poles (al-aqṭāb) is the beginning of the companions of Shaikh at-Tijānī. I have reviewed the [previous] words of the masters of the experiential sciences (arbāb al-maʿārif). I have only located their words in the first step amidst the lowest of the [spiritual] opening’s (al-fatḥ) levels for us. They have not sensed the second and third reality whatsoever, what to say of that which is beyond the two. Do not find it strange should something wondrous occurs from the people of the Fayḍa. I have renewed the permission (i.e., spiritual connection)  for all those whose inner selves have spoken to them (i.e., in admiration) about [spiritual mentors] from outside the companions of the Shaikh [at-Tijānī] with the condition that their selves never speak to them like that afterward. All praise is due to God. This permission is in precaution of the Shaikh’s  jealousy (26) , may God be pleased with him. May God cause us to die and to live on his covenant and love. He is responsible for that and capable of it. Peace. 
Ibrāhīm b. al-Ḥaj ʿAbd Allāh at-Tijānī (Inyās nd., Vol.2, 26-27

Shaikh Ibrāhīm eschews the binary of human thought prior to full realization in his “Three Levels of Religion” In other words, if one were to attain cognizance, one would have to transcend  the notion binary of opposites that constitutes rational thinking. He states in the 57th letter in the Ziyādat ar-rasāīʿil: 

“The second (way-station of Excellence) is witnessing (mushāhadah), or seeing the Truth clearly and thoroughly. As long as a slave can claim the existence of a single hair, he will not arrive at this station. Instead, he is annihilated from the existence of the self, the other (ghayr), and otherness (ghayrīyah) (with respect to Allah), uttering with the tongue of his state that: Nothing remains but Allah, there is nothing but Him. Thus, there is no arrival nor existential difference. This is because there is no name (ism), description (waṣf), symbol (rasm), nor definition (ḥadd) (to be found). This vision has no qualification (min ghayr kayf), nor bounds (lā taḥdīd). It is not united (lā ittiḥād). It has no rememberer (dhākir), nor remembered (madhkūr). Truth has come, and falsehood has departed. Indeed is falsehood [by nature] ever bound to depart. This is the (Q. 17:81) lowest level of the spiritual opening (fatḥ). Whatever is before this is not an opening. This level is the door to experiential knowledge. It is not experiential knowledge itself. Thus, every experiential knower (ʿārif) has experienced a spiritual opening, but not all who have experienced a spiritual opening are experiential knowers. 

The third (way-station of Excellence) is experiential knowledge (maʿrifah), which is the soul’s deep understanding and its fixity in the witnessing presence (ḥaḍrat al-mushāhadah) with complete annihilation (fanā’) and continuity (baqā’) through Allah. According to the Sufis, the experiential knower (ʿārif) sees the other as the same, i.e. he bears witness to the Truth in the other. For me, the (true) experiential knower is the one who has been eradicated in the Essence (Dhāt) once, in the Attribute (Ṣifah) two or three times, and in the Name (Ism) once. He confirms Existence (Wujūd) via the Three Realities (al-Ḥaqā’iq alThalāth). He confirms the Names (Asmā’) through the Name (Ism). 

This station is challenging and harrowing to attain. It is not attained through spending one’s wealth and children (in its pursuit). One who possesses this station is entirely aware of Allah’s decisions and judgments. He is entirely accepting concerning matters of fate. It is appropriate that his self be addressed by Al-lah’s words: And enter among My servants. And enter My Paradise.(Q.89:29-30). Experiential knowledge (maʿrifah) is the conclusion of the stations of true religion. Their introductory station is repentance (tawbah), although it is better than experiential knowledge (i.e. the conclusion), since (true) repentance is the result of experiential knowledge. However, the reality of repentance is the absence (ʿadam) of repentance. This reality is only attained through expe-riential knowledge. This truth is the reason why our Shaykh, the Seal (Khatm) al-Tijānī—mayAllah be satisfied with him, satisfy him, and be satisfied with us through him—says, “I swear byAllah, Who is sole in divinity, I never reached the station of repentance.” He meant that he had repented from noticing his repentance. As long as the slave sees an existential possibility for himself to repent, he has failed to reach the station of repentance.” (Niasse nd, Vol.2, 53-54)


Al Mishri and cognizance’s place beyond the binary of witnessing:

In a letter sent from Niasse to Muḥammad al-Mishrī (d.1975) the people of his village in Maʿaṭa Mawlāna , Mauritania, Niasse engages the latter bearing witness to the praiseworthy attributes of God. Niasse writes:

All praise belongs to God. The slave belongs to God. ‘Blessed is He who revealed the Criterion (al-furqān) upon His slave. Blessed is He in Whose Hand is the outward dominion (mulk), the inward dominion (malakūt), and affair (amr). Is the creation (al-khalq) and the affair (al-amr) not His, Be God exalted! [As is the] spirit (rūḥ) and material (mādda), world (dunyā) and after-life (ukhrā), outward (thāhir) and inward (bāṭin), sensory (ḥiss) and meaningful (maʿanawī), lower (suflī) and upper (ʿulwī), unseen (ghaib) and seen (shahāda), first (awwal), (and) last (ākhir). There is nothing but glorifies His praise. That which is in the heavens and earth has glorified Him. Glorified is God. Say, ‘Look in the heavens and the earth…(Niasse 1986-87, 92) 


The letter mentions an interaction between the two parties. Then al-Mishrī responds with the following: “These verses were said by my father (i.e., ʿAbd Allah Ould al-Ḥajj) to our (spiritual) father (i.e., Niasse), may God be pleased with him: 
 

Enlightenment (al-fatḥ), monotheism (at-tawḥīd), and experiential sciences (al-maʿarif)
	Has three classes, oh cognizant one (ʿārif)!
The enlightened (ṣāḥib al-fatḥ) has certainly rejected
	The existence of other than the One (al-Wāḥid), the Individual (al-Fard), the Unique (al-Aḥd)

For this reason he became a disbeliever, legally due to his having apostasized
	Regarding the words of the Creator (al-Khāliq) of the creations, the Everlasting (aṣ-Ṣamad)

Confirmed for the monotheist (ṣaḥib at-tawḥīd) 
	Are His Qualities (Ṣifātuhu),  and His Actions (faʿalahu) are operative.

The cognizant (al-ʿārifūn) witness His Perfection (kamālahu)
	Outside the cite of Majesty (al-Jalāl),  and Beauty (al-Jamāl) (Niasse 1986-87, 93) 

al-Mishrī seems to be indicating how well he understood the opening greeting of Niasse’s letter by taking his witnessing (mushāda) to the next level wherein cognizance (maʿarifa) is fully realized. There, the cognizant is beyond the binary commensurate with the witnessing conveyed in the  letter above. By doing so, he was also paying tribute to his father who had been the first to discover Niasse as a child. It is presumed that these verses were recited to the youth at the time of their meeting. Thus, al-Mishrī was bonding with Niasse on the depth and type of knowledge that had become secured between them. 
Niasse , Ibrāhīm. 1986-1987.  Al-Juz ath-thalāth min khuṭab wa’r-rasāʿil ash-shaikh Ibrāhīm Inyās, Raḍiya Allāhu ʿanhu. Edited by Muḥammad b. Daḥḥān 1st ed.: Muḥammad b. Daḥḥān, n.d. 


Muḥammad al-Mishrī said in the “Hand Grenades” (Qanābil al-yadawiyya) mentions the place of Ibn al-ʿArabī with relation to the Tijāniyya: 

“Ibn al-ʿArabī al-Ḥātimī said: 

‘Humanity consists of common people, scholars of jurisprudence, aspiring Sufis, Sufis who have received their spiritual openings, and knowers (ʿārifūn). Each group denies the group above it, due to the veil between them. The level of the knowers is where the path of this great pole (Quṭb) Ibn al-ʿArabī al-Ḥātimī ended. Hence why he listed it last-yet is where the path of Shaikh at-Tijānī, may God be pleased with him, companions begins, and beyond it remains many levels.” 

al-Mishrī, Muḥammad, ‘Qanābil al-yadawiyya,’ unpublished manuscript attained by the author, 2023, 12. 


All praise belongs to God. The slave belongs to God. ‘Blessed is He who revealed the Criterion (al-furqān) upon His slave. Blessed is He in Whose Hand is the outward dominion (mulk), the inward dominion (malakūt), and affair (amr). Is the creation (al-khalq) and the affair (al-amr) not His, Be God exalted! [As is the] spirit (rūḥ) and material (mādda), world (dunyā) and after-life (ukhrā), outward (ṭāhir) and inward (bāṭin), sensory (ḥiss) and meaningful (maʿanawī), lower (suflī) and upper (ʿulwī), unseen (ghaib) and seen (shahāda), first (awwal), (and) last (ākhir). There is nothing that does not glorify the praise [of God]. That which is in the heavens and earth has glorified Him. Glorified is God. Say, ‘Look in the heavens and the earth: 

But God’s Light is majestic so nothing is seen
	But through God’s allocation, the Everlasting (aṣ-Ṣamad)

There is no God but God. Muḥammad is the Messenger of God, may God’s Mercy and Peace be upon him. 

My completely beloved al-Mishrī (Verily, God has purchased…) Muḥammad b. ʿAbd Allāh and [his village] Maʿaṭa Mawlāna. May God’s Peace, Mercy, and Blessings be upon you. Your trust has been received. God was faithful to you


Ibn al-ʿArabī on the Truth’s Existence and the Universe’s Existence (wujūd al-Ḥaqq wa’l wujūd al-ʿālam)

“... Truth is not constrained with the existence of the world (al-ʿālam). [It is not ] a priorial [to it] nor co-existence [with it], [nor do so] in temporal dimension [outside of it]. Reality ejects temporal and spatial advances, in Truth's right, in the face of those who say so with specificity, unless they said it out of communication, as the Messenger said it, peace be upon him, or as the Book said it because not everyone can discern these realities. 

Thus, there is nothing left for us to say except that the Truth, Be He exalted, exists by Itself, for Its own sake as Absolute Existence (muṭlaq al-wujūd), not restricted to other-than-He, not caused by anything, nor a cause for anything. Rather, He is, Sublime and Exalted, is the Creator of the effects and causes. He is the Holy King who remains. And that the world exists through Himself, be He exalted, and for Himself as existence restricted to the Existence of [that which is] in Its Self the Truth.  Thus, the existence of the world is not valid at all except through the Existence of the Truth. If time were to become absent from Truth’s Existence and from the principle of the world, then the world would be found outside of time. It is not right for us to say in terms of what the matter is that God Exists before the world since it has been established that “before” is one of the formulas of time, and there is no time. Nor is it for us to say that the world exists after the Truth as afterness does not exist. Nor are we to say that the world exists with the Truth, for the Truth is the one who made it exist, He is the Doer and Inventor of it, while it was nothing. Truth, as we stated earlier, Exists by Itself and for Itself and the world exists through Him alone. 

If a delusional person asked “when” the world’s existence with relation to the Truth’s Existence?” We say: ‘When?’ is a temporal question. Time is from the world of relationships and is created by God, be He exalted. 

It does not depend on it before or after its existence, nor in temporal afterness (baʿadiyya zamāniyya). [...] There is nothing left to say but that the Truth, be He exalted,  exists through His Essence for His Essence (maujūd bi dhātihi li dhātih). [He is] Absolute Existence (muṭlaq al-wujūd), non-limited by other than He, 

Ibn al-ʿArabī on the Possibility of Knowledge of the Essence and the Qualities from the Futūḥāt:

Know that there are four objects of knowledge (al-maʿalūmat). [The first of them is] The Truth. He is described as Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) because He was not caused  (maʿlūl li shayʿ) nor is He a cause (ʿilla). Rather, He exists as His Essence (maujūd bi dhātihi). “God's Knowledge” refers to the awareness of His existence. There is no difference between His Existence and His Essence, yet His Essence is unknown. He can only be recognized via approximation through His Attributes. By Attributes I mean the Attributes of Meaning (Ṣifāt al-maʿānī). These are the Attributes of Perfection (Ṣifāt al-kamāl). It is forbidden to gain knowledge of the reality of the Essence (118). It is not known through evidence nor proof. It is indefinable. He does not resemble anything. Nothing resembles Him. How can that which resembles things know one who is not resembled by anything nor does He resemble anything? The only thing you know about Him is that He is unlike anything else and that He warns you about Himself. The Sacred Law prohibits contemplation of God's Essence.  Futūḥāt 1. 118-119 


Know that there are four objects of knowledge (al-maʿalūmat). [The first of them is] The Truth (al-Ḥaqq). He is described as Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) because He was not caused  (maʿlūl li shayʿ) nor is He a cause (ʿilla). Rather, He exists as His Essence (maujūd bi dhātihi). “The Knowledge of God” refers to the awareness of His Existence. There is no difference between His Existence and His Essence, yet His Essence is unknown. He can only be recognized via approximation through His Attributes. By Attributes I mean the Attributes of Meaning (Ṣifāt al-maʿānī). These are the Attributes of Perfection (Ṣifāt al-kamāl). It is forbidden to gain knowledge of the reality of the Essence (118). It is not known through evidence nor proof. It is indefinable. He does not resemble anything. Nothing resembles Him. How can that which resembles things know one who is not resembled by anything nor does He resemble anything? The only thing you know about Him is that He is unlike anything else and that He warns you about Himself. The Sacred Law prohibits contemplation of God's Essence.  Futūḥāt 1. 118-119

In Ibn al-ʿArabī, the Essence does not provide an entry point into the roots and paths of knowledge about Its Essence, the Truth (i.e., God) is paradoxically beyond the scope of any theory of knowledge. As essence and existence are synonyms their treatment is synonymous thus, there is no inroad provided for the studying existence as it pertains to the Truth either. Ontology and epistemology are out of the question, leaving only the once removed approximate awareness of the existence of the Essence via the Attributes of Meanings (Ṣifāt al-maʿānī). 

The Attributes of Meaning are typically seven: 1) Ability (al-Qudra), 2) Will (al-Irāda), 3) Knowledge (al-ʿIlm), 4) Life (al-Ḥayāt) 5) Hearing (al-Samuʿ), 6) Seeing (al-Baṣr), 7) Speech (al-Kalām). According to the above, while Absolute Existence is beyond qualification (a qualification all its own, ironically) Knowledge is one of its Necessary Qualities (read as “limitations?”). Based upon Ibn al-ʿArabī’s view, while Knowledge is commensurate with the Essence, the latter is unknowable and as such so is His Knowledge. 

Putting aside epistemic language momentarily, all we may recognize regarding Existence, then, is that He has it. That is to say, while we may concede to the Truth, that concession in no way provides epistemic access to God: He exists, whatever that may mean. The utter lack of onto-epistemic overlap between us and God means that whatever we may say regarding His Knowledge, other than He must Know, logically speaking, is mere indiscernible approximation (for closeness to what is achieved by what, exactly). The Attributes of Meaning, Knowledge, in particular are concomitant with the Essence, that is, they are simultaneous with Existence, for Ibn al-ʿArabī. Wherever Existence is concerned, Knowledge is implied. However, neither are onto-epistemically accessible. He is onto-epistemically free of other-than-It. II 533.4 SPK 64

The Truth is onto-epistemically separate from the Names well. 

The Truth is onto-epistemically free from With regard to the the Names (al-asmāʿ) and the Essence, Ibn al-ʿArabī states:



	Theologians divide between essence and attribute, and creation ibn arabi divides between essence attribute of meaning and all other onto-epistemic considerations

Ḥassan Cisse (d. 2008), a grandson of Niasse, the Imam of the Mosque of Madina Baye, Kaolack, considered the relationship between the Essence and Knowledge in his commentary on Niasse’s “The Spirit of Good Morals.” He said: 

The people of the knowledge of jurisprudence argue with the Sufis over the closeness of Allah. The former claims that Allah is with His creations in knowledge, while His Essence remains somewhere. But the Sufis maintain that Allah is with us in every respect, whether in Essence or Knowledge. The proof of the Sufis is (72) the Qur'an. Allah says in the description of death in the Qur'an:"When it (the soul) reaches the throat (during death). You shall by this time be looking (at the dying).We are however closer to him (the dying) than you, but you cannot see."(Q.56:83-85) 

“From the above verse,” he continues: “we deduce that Allah is with us in His Essence, as only Essence can be seen or not seen, contrary to knowledge which is not visible. Allah also said in the Qur'an (7:7): "And We shall narrate to them (their past actions) with knowledge, for We were never absent." 

Here Allah mentions two things, knowledge and presence (by essence). The 
jurist usually claim that Allah is physically established on the throne, and 
justify this claim by referring to verses of the Qur'an such as 7:54 where 
Allah says: 

"Your Guardian Lord is God, Who created the heavens and the earth in six 
days and is firmly Established on the Throne (of Authority)." 

Other similar verses include Qur'an 10:3, 12:100, 13:2, 20:5, 32:4, and 
57:4. However, all of these refer to the Throne of Authority and NOT [the] 
ESSENCE OF ALLAH. 

To further disapprove their argument, Allah said in Qur'an 69:17: "And the angels will be on its sides And eight will, that day, carry the throne of the Lord above them." Certainly these angels couldn't (be) carrying the Essence of Allah, Glory be 
to Him, over their heads! (Niasse, and Cisse 2001, 71-72)

Niasse Ibrāhīm, and Ḥassan Cisse. 2001. “The Spirit of Good Morals” (Ruḥ al-adab). Edited by ʿAbd al-Hakīm Halīm. 2nd ed. Kaolack, Senegal: The African American Institute.
According to this timeline and later examples, the identity of the "Sufis" in Tijānī  changes with the context of their writings. The term seems to apply to groups inclined toward intuitive knowledge, as opposed to those who study theological sciences. Cisse states: 

The people of the knowledge of jurisprudence argue with the Sufis over the closeness of Allah. The former claims that Allah is with His creations in knowledge, while His Essence remains somewhere. But the Sufis maintain that Allah is with us in every respect, whether in Essence or Knowledge. The proof of the Sufis is (72) the Qur'an. Allah says in the description of death in the Qur'an:"When it (the soul) reaches the throat (during death). You shall by this time be looking (at the dying).We are however closer to him (the dying) than you, but you cannot see."(Q.56:83-85) 


Conversely, for Niasse, cognizance ‘begins’ and continues in the Essence. There are no names or attributes that get expressed. For Niasse, the Name(s) are inseparable from the Named, i.e., the Essence.


 I think this quote, even more so than the quotes by sh tijani & sh ibrahim, is more direct and piercing. It goes directly to the heart of the matter: the unknowability and inaccessibility of the Essence for the Akbarians. Precisely because Akbarian thinking is founded on the inaccessibility of the Essence (find evidence for this) is why their thinking remains dualistic throughout. Sh Hassan brillantly points out here that “only Essence can be seen or not seen,” that is to say—Essence alone eradicates the bifurcation between transcendence/immanence, seen/unseen, knowable/unable, etc… 

To say that ‘God is so nondelimited  that he’s not delimited by delimitation‘ is ironically to privilege ‘Nondelimition’. Conversely, for the Tijaniya, God(Essence) is ‘beyond’/‘before’ all dichotomies, even that of nondelimitation/delimitation. Because Akbarians do not engage the Essence, their marifa inevitably accents/privileges something, starting with Nondelimitation (what does that even mean?!) This is, of course, a matter that only the arifeen can understand, as Sh Tijani noted. 

Sh Hassan’s quote sets the foundation for engaging the radical non-dualist language of Sh Tijani and Sh Ibrāhīm.

Introduction


Onto-epistemics considers the study of ontology and epistemology at once. It does not presuppose a distinction between the two on the basis that one is what they know and only know what they are. Monism is a theory or doctrine wherein onto-epistemics are considered with the supposition that denies the distinction between apparent opposites like matter and mind, or God and the world. Dualism considers onto-epistemics presupposing the above distinction between such opposites. Non-duality, finally, is neither monistic or dualistic. Rather, it forgoes such distinctions altogether. 

I would like to explore non-dualism through Jacques Derrida's (d. 2004) différance. Différance, a play on the French words “différer” meaning “to defer” or “to differ.” The meaning of words, he suggested is suspended and as such other than what it conjures for the one who engages it. Thus, 

The key idea behind différance is that the meaning of words is always deferred such that no absolute meaning may be determined through them. On this basis, one cannot decipher the epistemic essence of a word as  Concepts, delivered to us through language, are, like the latter, devoid of essence


Question: Are Ibn al-Arabī’'s and the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics based upon the same assumption? 

Conclusion: The binary underpinning Ibn al-Arab's onto-epistemic structure informs us of its dualism. 

Conclusion: A radical non-dualist premise underpins the Faya's onto-epistemic structure.

Conclusion: Ibn al-ʿArabī cannot escape onto-epistemic dualism while the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics function fluidly within radical non-dualist freedom. 


Conclusion


A binary underpins Ibn al-Arab's onto-epistemic structure. A non-dualist premise underpins the Faya's onto-epistemic structure. Ibn al-ʿArabī cannot escape onto-epistemic dualism while the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics function fluidly within non-dualist freedom. A problem with Ibn al-Arab's onto-epistemics is that he cannot escape onto-epistemic dualism, whereas the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics operate fluidly non-dualistically.

A non-dualist premise underpins the Faya's onto-epistemic structure.

Ibn al-ʿArabī cannot escape onto-epistemic dualism while the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics function fluidly within non-dualist freedom. 

A problem with Ibn al-Arab's onto-epistemics is that he cannot escape onto-epistemic dualism, whereas the Fayḍa’s onto-epistemics operate fluidly non-dualistically.

On Leaving the Tariqa:
On Leaving the Tariqa 

#رسالة  بخط سيدي أحمد التجاني رضي اللَّه عنه

بعد البسملة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العبد الفقير إلى الله أحمد بن محمد التجاني أن طريقتي طريقة محمدية أعطاها صلى الله عليه وسلم منه اليّ وتلاميذي تلاميذه صلى الله عليه وسلم وفقرائي فقراؤه ولم تكن هذه الطريقة لغيري من أولياء من آدم إلى النفخ في الصور ولأصحابي عند الله وعند رسوله في الدار الاخرة من فضل الله والعز الأكبر في الآخرة أمر لا مطمع فيه لغير الصحابة من جميع الأولياء حتى الأقطاب لا يلحقون مراتب أصحابي في الآخرة لكن لا يتأتى لطريقي الا التفرد بها فمن ذكر وردا من أوراد المشايخ مع وردنا فهو خارج عن طريقتنا المحمدية وكل الطرق لجميع الشيوخ تدخل عليهما طريقي وتبطلها ولا يخاف ترك طريق غيرنا لطريقتنا لا في الدنيا ولا في الاخرة ومن تعمد وادخل طريق أخرى على طريقنا حل به الهلاك في الدنيا والاخرى ومن ترك طريق غيرنا لاجل طريقتنا فهو آمن في الدنيا والاخرة وهذا لنا على جميع الأقطاب والأكابر ولنا عليهم الحرمة الدايمة والعلو الكامل في الدنيا والأخرة من عظم منهم شأنه ومن صغر والله ولي التوفيق وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد واله
منقول ،
￼

“On Leaving the Tariqa”

#رسالة  بخط سيدي أحمد التجاني رضي اللَّه عنه

بعد البسملة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العبد الفقير إلى الله أحمد بن محمد التجاني أن طريقتي طريقة محمدية أعطاها صلى الله عليه وسلم منه اليّ وتلاميذي تلاميذه صلى الله عليه وسلم وفقرائي فقراؤه ولم تكن هذه الطريقة لغيري من أولياء من آدم إلى النفخ في الصور ولأصحابي عند الله وعند رسوله في الدار الاخرة من فضل الله والعز الأكبر في الآخرة أمر لا مطمع فيه لغير الصحابة من جميع الأولياء حتى الأقطاب لا يلحقون مراتب أصحابي في الآخرة لكن لا يتأتى لطريقي الا التفرد بها فمن ذكر وردا من أوراد المشايخ مع وردنا فهو خارج عن طريقتنا المحمدية وكل الطرق لجميع الشيوخ تدخل عليهما طريقي وتبطلها ولا يخاف ترك طريق غيرنا لطريقتنا لا في الدنيا ولا في الاخرة ومن تعمد وادخل طريق أخرى على طريقنا حل به الهلاك في الدنيا والاخرى ومن ترك طريق غيرنا لاجل طريقتنا فهو آمن في الدنيا والاخرة وهذا لنا على جميع الأقطاب والأكابر ولنا عليهم الحرمة الدايمة والعلو الكامل في الدنيا والأخرة من عظم منهم شأنه ومن صغر والله ولي التوفيق وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد واله
منقول ،

A Letter in the Handwriting of Sayyidi Ahmad al-Tijani — may Allah be pleased with him

After the basmala (In the Name of Allah…) and prayers upon the Prophet — peace and blessings be upon him — the poor servant in need of Allah, Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Tijani, said:

“My Tariqa is a Muhammadan Tariqa. He — peace and blessings be upon him — gave it from himself to me, and my disciples are his — peace be upon him — disciples, and my poor ones (fuqara’) are his poor ones. This Tariqa was not for anyone else among the saints (awliya’) from Adam until the blowing of the trumpet (on Judgment Day). For my companions, with Allah and with His Messenger, in the Hereafter, from the bounty of Allah and the greatest honor in the Afterlife — it is something that no one outside of my companions can hope for, from among all the saints, even the Qutbs (spiritual poles); they do not reach the ranks of my companions in the Hereafter.

But it is only possible in my Tariqa to adhere to it exclusively. Whoever mentions a wird (litany) from the awrad (litanies) of the shuyukh (other spiritual masters) along with our wird is outside of our Muhammadan Tariqa. And all the paths of all the shuyukh, when combined with my path, nullify it. And there is no fear in leaving any other path for our path — not in this world nor in the Hereafter. But whoever deliberately introduces another path into ours, destruction will befall him in this world and the Hereafter. And whoever leaves another path for the sake of our path is safe in this world and the Hereafter.

This applies to us over all the Qutbs and the great ones, and for us over them is permanent reverence and complete superiority in this world and the Hereafter — whether their station is great or small. And Allah is the One who grants success. And may blessings be upon our Master Muhammad and his family.”

The Supplication: “Yā Man Az’hara al-Jamīl”:
The Supplication: “Yā Man Az’hara al-Jamīl”

1. O the One who has manifested beauty
ﻳﺎ ﻣﻦ ﺃﻇﻬﺮ ﺍﻟﺠﻤﻴﻞ ﻭﺳﺘﺮ ﺍﻟﻘﺒﻴﺢ
Yā Man az’hara al-Jamīla wa Sattara al-Qabīḥa
Oh You who manifested beauty and concealed what is ugly.

2. Who did not reproach the offensive, nor tear the veils
ﻭﻟﻢ ﻳﺆﺍﺧﺬ ﺑﺎﻟﺠﺮﻳﺮﺓ ﻭﻟﻢ ﻳﻬﺘﻚ ﺍﻟﺴﺘﺮ
Wa lam yu’ākhidh bil-jarīrah, wa lam yahtik as-sitra
And did not take to task for the wrong, nor tear the veil.

3. O Great Pardoner, O Best in Overlooking
ﻭﻳﺎ ﻋﻈﻴﻢ ﺍﻟﻌﻔﻮ ﻭﻳﺎ ﺣﺴﻦ ﺍﻟﺘﺠﺎﻭﺯ
Wa yā ‘Aẓīma al-‘Afwi wa yā Ḥasana at-Tajāwuz
O Great in Forgiveness, O Best in Overlooking.

4. O Extensive in Forgiveness, O One who stretches out both hands in Mercy
ﻭﻳﺎ ﻭﺍﺳﻊ ﺍﻟﻤﻐﻔﺮﺓ ﻭﻳﺎ ﺑﺎﺳﻂ ﺍﻟﻴﺪﻳﻦ ﺑﺎﻟﺮﺣﻤﺔ
Wa yā Wāsi‘a al-Maghfirah, wa yā Bāsita al-Yadayn bi-Raḥmah
O Wide in Forgiveness, O One whose hands are extended with Mercy.

5. O Hearer of every secret, O End of every complaint, O Generous in Pardon
ﻭﻳﺎ ﺳﺎﻣﻊ ﻛﻞ ﻧﺠﻮﻯ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﻨﺘﻬﻰ ﻛﻞ ﺷﻜﻮﻯ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻛﺮﻳﻢ ﺍﻟﺼﻔﺢ
Wa yā Sāmi‘a kulli Najwā, wa yā Muntahā kulli Shakwā, wa yā Karīma aṣ-Ṣafḥi
O Hearer of every whisper, End of every complaint, Generous in pardon.

6. O Magnificent in Gifts, O Lifter of Stumbles, O Beginner of Blessings before they are deserved
ﻭﻳﺎ ﻋﻈﻴﻢ ﺍﻟﻤﻦ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﻘﻴﻞ ﺍﻟﻌﺜﺮﺍﺕ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﺒﺘﺪﺋﺎ ﺑﺎﻟﻨﻌﻢ ﻗﺒﻞ ﺍﺳﺘﺤﻘﺎﻗﻬﺎ
Wa yā ‘Aẓīma al-Manni, wa yā Muqīla al-‘Atharāt, wa yā Mubtadi’an bi-n-Na‘am qabla istiḥqāqihā
O Tremendous in bestowal, Reliever of stumblers, Originator of blessings before they are earned.

7. O my Lord, O my Master, O my Protector, O my utmost desire
ﻳﺎ ﺭﺑﻲ ﻭﻳﺎ ﺳﻴﺪﻱ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﻮﻻﻱ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻏﺎﻳﺔ ﺭﻏﺒﺘﻲ
Yā Rabbī, wa yā Sayyidī, wa yā Mawlāyā, wa yā Ghāyata Raghabatī
O my Lord, O my Master, O my Patron, O Zenith of my longing.

8. I ask You not to disfigure my character with the trials of this world or the punishment of the Fire
ﺃﺳﺄﻟﻚ ﺃﻥ ﻻ ﺗﺸﻮﻩ ﺧﻠﻘﺘﻲ ﺑﺒﻼﺀ ﺍﻟﺪﻧﻴﺎ ﻭﻻ ﺑﻌﺬﺍﺏ ﺍﻟﻨﺎﺭ
As’aluka an lā tushawwih khalqatī bi-balā’i ad-dunyā wa lā bi-‘adhābi an-Nār
I ask You not to disfigure my being through worldly affliction or the punishment of the Fire.

Ameen. Thumma Ameen!

⸻

Virtue and Merit of the Duʿāʾ

Source: Jawāhir al-Ma‘ānī wa Bulūgh al-Amānī fī Fayḍ Sīdī Abī al-‘Abbās at-Tijānī by Sidi Abul Ḥasan ʿAlī Ḥarāzim Berrāda al-Fāsī (d. 1212/1797)
	•	This duʿāʾ is considered greater in merit than Hizb Sayfī.
	•	Reported from the Holy Prophet (SAW) through Jibrīl (AS) as a gift from Allah.
	•	The angels cannot enumerate its virtues, even if they tried until the Day of Judgment.
	•	Whoever recites it will:
	•	Have their defects veiled in this world and the next.
	•	Be forgiven, even of major sins.
	•	Be showered with abundant mercy.
	•	Be granted nobility like the prophets.
	•	Be freed from the Fire along with their family and a thousand others through their intercession.
	•	Have their heart filled with īmān.
	•	Be loved by all creation on the Day of Judgment.

Gabriel said this is the duʿāʾ of the inhabitants of Bayt al-Maʿmūr, and the Prophet (SAW) was told to teach it only to the righteous.



O The One who has manifested beauty 

ﻳﺎ ﻣﻦ ﺃﻇﻬﺮ ﺍﻟﺠﻤﻴﻞ ﻭ ﺳﺘﺮ ﺍﻟﻘﺒﻴﺢ
-Yaa Man az'hara-l-Jameela wa Sattara-l-Qabeeha.
-Oh The One who has manifested beauty and concealed what is ugly.


ﻭﻟﻢ ﻳﺆﺍﺧﺬ ﺑﺎﻟﺠﺮﻳﺮﺓ ﻭﻟﻢ ﻳﻬﺘﻚ ﺍﻟﺴﺘﺮ
-wa lam yu'aakhidh bil- Jareerah, wa lam yah'tik as-sitra.
-Who did not reproach the offensive, nor shred the veils (covering our faults).


ﻭﻳﺎ ﻋﻈﻴﻢ ﺍﻟﻌﻔﻮ ﻭﻳﺎ ﺣﺴﻦ ﺍﻟﺘﺠﺎﻭﺯ
-wa yaa Azeem al-Af'wi. Wa yaa Hassan at-Tajaawuz.
-Oh Great Benefactor. Oh goodly  Overlooker.


ﻭﻳﺎ ﻭﺍﺳﻊ ﺍﻟﻤﻐﻔﺮﺓ ﻭﻳﺎ ﺑﺎﺳﻂ ﺍﻟﻴﺪﻳﻦ ﺑﺎﻟﺮﺣﻤﺔ
-wa yaa Waasi'a al-Maghfirat. Wa yaa Baasita al-Yadayni bi Rahmah.
-Oh Extensive forgiver. Oh You whose hands are outstretched with Mercy.


ﻭ ﻳﺎ ﺳﺎﻣﻊ ﻛﻞ ﻧﺠﻮﻯ ﻭ ﻳﺎ ﻣﻨﺘﻬﻰ ﻛﻞ ﺷﻜﻮﻯ ﻭ ﻳﺎ ﻛﺮﻳﻢ ﺍﻟﺼﻔﺢ
-wa yaa Saami'ha kullu Najwaa. Wa yaa Muntahaa kullu Shakwaa. Wa yaa Kareem as-Saf'hi.
-Oh One who hears every intimate discourse. Oh you who are the end of every grievance. Oh you who are the best in place after every stumble


ﻭﻳﺎ ﻋﻈﻴﻢ ﺍﻟﻤﻦ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﻗﻴل العثرات ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﺒﺘﺪﺋﺎ ﺑﺎﻟﻨﻌﻢ ﻗﺒﻞ ﺍﺳﺘﺤﻘﺎﻗﻬﺎ
-Wa yaa Azeem al-Manni. Wa yaa Muqeel al-'Athraati. Wa yaa Mubtadi'aan bi Ni'ami qabla isti'hqaaqihaa.
Oh You who are Great in Bestowal. Oh You who are the Refuge for the stumblers. Oh You who are the source of unearned blessing


ﻳﺎ ﺭبي  ﻭﻳﺎ ﺳﻴﺪﻱ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻣﻮﻻﻱ ﻭﻳﺎ ﻏﺎﻳﺔ ﺭﻏﺒﺘﻲ
-yaa Rabii, wa yaa Sayidii, wa yaa Mawlaaya. Wa yaa Gaayata Ragbatii.
-Oh my Lord, Oh my Master, Oh my Patron. The zenith of my longing;


ﺃﺳﺄﻟﻚ ﺃﻥ ﻻ ﺗﺸﻮﻩ ﺧﻠﻘﺘﻲ ﺑﺒﻼﺀ ﺍﻟﺪﻧﻴﺎ ﻭﻻ ﺑﻌﺬﺍﺏ ﺍﻟﻨﺎﺭ
-as'haluka an laa tushawiha khulqatii bi-balaa'i dunyaa wa laa bi 'adhaabi naar!
-I ask that You not disfigure my character by the affliction of the world, or by the punishment of the (Hell) Fire!

Aameen thumma Aameen!!!

THE VIRTUE OF THE DUA
'YAA MAN AZ'HARA-L-JAMEEL.....'
via: http://www.duas.org/yaman.htm
Here the Holy Prophet (SAW) said to Gabriel:
What is the virtue of these words?
Gabriel said: Far away! Far away! It is
something impossible, for if the angels of seven
heavens and seven earths gather to describe its
virtues till the Day of Judgment, they are not able
to describe a single part of it.”
“Therefore when a man says: O You who reveal
the beauty and conceal the ugly, God covers up
his defects and has mercy on him and makes him
7
look beautiful on the Day of Judgment and
covers his defects with a thousand veils in the
world and the hereafter.”
“And when he says: O You who do not take the
wrongdoer to task and do not tear the veil, God
will not take him to task on the Day of Judgment
and on the day all veils are torn, God will not tear
his veil.”
“And when he says: O You who are Great
Forgiver, God will forgive his sins even if they
are as much as the sea foam.”
“And when he says: O You are of great
forbearance, God will forgive him such sins as
theft, drinking wine, and other sins.”
8
“And when he says: O You who have pardon
abounding, God will open seventy gates of
Mercy to him in a way that he will be
overwhelmed by God’s Mercy till he dies.”
“And when he says: O You who have opened
Your hands for mercy, God opens His hands of
Mercy to him.”
“And when he says: O Hearer of all whisperings,
O You to whom all complaints are made, God
will give him rewards as many as given to every
afflicted and unaffiliated, every losing and sick
as well as destitute and every one affected by
calamity till the Day of Judgment.”
9
“And when he says: O Possessor of great
favor, God will make him noble as prophets.”
“And when he says: O You who give blessings
to Your servants when they do not deserve it,
God will grant him rewards as many as the
number of those who have thanked His
blessings.”
“And when he says: O our Master, O our Lord,
God will say: My angels! Be witness that I
forgave him and I will give him rewards as many
as those being in paradise and Hell, the seven
heavens and the earths, the sun, the moon, the
stars, drops of rain, sands mountains, dews and
throne.”
10
“And when he says: O our Guardian, God will
make his heart replete with faith.”
“And when he says: O the Goal of our desires,
God will give him the love of all creatures on the
Day of Judgment.”
“And when he says: I beseech You O God not to
make my being ugly with Fire, God will say: My
servant has asked Me to free him from Fire. O
My angels! Be witness that I set him, his parents,
his brothers, his household, his children and his
neighbors free from the Fire and accepted his
intercession for a thousand others who deserved
the punishment by fire and saved them from it.”
“O Muhammad! Teach this Dua only to men of
11
piety. Do not even teach it to hypocrites, for it is
a Dua which God will answer. This is the Dua
recited by the men of Bayt al-Ma’moor (an
edifice in the seventh heaven as sacred as
Ka’aba) when they circumambulate it.”
“While being happy and having a smile on his
lips, Gabriel come down from heaven to the
Holy Prophet (SAW) bringing the following
Dua saying: God has sent a gift for you.
The Holy Prophet said: What is the gift O
Gabriel! Gabriel said: Words along with
treasures of heaven by which God has honoured
you.
