Al-jāmiʿli-durar al-quṭb al-maktūm:
Al-jāmiʿli-durar al-quṭb al-maktūm

Shaikh al-Tijānī (ra) on the difference between the absolute oneness of existence (al-aḥadiyya), relative oneness (al-waḥda), and monism (al-wāḥidiyya)
The most approximate statement about the difference between absolute oneness of existence (al-aḥadiyya), relative oneness (al-waḥda), and monism (al-wāḥidiyya) is that the absolute oneness of existence is an ontological level (martaba) of the Truth’s nature (s.w.t.) (kunh al-ḥaqq) which is His manifestation through His Essence to HIs Essence through all of His Attributes (ṣifātih) and Names (asmāʿih) for all the commensurate requisites (al-lawzim) and necessities (al-muqtaḍiyāt) therein. None but He has access to it. Relative oneness is His manifestation to His Messenger (s.a.w.s.) through some of His Attributes and Names. Much of what occurs in the absolute oneness of existence is kept from him. Monism is His manifestation to all of the prophets, messengers, the righteous, and knowers through His Divine Attributes and Names (bi ṣifātih wa asmāʿih al-lahūtiyya). This [ontological level] is what the creation seeks [its needs from]. He hides much of what He reveals to His Messenger, our master Muḥammad (s.a.w.s.), regarding His Attributes and Names.
The difference between these two levels is only understood experientially. Mere statements do not reveal anything about them. Instead, such statements are mere approximations for the sake of conceptual understanding. No one knows the meaning of these expressions but those who have experienced them. As for [the statement above regarding one who] wanted to drown in oceans of relative oneness, relative oneness is the previously mentioned manifestation to the Prophet (s.a.w.s.). The essence (al-ʿayn) of relative oneness is the Muhammadan Reality (al-ḥaqīqa al-muḥammadiyya). To be drowned in it is to view it without veils. This perspective is from amongst those undefined and limitless virtues, gifts, secrets, and wisdom. As for drowning in the essence of the ocean of relative oneness without veils-none but he (s.a.w.s.) can do so. (Al-Mishry n.d., 174)
Work Cited
Al-Mishry, Muḥammad. n.d. Al-jāmiʿli-durar al-quṭb al-maktūm. Rabāṭ: dar al-imān.

Shaikh al-Tijani and Allah's Absolute Divinity (The Oneness of Existence and The Existential Affair)
Know that the Truth’s Presence (ḥaḍrat al-ḥaqq) (s.w.t.) is one with regard to the Essence (al-ḏāt), the Attributes (aṣ-ṣifāt), the Names (al-asmāʿ), and aspects (al-wujūh). Existence, in every sense, faces the Exalted Presence (al-ḥaḍra al-ʿalā) with humility, (pg.167) self-abasement, enslavement, and passivity underneath the coercive power(of Allah), in obedience, love, exaltation, and reverence. There are those amongst them who encounter the form of the Divine Presence (al-ḥaḍra al-ilāhīyya) explicitly and obviously in the obliteration of other (al-ġayr) and otherness (al-ġayriyya). Amongst them are those who encounter the Exalted Presence from behind a thick veil. They are the idol worshippers and whoever resembles them. This is because while they are focused on their idols they have not focused on any other than the Truth (s.w.t.) and do not worship other than He. However, the Truth (s.w.t.) manifests to them behind these veils with His exaltedness and sublimity, enrapturing them according to that focus based upon the fate (al-qaḍā) and destiny (al-qadr) of which no dispute can be made with Him. This is the [idea of] ‘mandatory engagement’ with Allah. He says (s.w.t.) [regarding it], ‘and to Allah prostrates whoever is within the heavens and earth, willingly or by compulsion…). (13:15)
So, all of existence, each individual one by one (fardan farda), engages the Presence of the Truth (s.w.t.) in the manner we have mentioned. The disbelievers, rebels, criminals, and oppressors are all included in that comingling (al-taḫlīṭ) wherein they contradict the text of the Sacred Law and the outward form of the Divine Command. They are only outside of His decision and desire by contravening Allah’s command (t.a.) for having abandoned the external form of the Divine Command while being drowned in it internally. If you understand this, know that the universe (al-kawn), each individual existent, one by one-every one of its atoms is a level (martaba) for the Truth. He governs it with a specific decision. He does not rule another level with the same judgment. He acts with a specific action which He does not do so elsewhere. He engages that atom in a specific fashion with which He does not show toward others. Contentment and submission to Him are obligatory regarding HIs judgment. They have disobeyed Allah’s command outwardly while fulfilling it inwardly and do not realize it. They do not receive a reward afterward, retribution, or penalty in the Abode (p.168) of Returning (dār al-maʿāb) as [commensurate] punishment or a blessing. All of that is decided by the Will’s Determination (ḥukm al-mashīʿa) which can not be refuted. He is not asked about what He does. If you understood and pondered over this you would find that every single atom in existence has an engagement with the Truth specific to it that it does not share with others. Perhaps other atoms are like it in a specific way but they differ in other ways.
Apply this principle and travel with it throughout all the parts of existence from angels, humans, and others, and know the various ways in which the creation engages the Truth’s Presence. If you know this and have rightfully distinguished it, a great field of direct experiential knowledge (al-maʿarifa) of Allah (t.w.t.) has expanded for you. The expansion of His manifestations in existence has no limit nor restriction outside of the Sacred Law and the Reality’s commingling in this arena.
The decisive word in the matter [above] is that He (s.w.t.) is the Mover of all existence (al-muḥrrik li-jamīʿi al-wujūd). He is in charge of all their affairs (qāʾim ʿalayhim fī kullī amr), established in every move and stillness (muqīm lahum fi kulli ḥaraka wa sukūn) for their benefit. Nothing belongs to them independently. They have no force, movement, decision, advance, or delay. Rather, they are in His grasp (s.w.t.) (pg.169) and under His Will’s decision. He does with them as He likes, turns them whichever way He wants, in whatever He wants, good or evil, beneficial or harmful, in obedience or disobedience, drawing near or dispersing. Then, [understand that He is] behind this reality and has manifested with that wisdom.

The Sacred Law is determined by conditions, means, precepts, exigencies, and requirements. [Regardless], there is no disengagement in this wisdom from what He wants (s.w.t.). All of this runs according to the law of the Will. It is then arranged in the form of this wisdom in accordance with the [various] aspects of these precepts and ties as divine rulings. He called them limits, punitive measures, rewards, penalties, fear, and hope. No one can escape these precepts and restrictions. He may judge and choose whatever action He does in the form of the Reality and the Sacred Law. He is not disputed with nor is it said to Him, ‘why did you do this or to what end, nor upon what grounds?' There is nothing [left] but the extension of the neck, the closing of the eyes, and the submission of the heart underneath the Sultan of Divinity and Sublimity. Peace. (al-Mishry n.d., 167-170)
Works Cited
—Al-Mishry, Muḥammad ibn. n.d. al-Jāmiʿ li-durar al-ʿulūm al-fāʿiḍa min biḥār al-quṭb al-maktūm. Rabāṭ: dar al-imān.

Ibn Arabi on Khatm al-Wilaya (Seal of Sainthood):
Ibn Arabi on Khatm al-Wilaya (Seal of Sainthood) 


Al-Hakim al-Tirmidhi r raised several questions in his book Khatm al-Awliya regarding the spiritual rank of the Seal of the Saints. His thirteenth question was: "Who is worthy of being called the ‘Seal of the Saints’ (Khatm al-Wilaya), just as Muhammad (may Allah bless him and keep him) is worthy of the title ‘Seal of Prophethood’ (Khatm al-Nubuwwah)?" More than three hundred years after al-Tirmidhi posed this question, Shaykh Muhammad ibn ‘Ali ibn al-‘Arabi al-Hatimi (d. 1240), renowned as Shaykh al-Akbar (The Greatest Shaykh), addressed this concept in his monumental and illuminating work, Al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya (The Meccan Revelations). His discussion of the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood preceded the physical birth of Shaykh Ahmad al-Tijani by over five hundred years: 


“As for the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood, it belongs to a man of the Arabs, of the noblest of them in lineage and power, who exists today in our own time. I was introduced to him (‘urriftu bi-hi) in the year 595 AH (1198), and I saw the distinguishing Sign (al-‘alamah) which he has, which The Real has hidden in him, concealed from the eyes of His servants (sci., mankind), but which He revealed to me in the city of Fez, so that I might discern in him the Seal of Sainthood (khatm al-Wilaya), he being the Seal of Absolute Prophecy (khatam al-nubuwah al-mutlaq) about which most people know nothing. Allah has afflicted (the Seal) with the people who refute and censure him (ahl al-inkar alayhi) concerning that which he ascertained from The Real in his innermost heart. But just as God has sealed the Prophethood of (all) Laws (nubuwat al-shara’i) with Muhammad (may Allah bless him and keep him), so has He sealed the Muhammad ‘Seal’ the Sainthood which emanates from the Muhammadan Heritage (al-wirth al-Muhammadi)—as opposed to what derives from the other Prophets. For, indeed, among the Saints are those who inherit from (the Prophets) Abraham, Moses and Jesus (etc.), so that these may well be found to exist after this Muhammadan Seal; but after him there shall be no Saint belonging to the Heart of Muhammad (‘ala qalbi Muhammad). This is the meaning of the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood…but I shall not name him.” 

Ibn al-‘Arabi, a towering figure in Islamic mysticism, introduces the concept of the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood (Khatm al-Wilaya al-Muhammadiyya), the final and most perfect saint (wali) inheriting directly from the spiritual legacy of the Prophet Muhammad. He describes this figure as an Arab of noble lineage who was alive during his time and whom he encountered in Fez in 595 AH (1198 CE). This Seal of Sainthood, he asserts, remains hidden from most of humanity but was revealed to him through divine knowledge. Ibn al-‘Arabi parallels this seal with the Seal of Prophethood (Khatm al-Nubuwwa), arguing that just as Muhammad was the last law-bearing prophet (nubuwat al-shara’i), this final Muhammadan saint marks the completion of a particular spiritual lineage deriving uniquely from Muhammad. He distinguishes this sainthood from those who inherit from other prophets, such as Abraham, Moses, and Jesus, suggesting that saints in their respective traditions may still arise, but none will partake in the direct "Heart of Muhammad" (ʿala qalbi Muhammad) after this final saint.
Ibn al-‘Arabi further notes that this figure will face opposition (ahl al-inkar alayhi) from those who reject or misunderstand his spiritual station, just as prophets and saints before him have faced resistance. Despite such opposition, his role is divinely determined, and his status remains unchanged regardless of public recognition or denial. Notably, Ibn al-‘Arabi declines to name this figure explicitly, leaving room for later interpretations. This passage has played a crucial role in Sufi discourse on sainthood, with later traditions, particularly the Tijaniyya Order, interpreting it as a prophecy foretelling Shaykh Ahmad al-Tijani (1737–1815) as the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood. However, because Ibn al-‘Arabi does not identify the figure, debates persist over the meaning and application of this concept within different Sufi traditions.

How to Meet a Shaykh with this Description and How is He:
How to Meet a Shaykh with this Description and How is He
Recognized

“The Shaykhs fitting this description are many. The majority of them are in the large cities because that is where they live. As for recognizing and meeting them, that is a difficult matter to achieve, rarer than the Red Sulfur, for they have taken on the appearance and the states of the normal folk. And whoever asks them about that state, they turn him away and reject him and give him the impression that they don't possess any of that. The defect that obliges them to that is that the general order of the universe has been corrupted by the will of the Real (Blessed and Exalted) from which there is no escape. So all human beings are completely immersed in their worldly pursuits and desires, rejecting the Divine Presence, and the rights and moral conduct it is due.
 In this time, the common folk do not rush to the Saints except desiring to fulfill corrupt aims such as the enjoyment of this world, its delights and passions, or to be saved from the afflictions and ruins of this abode, along with their entering into and persistence in highly disastrous and destructive habits from the greatest abominations which leave no end for their perpetrator except the abode of perdition. And they have no way out of this state of affairs, nor have they any means of entry into the sphere of returning to the Divine Presence. So when the Knowers of God recognized that this was the affair of the common folk, they veiled themselves to the common folk and warded them off in every circumstance and from every point of view. What that required was for them to live in desolate and uncultivated regions.

 However, the Real wanted from them that they should remain in the midst of the common folk and live amongst them for some matters that the Real wanted from them, Blessed and Exalted is He, which He had decreed for them. And they have no escape from His decree. So they did not see any way out of that, nor did they see any way to rectify the common folk and return them to the Divine Presence. So they are in the same position as the person who has been placed among a foolish mob who are stoning him, but has been tasked with being patient and remaining among them. He is in torment.
 For that reason, they have veiled themselves from the common folk and repelled them in every circumstance. But it is possible that the common folk sense the breeze of their arrival from behind a veil and pounce at (the opportunity) to connect themselves with them seeking what they desire of worldly pursuits. So the Knowers of God commingled with them in several different ways, covering themselves from the common folk by manifesting serious matters such as fornication, excessive lying, consuming alcohol, murder and other such destructive habits by which it is judged that the one who does them is in the displeasure of God and His punishment. But the matters in which the Knowers of God involve themselves in this sphere are only  forms that manifest from the unseen, having no reality for the most part. They are only imaginary forms that others see as a reality. 

And they do, in these forms, things that are
blameworthy according to the Sacred Law. But they in reality have not done a thing. So
they veiled themselves with this from the common folk, guarding their station and
avoiding their conduct. Knowing this, the fact is that the truthful and the liars have been commingled in this sphere. And one is not known from the other. And there is no power for anyone to recognize the accomplished knower completely or partially, except for a rare, most exceptional case. 

That is that some of the Complete Ones had manifested in the spheres of following the Sacred Law completely. So whoever manifests in this sphere and claims shaykhhood, then he is recognized by his calling to God, the Exalted,  to returning to Him, to abstaining from the world and its people and not being concerned  with it or its existence, along with the manifestation of the illumination in others upon his hand. If he should manifest himself to the seeker in this description, he should give himself over to him in the first meeting. What is required of the disciple, however, in this regard is that he should not give himself over to him until he has investigated the widespread stories about him from his trustworthy followers and his neighbors. And if the aforementioned description manifests from him, he should keep his company. If not, then no.
 Whoever desires to Connect himself to a shaykh in this time, yet does not find himself able to recognize one, and fears that he may the snares of the liars, should turn to God with absolute sincerity, fleeing to him with the heart at all times along with constantly humbling oneself before Him and humbly supplicating to Him to reveal to you the accomplished Shaykh who can deliver him from this darkness and that He lead him to him and enable him to follow his commands until he completely drowns in the waves of his ocean. For he is not capable of more than that. 

But greater and more important than that and more beneficial and more effective for obtaining his goal, and more exalted for  the one who does not have the capability of discovering a complete Shaykh is that he  should consume whatever time he has in sending a lot of blessings on the Prophet (may
Allah, bless him and give him peace) with proper décor and presence of the heart, and the conviction of the heart that he is sitting before him (may Allah bless him and give him peace. And he should persist in that. 
For whoever persists in that, and his earnestness to arrive before God is like the
earnestness of one dying of thirst to find water, trod will take him by the hand and pull him towards Himself either by assigning a complete, accomplished Shaykh to take him by the hand, or He will assign His Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace) to train him, or yet He may open a door to arrival and the lifting of the veils by reason of his adhering to sending blessings upon His Beloved (may Allah bless him and give him peace) Since that is the greatest means to God, the Exalted, and to arrival before him. And do one adheres to it, whatsoever, seeking arrival before God and ever fails.”


---
The Obligation of Seeking a Shaykh:
The Obligation of Seeking a Shaykh
Regarding the question about whether seeking a Shaykh is obligatory on every single
individual, or some people apart from others, and under what conditions:
In the Sacred Law, seeking a Shaykh is not obligatory in terms of legal obligations
whose performance is rewarded and whose neglect is punished. For there is nothing in
the Sacred Law that obligates that. Instead, it is obligatory from the standpoint of
discernment, like the dehydrated person, who, if he does not seek water will perish. For
him, it is obligatory to seek it, from the standpoint of discernment.

The standpoint of discernment in this (seeking a Shaykh) is what we had already
mentioned regarding humanity being created to worship God, and for focusing on the
Divine Presence by rejecting everything apart from it. The aspirant knows well the
impediments and hindrances- to his advancement towards the Divine Presence- exist
within him. He also knows his inability to rectify himself according to what he desires:
entrance into the Divine Presence and discharging its rights and the proper conduct
owed to it. And he knows that He has no escape from God and no savior if he should
agree with his ego, following its desires, turning away from God, the Exalted. So, from
this point of view, it is obligatory for him to seek a Complete Shaykh.

Therefore, this recognized obligation, although it is not from a legislative text, is a
natural and conventional conclusion- since there is nothing in the legislative texts except
for the obligation upon every single individual among the slaves to uphold the rights of
God, inwardly and outwardly. And there is no excuse for anyone to abandon that from
the standpoint of the Sacred Law, nor is there any excuse for his desires dominating
him nor his being incapable of rectifying himself. There is nothing in the Sacred Law
except that obligation and the prohibition of leaving that by obligating punishment upon
the perpetrator. That is what is in the Sacred Law. And there is no Shaykh who it is obligatory to follow except the Shaykh of instruction who teaches the manner of legislative matters whose performance is sought from the
slaves- commands, prohibitions, acting and refraining. It is obligatory for every ignorant
person to seek this Shaykh. And it is not proper for anyone to abandon that. But beyond
this, it is not obligatory according to the Sacred Law to seek a Shaykh. 

Instead, it isobligatory from the standpoint of discernment, in the same manner of the sick person
who has a puzzling illness, which he is unable to remedy from all angles, and his health
has diminished, we say, "If he wishes to remain in that illness, he remains." But, if he
wishes to become free of it and attain perfect health, we say to him, "It is imperative for
him to seek an adept physician who is familiar with the illness and its cause, as well as
the remedy to required to remove it and the method of treatment, in terms of amount,
method of administration, length of time and condition.

The Ta’ifa | al-Ifāda al-aḥmadiyya |:
The Ta’ifa | al-Ifāda al-aḥmadiyya |

A compilation of Shaikh al-Tijānī’s statements, entitled The Ahmadan Reports (al-Ifāda al-aḥmadiyya), assembled by Muḥammad al-Ṭayyib ibn Sīdī Muḥamad, commonly referred to as “al-Sufyānī) (hereafter al-Sufyānī) (d.1842) includes the former’s statements in alphabetical order. 


“There is a group amongst our companions whose maqam is such that all the aqtabs (spiritual poles) of this community fail to weigh against a single hair of the ocean of virtue of a single one of them.” —Shaikh Ahmad al Tijani r.a., Al Ifadah al ahmadiyya

 “if the Poles of this community were combined they could not outweigh a single hair of any members of a group amongst our companions.”  

The commentator on the text, the great scholar of prophetic traditions, Muḥammad al-Ḥāfiḍ al-Miṣrī, (d.1978) (hereafter al-Ḥāfiḍ) holds that, this statement does not override the status of the Prophet’s Companions, as their position is over and above discussion. Rather, these elite individuals are the “seniors of the people of experiential knowledge (al-maʿarifa) and spiritual training (al-tarbiyya).”  In another place, Shaikh al-Tijānī says, “an effulgence (fayḍa) will come to my Companions, until people will come to our path in waves. This effulgence will come when people are experiencing the extremes of constriction and difficulty.” 

al-Ḥāfiḍ clarifies: ‘He meant that this effulgence would come to many of his Companions, may Allah be pleased with him. The era for this to occur was deemed imminent.’  

In another place, Sheikh Tijani said: “A man has appeared from the group (al-ṭāʾifa).” 

al-Ḥāfiḍ concludes by saying that Shaikh al-Tijānī “did not identify this person but kept him exceedingly hidden. He did so until saying, ‘By Allah, He is unknown in this world nor the next.’ “

---
On Yaqutat al-Haqaiq:
On Yaqutat al-Haqaiq

The Prophet (peace and blessing be upon him) had also taught him the Prayer of “Yaqutat al-Haqaiq fi-Ta’ariif bi-Haqiqat Sayyid al-Khalaiq” (The Prayer of the Jewel of Realities in the Definition of the Reality of the Chieftain of Mankind). From the qualities of the latter is that if someone recites it twice in the morning and twice in the evening he would never face illusions in the Oneness of God (tawhid).” (Jawahir al-Maani) “And the Prayer of Yaqutat al-Haqaiq summarizes in full the Book of the “Meccan Openings” (al-Futuhat al-Makkiya) by Shaykh Ibn Arabi” (Mizab Rahma Rabbaniya) 

YĀQŪTAT AL-HAQĀ'IQ FĪ TA'ARĪF BI HAQĪQAT SAYYID AL-KHALĀ'IQ

 يَاقُوتَةُ الْحَقَائِقِ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ بِحَقِيقَةِ سَيِّدِ الْخَلَائِقِ 
THE RUBY OF REALITIES IN INTRODUCING THE REALITY OF THE MASTER OF CREATION
— Dictated by the Prophet (SAWS) to Shaykh Ahmad al-Tijani (RTA) —
(This Salat requires Special Ijazah from your Shaykh to recite)

بِسْمِ اللّٰهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحيمِ
In the name of Allah the most-Merciful the ever-Merciful
 
 
الله الله الله اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ اللهُ الَّذِي لاَ إِلَهَ إِلاَّ أَنْتَ
Allah Allah Allah. Allahumma ant Allahu lladhī Lā 'ilaha illā Anta,
Allah! Allah! Allah! O Allah you are Allah! And Besides You there is no other God!
 
 
العَلِيُّ فِي عَظَمَةِ انْفِرَادِ حَضْرَةِ أَحَدِيَّتِكَ التِي شِئْتَ فِيهَا بِوُجُودِ شُؤُونِكَ
Al-'Aliyyu fī 'azamati infirādi hadrati ahadiyyatika llatī shi'ta fīhā bi-wujūdi shu'ūnika
The Sublime in the vastness of the uniqueness of His Absolute Oneness/ Wherein You decided to manifest Your hidden affairs!
 
 
وَ أَنْشَأْتَ مِنْ نُورِكَ الكَامِلِ نَشْأَةَ الحَقِّ وَ أَنَطْتَهَا وَ جَعَلْتَهَا صُورَةً كَامِلَةً تاَمَّةً
wa ansha'ta min nūrika  al-Kāmili nash-at al-haqqi wa anattahā wa ja'altahā sūratan kāmilatan tāmmatan
And (then) You created from Your Perfect Light the manifestation of Truth/ And You binded (everything) to it and made it a complete & perfect Image!
 
 
تَجِدُ مِنْهَا بِسَبَبِ وُجُودِهَا مِنْ انْفِرَادِ أَحَدِيَّتِكَ قَبْلَ نَشْرِ أَشْبَاحِهَا
tajidu minhā bi-sababi wujūdihā min infirādi hadrati ahadiyyatika qabla nashri ashbāhihā
Who’s existence manifested the Uniqueness of Your Absolute Oneness before the appearance of its physical realities!
 
 
وَ جَعَلْتَ مِنْهَا فِيهَا بِسَبِبِهَا انْبِسَاطَ العِلْمِ
wa ja'alta minhā fīhā bi-sababihā inbisāt al-ilmi  And from it, through it and by it…You manifested all (Your) Knowledge
 
 
وَ جَعَلْتَ مِنْ أَثَرِ هَذِهِ العَظَمَةِ وَ مِنْ بَرَكَاتِهَا شَبْحَةَ الصُّوَرِ كُلِّهَا جَامِدِهَا وَ مُتَحَرِّكِهَا
wa ja'alta min athari hādhihi al-azamati wa min barakatihā shab-hat al-suwari kullihā jāmidihā wa mutaharrikihā
And from the impact of this Grandness and its blessings…/ You created all bodies, the still and the moving!
 
 
وَ أَنَطْتَهَا بِإقِبَالِ التَّحْرِيكِ وَالتَّسْكِينِ وَ جَعَلْتَهَا فِي إِحَاطَةِ العِزَّةِ
مِنْ كَوْنِهَا قَبِلَتْ مِنْهَا وَ فِيهَا وَ لَهَا 
wa anattahā bi-iqbāl al-tahrīki wa t-taskīni wa ja'altahā fī ihātat il-'izzati min kawnihā qabilat minhā wa fīhā wa lahā 
And You made all movement and stillness dependant on it!/ And You surrounded it with Your Might, as it emanated from it, in it and for it!
 
 
وَ تَشَعْشَعَتِ الصُّوَرُ البَارِزَةُ بِإِقْبَالِ الوُجُودِ
watasha-sha'ati s-suwar ul-bārizatu bi-iqbāl il-wujūdi
And so the images manifesting existence shined & appeared (in the universe)!  
 
 
وَ قَدَّرْتَ لَهَا وَ فِيهَا وَ مِنْهَا مَا يُمَاثِلُهَا مِمَّا يُطَابِقُ أَرْقَامَ صُوَرِهَا 
wa qaddarta lahā wa fīhā wa minhā mā yumāthiluhā mimmā yutābiqu arqāma suwarihā
And You proportioned for it, in it and from it, what suited it of its numerical value!
 
 
وَ حَكَمْتَ عَلَيْهَا بِالبُرُوزِ لِتَأْدِيَةِ مَا قَدَّرْتَهُ عَلَيْهَا
wa hakamta 'alayhā bi l-burūzi li-ta'adiyati mā qaddartaha 'alayhā
And You commanded it to manifest itself…to fulfil what You decreed for it!
 
 
وَ جَعَلْتَهَا مَنْقُوشَةً فِي لَوْحِهَا المَحْفُوظِ الذِي خُلِقَتْ مِنْهُ بِبَرَكَاتِهِ
wa ja'altahā manqūshatan fi law'hiha l-Mahfūzi lladhī khalaqta minhu bi-barakātihi
And You inscribed all of that in the Preserved Tablet / which itself was created from his grace!
 
 
وَ حَكَمْتَ عَلَيْهَا بِمَا أَرَدْتَ لَهَا وَ بِمَا تُرِيدُ بِهَا وَ جَعَلْتَ كُلَّ الكُلِّ فِي كُلِّكَ
wa hakamta 'alayhā bimā aradta lahā wa bimā turīdu bihā wa ja'alta kulla al-kulli fī kullika
And You prescribed for it what You wished for it and through it! / And You made the whole of this whole in Your Wholeness!
 
 
وَ جَعَلْتَ هَذَا الكُلَّ مِنْ كُلِّكَ وَ جَعَلْتَ الكُلَّ قَبْضَةً مِنْ نُورِ عَظَمَتِكَ
wa ja'alta hādhā l-kulla min kullika wa ja'alta l-kulla qabdatan min nūri 'azamatika
And You made this whole from Your Whole! / And You made the whole from a portion of Your Light!
 
  
رُوحاً لِمَا أَنْتَ أَهْلٌ لَهُ وَ لِمَا هُوَ أَهْلٌ لَكَ
rūhān limā anta ahlun lahu wa limā huwa ahlun laka.
And You made it the Spirit of what You deserve and what is deserving of You!
 
 
 
أَسْأَلُكَ اللَّهُمَّ بِمَرْتَبَةِ هَذِهِ العَظَمَةِ وَ إِطْلاَقِهَا فِي وُجْدٍ وَ عَدَمٍ 
As'aluka Allahumma bi-martabati hādhihi l-'Azamati wa itlāqihā fi wujdin wa 'adamin
O Allah! I ask You by the sublime rank of this Vastness
 and its Manifestation in creation and annihilation…
 
 
أَنْ تُصَلِّي وَ تُسَلِّمَ عَلَى تُرْجُمَانِ لِسَانِ القِدَمِ اللَّوْحِ المَحْفُوظِ وَ النُّورِ السَّارِي المَمْدُودِ
an tusallī wa tusallima 'alā tarjumāni lisāni l-qidami l-Lawhi l-Mahfūzi wa n-nūri s-sārī l-mamdūdi
To bless and salute the Articulator of the Tongue of Eternity!
(He who is) The Preserved Tablet and the All-Permeating Light!
 
  
الَّذِي لاَ يُدْرِكُهُ دَارِكٌ وَ لاَ يَلْحَقُهُ لاَحِقٌ الصِّرَاطِ الْمُسْتَقِيمِ نَاصِرِ الحَقِّ بِالحَقِّ
lladhī lā yudrikuhu dārikun walā yalhaquhu laahiqun. As-Sirāti l-mustaqīmi. Nāsiri l-Haqqi bil Haqqi.
He who cannot be comprehended by any comprehender or apprehended by any apprehender! (He who is) The Straight Path & the Supporter of the Truth by the Truth!
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ وَسَلِّمْ عَلَى أَشْرَفِ الخَلاَئِقِ الإِنْسَانِيَّةِ وَ الْجَانِّيَةِ صَاحِبِ الأَنْوَارِ الفَاخِرَة
Allahumma salli wa sallim 'alā ashrafi l-Khalā-iqi l-insāniyyati wa l-jāniyyati. Sāhibi l-anwāri l-fākhirati.
O Allah! Bless & salute the noblest among the Human and Spiritual beings!
The possessor of the greatest lights!
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ وَ سَلِّمْ عَلَيْهِ وَ عَلَى آلِهِ وَ عَلَى أَوْلاَدِهِ وَ أَزْوَاجِهِ وَ ذُرِّيَتِهِ
وَ أَهْلِ بَيْتِهِ وَ إِخْوَانِهِ مِنَ النَّبِيِّينَ وَ الصِّدِّيقِينَ
Allahumma salli wa sallim 'alayhi wa 'alā ālihi wa 'alā awlādihi wa azwājihi wa dhurriyatihi wa ahli baytihi wa ikhwānihi mina n-nabiyyīna wa s-siddiqīna
O Allah! Bless & salute him, his family, his children, his wives, his descendants,
his entire household, his brothers from the prophets, and the saints!
 
 
وَ عَلَى مَنْ آمَنَ بِهِ وَ اتَّبَعَهُ مِنَ الأوَّلِينَ وَ الآخِرِينَ
wa'alā man āmana bihi wa ttaba'ahu mina l-awwalīna wa l-ākhirīna.
And all those who believed in him & followed him, from the first till the last!
 
  
اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْ صَلاَتَنَا عَلَيْهِ مَقْبُولَةً لاَ مَرْدُودَةً
Allahumma aj'al salātanā 'alayhi maqbūlatan lā mar'dūdatan.
O Allah! Make our Salat on him accepted and not rejected!
 
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا وَ مَوْلاَنَا مُحَمَّدٍ وَ آلِهِ
Allahumma salli wa sallim a'lā sayyidinā wa mawlānā Muhammadin wa ālihi.
O Allah! Bless our leader & our master Muhammad and his family!
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ وَ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا رُوحاً وَ لِعِبَادَتِنَا سِرّاً
Allahumma waj'alhu lanā rūhān wa li-ibādatinā sirrān. 
O Allah! And make him (SAW) our (guiding) Spirit
and the Secret (of acceptance ) in all our acts of worship!
 
 
وَ اجْعَلِ اللَّهُمَّ مَحَبَّتَهُ لَنَا قُوَّةً أَسْتَعِينُ بِهَا عَلَى تَعْظِيمِهِ
Waj'al Allahumma mahabbatahu lanā qūtān asta'īnu bihā 'alā ta'zīmihi.
And O Allah! Make our love for him the strength that assists us in truly honoring him!
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ وَ اجْعَلْ تَعْظِيمَهُ فِي قُلُوبِنَا حَيَاةً أَقُومُ بِهَا وَ أَسْتَعِينُ بِهَا عَلَى ذِكْرِهِ وَ ذِكْرِ رَبِّهِ
Allahumma waj'al ta'azīmahu fī qulūbinā hayātan aqūmu bihā wa-sta'īnu bihā 'alā dhikrihi wa dhikri Rabbihi.
And O Allah! Make our honouring of him in the depth of our hearts...
 the life-support that assists me in remembering him and his Lord!
 
 
اللَّهُمَّ وَ اجْعَلْ صَلاتَنَا عَلَيْهِ مِفْتَاحًا
  Allahumma waj'al salātanā 'alayhi miftāhān
And O Allah! Make our Salat on him a key (to all blessings & to all knowledge of You)!
 
 
وَ افْتَحْ لَنَا بِهَا يَا رَبِّ حِجَابَ الإِقْبَالِ
waf'tah lanā biha Yaa Rabbi hijāb al-Iqbāli 
And open for us through it, the veil between us & between turning towards (You)
And between Your turning towards us (with Your grace and bounty)!   
 
 
وَ تَقَبَّلْ مِنِّي بِبَرَكَاتِ حَبِيبِي وَ حَبِيبِ عِبَادِكَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ
wa taqabbal minnī bi-barakati habībī wa habībi 'ibādik al-mu'minīna
And accept from me, through the blessings of my beloved (SAW)
and the beloved of all your believing servants…
 
 
مَا أَنَا أُؤَدِّيهِ مِنَ الأَوْرَادِ وَالأَذْكَارِ وَالْمَحَبَّةِ وَالتَّعْظِيمِ لِذَاِتكَ
mā anā u'addihi min al-awrādi wa l-dhkāri wa l-mahabbati wa t-ta'azīmi li-Dhātika. 
All that I recite from Awrad & Adhkar, and all my love and reverence for Your Being!
 
 
لِلَّه لِلَّه لِلَّه آهْ آمِينْ
Li-llahi Li-llahi Li-llahi. Ah. Ameen. 
Purely for Allah! Purely for Allah! Purely for Allah…..Ah! Amen!
 
 
هُوَ هُوَ هُوَ آمِينْ
Huwa Huwa Huwa. Ameen.
Him! Him! Him….Amen!
 
 
 وَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ آمِينْ 
Wa sall Allahu 'alā Sayyidinā Muhammadin....Āmīn.
And may Allah bless our master Muhammad! Amen!

Imams and Shuyukh of the Zawiya al-Kubra of Fes, Morocco:
Imams and Shuyukh of the Zawiya al-Kubra of Fes, Morocco 

The Imams
	•	1215–1230 AH → 1800–1815 CE: Seyyidina led the prayers.
	•	1230–1259 AH → 1815–1843 CE: Sherif Sidi Tayeb Wadghiry (Sefiani).
	•	1259–1300 AH → 1843–1883 CE: Sherif Mulay Tahar, son of Mulay Muhammad ben Abi Nasr El Alawi.
	•	1300–1306 AH → 1883–1889 CE: Ahmed ibn Ahmed Kala Bannani.
	•	1306–1326 AH → 1889–1908 CE: Hajj AbdSalam Kanun.
	•	1326–1365 AH → 1908–1946 CE: Sherif Ahmed Khayyat.
	•	Resignation of Sheikh Idriss El Iraqi: No specific Hijri year mentioned.

The Shuyukh of the Zawiya el Kubra of Fes
	•	1273 AH (1856 CE): Death of Sidi Abu Ya’za, son of Sidi Hajj Ali Harazim.
	•	1273–1300 AH (1856–1883 CE): Mulay Tahar El Alawi.
	•	1300–1316 AH (1883–1898 CE): Sidi Ghali, son of Sidi Musa ibn Mazuz.
	•	1316–1357 AH (1898–1938 CE): Sidi Mulay Tayeb, son of Sidi Ahmed, son of Sidi Tayeb Sefiani.
	•	1357–1367 AH (1938–1948 CE): Mulay Ghali Sefiani.
	•	1367 AH (1948 CE): Resignation of Sheikh Idriss El Iraqi.

al-Irshadat al-Rabbaniyyah 1.7 - The Night Journey and Ascension:
al-Irshadat al-Rabbaniyyah 1.7 - The Night Journey and Ascension
￼

---
The Shin & Manifestation of the Lord:
The Shin & Manifestation of the Lord 

It is narrated that both the righteous and the wicked will be presented with God in a form different from what they recognize. He will say, “I am your Lord,” but they will respond, “We seek refuge in God from you. We will stay in our place until our Lord comes to us. When our Lord comes, we will recognize Him.”

Then God will come to them in the form they recognize and say, “I am your Lord.” They will respond, “You are our Lord,” and they will fall in prostration before Him. However, only those who used to prostrate to God sincerely of their own accord will be able to do so, while those who prostrated out of hypocrisy, ostentation, or for show will find themselves unable to and will instead fall backward. This is the ultimate trial mentioned in the verse: “They will be called to prostrate, but they will not be able to” (Qalam: 43).

As for the phrase concerning “the unveiling” (kashf) and “the shin” (saq), the intended meaning here is the manifestation of that immense majesty and unparalleled perfection. This is what is meant by “the shin,” and the phrase is expressed metaphorically, following the customary idioms of the Arabs. Among them, when matters become severe and intense combat and great endurance are required, they say: “Now the shin has been unveiled”—meaning that doubt has vanished, and the false hope that hardship would not befall them has been dispelled. The covering has been removed, revealing the necessity of enduring hardships and remaining steadfast in the face of trials, with no room for doubt about their reality and no hope for their avoidance. Thus, they say, “The shin has been unveiled.”

This is in terms of the outward, apparent image that corresponds to the literal meaning.

Similarly, in this metaphor, a person facing extreme hardship, standing in the position of bravery, and enduring great burdens must “unveil his shin,” meaning he rolls up his sleeves, tightens his belt, and prepares himself to confront the hardships ahead. This is why it is said: “The shin has been unveiled.” —Sheikh Ahmad Tijani (ra) [Tafsir of Quran and Hadith]

Different Types of Slaves:
Different Types of Slaves 
وهي

وأما محبتهم له سبحانه وتعالى فإنما يحبون ذاته العلية المقدسة لا لا تعقل ولا تكيف وإنما يعقلها من ذاقها.

وفي معنى هذا قال المرسي رضي الله عنه : إن الله عبادا يظهرهم في البداية، ويسترهم في النهاية، وإن الله عبادًا يسترهم في البداية ويظهرهم في النهاية، وإن الله عبادًا يسترهم عن العامة، ويظهرهم للخاصة، وإن الله عبادا ضن بهم عن الخاصة والعامة، فلا يظهر حقيقة ما بينهم وبينه حتى للحفظة فمن سواهم، حتى يتوفى أرواحهم بيده، فهم شهداء الملكوت الأعلى، وهم أهل الصف الأيمن من العرش، فهؤلاء خاصة الخاصة جعلنا الله منهم جميعا بمنه وكرمه. ما أملاه علينا رضي الله عنه. انتهى

And as for their love for Him, Exalted and Most High, they love His exalted and sacred essence—without rationalizing it or defining it in any particular way. Rather, only the one who has tasted it can truly comprehend it.

Regarding this, al-Mursi (may Allah be pleased with him) said:

“Indeed, Allah has servants whom He manifests in the beginning and conceals in the end. And He has servants whom He conceals in the beginning and manifests in the end. And He has servants whom He hides from the common people but reveals to the elect. And He has servants whom He has withheld from both the elect and the common people, so that the reality of what is between them and Him remains hidden—even from the recording angels and all others—until He Himself takes their souls. These are the witnesses of the highest dominion, the people of the right side of the Throne. They are the most elect of the elect. May Allah make us all among them by His grace and generosity.”

This is what he (Sheikh Tijani ر ) dictated to us (may Allah be pleased with him).

معنى : ﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينَا مِمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ )

وسألته رضي الله عنه عن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِّمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنُ ﴾ الآية [النساء: ١٢٥].

فأجاب رضي الله عنه بقوله معناه : أنه لا أحد أحسن دينا ممن أسلم وجهه الله وهو محسن كما قال في الآية الأخرى: ﴿وَمَن يُسْلِمْ وَجْهَهُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ * الآية [لقمان: ٢٢].

والوجهة هنا التي يسلمها إلى الله هي توجه القلب إلى الله تعالى بالإدبار عن كل ما سواه.

١١ - يقول : إن الله لا ينظر إلى صوركم وأعمالكم ولكن ينظر إلى

(١١) م : ( ٤ / ١٩٨٧ رقم ٣٣ - ٣٤ / ٢٥٦٤) (٤٥) كتاب البر والصلة (١٠) باب تحريم ظلم المسلم - من حديث أبي هريرة.

ولفظه: «إن الله لا ينظر إلى أجسادكم ، ولا إلى صوركم ولكن ينظر إلى قلوبكم وأشار بإصبعه إلى صدره.

٤٩

Meaning of the Verse:

﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾
“And who is better in religion than one who submits his face to Allah while being a doer of good?” (Qur’an 4:125)

I asked him (may Allah be pleased with him) about the meaning of Allah’s statement:

﴿وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ دِينًا مِّمَّنْ أَسْلَمَ وَجْهَهُ لِلَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾ (Surah An-Nisa: 125)

He replied (may Allah be pleased with him), saying:

“Its meaning is that no one has a better religion than the one who submits his face to Allah while being a doer of good, as stated in another verse: ﴿وَمَن يُسْلِمْ وَجْهَهُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَهُوَ مُحْسِنٌ﴾ (Surah Luqman: 22).”

Here, the “face” that is submitted to Allah refers to the heart’s complete turning toward Allah and its turning away from everything else besides Him.

The Hadith:

The Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said:

“Indeed, Allah does not look at your forms or your deeds, but He looks at your hearts.”

(Reported by Abu Huraira, recorded in Sahih Muslim, Book of Righteousness and Relations, Chapter: The Prohibition of Wronging a Muslim, Hadith No. 1987 & 2564).

And in one narration:

“Indeed, Allah does not look at your bodies or your appearances, but He looks at your hearts,” and he (the Prophet) pointed to his chest with his finger.

Rimah on Tarbiyah (Umar Futi Tal):
Rimah on Tarbiyah (Umar Futi Tal) 


Tarbiyya before Shaykh Ibrahim

according to Tāl:
When one among those on the spiritual path was seeking the station of repentance and forgiveness
from his sins, he suddenly acquired a clear illumination (al-fatḥ al-mubīn). This is because such
wayfarers attain illumination quite suddenly, without their expectation for it. As a consequence,
such an illumination arrives from divine (rabbāniya) bestowal. None attains it except the
steadfastly convinced, the beloved knower, who is not captivated by mystical unveilings and
visible miracles. [The latter point is important because] if in the case his thought wanders to
mystical unveilings and visible miracles, and he thinks he has attained them through his own
skill, his foot will descend into the depths of destruction, and he will be completely unaware of
that. He will go astray, and then lead others astray, in the manner that has happened to many of
the misguided misguiders. Those who travel on the path and practice spiritual retreat without an
authorized teacher, or at the hands of an unqualified teacher, who does not even have basic
authorization for spiritual guidance, fail to understand the goal of spiritual training (tarbiya).476

Dua For Qutbaniyya, Ghawtiyyah, Khilafa, Fardaniya, Qutb:
Dua For Qutbaniyya, Ghawtiyyah, Khilafa, Fardaniya, Qutb 

“ The upshot is that You not cause me to die until
You have given me everything that You gave to them in all of their Qutbaniyyah, in their
life and their death, from everything that I mentioned and everything I did not mention
and everything that Your knowledge encompasses; and that You give me along with that
that Qutbaniyyah of every Qutb from the time of his being dispatched (may Allah bless
him and give him peace) until the blowing of the trumpet, however, it may be, the
Khilafah of each khalifah, the Ghawthiyah of every Ghawth, and the All-encompassing
nature of every All-encompassing Qutb and the uniqueness of every unique saint, from
the time of his being dispatched (may Allah bless him and give him peace) until the
blowing of the trumpet.”  (301) 

"And that You make my Station in this Qutbaniyyah, Uniqueness, Ghawthiya, Khilafa,
All-Encompassing so large to the point that the stations of all of the Qutbs, Unique
Saints, Ghawths, Khalifahs and All-encompassing saints, as well as that of the Knowers
of God, Lovers, Beloveds, Wayfarers and Attracted ones dwindle and fade before it; and
that you make my illumination in that, at every blinking of an eye and moment, in the
same proportion of the Night of Power to other nights. Rather increase it nonillion
times” (302) 

As for the entirety of what he sought, we will not mention it all right now due to its
immensity and because it contains some things that should not be revealed. We only
mentioned the upshot of it seeking blessing from it and that the grandeur of our Master
(may Allah be pleased with him), and his Perfection and Realization in the Station of the
Greatest Qutbship. Peace. (303)

On The Meaning of “Salat al-Fatihi”:
On The Meaning of “Salat al-Fatihi”

I asked him, may Allah be pleased with him, about the meaning of Salat al-Fatihi lima
Ughliq and he answered, may Allah be pleased with him:
It means (that he is) the Opener of what had been locked of all forms of being.” That is
because they had been locked behind the veil of hiddenness in the state of
nonexistence. And their locks were opened by the means of his existence (may Allah
bless him and give him peace). So they emerged from the state of nonexistence to the
state of existence, and from the veils of hiddenness to (become) themselves in the
world of manifestation, since, if it were not for him, Allah would not have created any
being, nor would He caused it to emerge from non-existence to existence. That is one of
the meanings.
The Second is that he opened the locks of the doors of Divine Mercy. And by means of
him they were opened to the creation. And had Allah (Exalted is He) not created our
Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and give him peace), He would not have had
mercy on any created being. So mercy arrives from Allah to His creation by means of
His Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace). The third of its meanings is that the hearts were trapped in polytheism and filled with it.
And faith found no way of entering them. Then, they were opened by his call (may Allah
bless him and give him peace)] so that faith entered them and purified them of
polytheism. So they were filled with belief and wisdom. His saying, The Seal of what went before refers to Prophethood and Messengerhood,
since he sealed them both and locked their door (may Allah bless him and give him
peace). So there is no hope for (attaining) it for anyone after him. Likewise (he is) the
Seal of what went before of all kinds of Divine Manifestations by which the Real
(Blessed and Exalted) revealed Himself in the world of outward manifestation. That is
because he (may Allah bless him and give him peace) is the first being that Allah
caused to exist, emerging from the veils of hiddenness, and the state of Divine
Obscurity, to the universe. Then the forms of the universe continued to expand by the
manifestations of different species, according to the order erected by the Divine Will,
species after species, until the last of what He revealed Himself in, in the world of
manifestation, was the Adamic form- upon his own form (may Allah bless him and give
him peace). And that is what is meant by the "Adamic form.” Thus, just as the manifestation of existence was opened by him, the manifestation of
the different forms of being was sealed by him (may Allah bless him and give him
peace).
---
On the Muhammadan Reality:
On the Muhammadan Reality 

Expressing it another way, he said (may Allah be pleased with him):
The first being that Allah (Exalted is He) caused to exist from the Hidden Presence is
the spirit [ruh] of our Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and give him peace).
Then Allah caused the souls of the universe to descend from his soul (may Allah bless
him and give him peace). The spirit, here, is the means by which life stretched forth into
the bodies. And He created from his soul (may Allah bless him and give him peace), the
bodies of light, such as the Angels and those who resemble them. As for the thick
bodies of darkness, they were only created from a second connection belonging to his
soul (may Allah bless him and give him peace). That is because, his soul (may Allah
bless him and give him peace), has two connections, both of which He outpoured onto
all of existence. The first connection is that of pure light. From it were created all of the souls and the
bodies of light, which contain no darkness. The second connection that belongs to his
soul (may Allah bless him and give him peace) is that of darkness. And from this
connection were created the bodies of darkness, like the devils, thick bodies, and Hell
and its pits. Likewise, Paradise and all of its levels were created from the connection of
light. Thus, that is the relationship of all of existence with his soul (may Allah bless him
and give him peace).

As for the Muhammadan Reality (may Allah bless him and give him peace), it is the first
thing that Allah caused to exist from the Hidden Presence. And there was not with Allah
any created being before that. But this reality is not known as a “thing.” Some scholars
had deviated by examining this reality. They said:
This reality is singular. Nothing exists with it. But it cannot avoid being either a
substance or an accident. If it were a form, it would be in need of a place to indwell.
Then it would not be independent of another existent thing. That is because if it comes
to exist along with its place all at one time, it has no precedence, because, in that case,
they are two. If it were an accident and not a substance, then accidences are not even
addressed because an accident only exists for the blinking of an eye. Then it ceases.
So, where is the precedence that you speak of?

The answer to this issue is that it is a substantial reality, which has two connections: one
of light and one of darkness. As for its needing a place, this limitation is not sound. That
is because this limitation is has been laid down by those whose intellects are firmly
rooted in the Station of Forms. But what is confirmed is that Allah (Exalted is He) is able
to create these created beings without any place for them to indwell. The intellect’s
deeming this matter impossible is due to the impossibility that bodies should exist
without a place. That is because that is nature upon which Allah (Exalted is He) has
created them, and in which the intellect is firmly rooted. And it was not set free in the
unlimited existence of realities. If it had been set free in the unlimited existence of
realities, it would have known that Allah (Exalted is He) is capable of creating the universe without a place. This being the case, Allah created the Muhammadan Reality
as a substance, without the need of a place. And there is no doubt that if the Divine
Reality is unveiled to anyone, he will know certainly and unequivocally that causing the
universe to exist without a place is absolutely and verifiably possible.
As for the Muhammadan Reality, it is not known or perceived in that degree. And there
is no hope for anyone to reach it in that sphere. Then it was appropriated robes of
Divine Light and was veiled by them from the creation. And in this sphere, it is called "a
soul," after being veiled by the robes. And that is the limit of the knowledge of the
Prophets, Messengers, and Qutbs. They arrive at this place and stop. Then it
was appropriated more robes of Divine Light and, because of them, it was called "
intellect." Then it was appropriated more robes of Divine Light. And because of them, it
was called " heart." Then it was appropriated even more robes of Divine Light. And
because of them, it was called "a soul." Then, after that, his blessed body (may Allah
bless him and give him peace), manifested.And the Saints differ in their knowledge of these degrees. So the highest knowledge
that a group of them possess is that of his soul (may Allah bless him and give him
peace). And they have sciences, secrets and knowledge of that. And the highest
knowledge that a group of them possess is that of his heart (may Allah bless him and
give him peace). And they have different sciences, secrets and knowledge in that. And
the highest knowledge that another group of them possesses is that of his intellect. And
they have differing sciences, secrets and knowledge in that. But a group of them- the
highest of them- has reached the limit of knowledge. So they gain knowledge of the
Station of his Soul (may Allah bless him and give him peace). And that is the highest
form of knowledge. And there is no hope for anyone to know his reality in the original
form in which it was created.
And in this regard Abu Zayd says:

"I dived into the abyss of knowledge, seeking to know the source of the reality of the
Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace). But there were between it and me
one thousand veils of light. If I had lifted the first veil, I would have disintegrated, just as
a hair disintegrates when thrown into a fire."
Likewise, Shaykh Mawlana ʼAbd as-Salam said, in his prayer upon the Prophet (may
Allah bless him and give him peace):
“Before him, intellects dwindle. And it is disclosed to neither the first nor the last among
us."
In the same way, Uways al-Qarni said (may Allah be pleased with him), to our Master
ʼUmar and our Master ʼAli (may Allah be pleased with them both):
“You only saw the shadow of the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and give him
peace).”
They said:
“Not even Ibn Abi Qahafah (Abu Bakr as-Siddiq)?”
He said:
“Not even Ibn Abi Qahafah.”
And maybe he had dived into the abyss of knowledge seeking to know the source of the
Muhammadan Reality, and it was said to him:
258
"That is a matter that the greatest Messengers and Prophets were incapable of. So
there is no hope for other than them in it."

Continuity and Special Transmission: The Prophet’s Ongoing Spiritual…:
Continuity and Special Transmission: The Prophet’s Ongoing Spiritual Influence and Divine Mercy After His Passing (Jawahir al-Ma’ani, 248) 

This passage presents a nuanced exploration of the relationship between general and special commands from the Prophet Muhammad (may Allah bless him and give him peace), the transmission of knowledge after his passing, and the distinction between obligatory and non-obligatory actions in Islamic teachings. Below is an analysis and ordered breakdown of the key points discussed:

1. Distinction Between General and Special Commands
	•	General Commands: These are rules or injunctions meant for the entire community during the Prophet’s lifetime. These include the basic prohibitions and obligations, which were shared with all.
	•	Special Commands: These are tailored for an elite group within the community, chosen by the Prophet. These commands were not universally applied but given to a select few companions who were spiritually or intellectually prepared for them.
	•	Posthumous Transmission: After the Prophet’s death, only the special commands are transmitted to the elite. The ability to transmit general commands ended with his passing.

2. Misunderstanding of the Prophet’s Ongoing Influence
	•	Opposition to the Idea of Finality After Death: The passage refutes the belief that the Prophet’s influence ended upon his death, likening him to other deceased individuals. It stresses the enduring presence of his special guidance for the elite, which continues even after his physical death.
	•	Spiritual Status of the Prophet: Those who deny the ongoing special transmission are considered ignorant of the Prophet’s elevated status and are warned that such beliefs could lead to disbelief unless repented.

3. The Prophet’s Knowledge of Future Grace
	•	Prophet’s Awareness: The Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace) knew about the grace and spiritual benefits that would manifest later in time, even though it was not disclosed to his companions.
	•	Reasons for Non-Disclosure:
	1.	Timing: The Prophet understood that the right time for these benefits to materialize had not yet arrived, and there was no one at that moment capable of manifesting them.
	2.	Avoiding Premature Revelation: If the Prophet had shared these benefits, the companions’ eagerness might have led to requests for further explanation, but their circumstances were not conducive to such manifestations.

4. Mercy and Generosity of Allah
	•	Allah, in His mercy, has chosen to offer vast rewards for relatively small actions in times of spiritual weakness and negligence, providing great benefits for actions that would otherwise seem insignificant. This reflects divine generosity in the context of human spiritual conditions.

5. Consistency Between Prophet’s Life and After Death
	•	The passage reiterates that while the Prophet’s practices were largely consistent between his life and after his death, the main difference is the transmission of general versus special commands. The special commands continue to flow to the elite, but the universal rulings, once transmitted, ended with his death.

6. Distinction Between Obligatory and Non-Obligatory Actions
	•	Obligatory Actions: The passage notes that the special benefits discussed do not apply to obligatory actions, such as prayer. The hadith about the excellence of performing prayer at its earliest time underscores the ongoing importance of obligatory actions.
	•	Non-Obligatory Actions: The special benefit discussed earlier, such as the multiplied rewards of prayers upon the Prophet or specific litanies, applies to non-obligatory actions, where the benefits are greater than those of earlier generations of worshipers.

7. Recitation and Rewards
	•	Greater Benefits of Recitation: The passage compares the benefits of reciting prayers upon the Prophet, especially in the form of Salat al-Fatihi, suggesting that its reward surpasses the combined rewards of the prayers of earlier generations of believers.
	•	Da’irah al-Ihatah: The recitation of Da’irah al-Ihatah is mentioned as an exception where this multiplication of reward does not apply, though its specific nature is not explained.

Conclusion:

The passage provides a sophisticated view of the Prophet’s ongoing spiritual influence, emphasizing the distinction between general and special commands, the Prophet’s foresight of future grace, and the continued relevance of his teachings for the elite after his death. It encourages a deeper understanding of the enduring spiritual benefits, especially for non-obligatory actions, while maintaining a focus on the mercy of Allah in granting rewards for small actions in times of spiritual weakness.
——-

“And our Master (may Allah be pleased with him) had responded to this (apparent)
contradiction, saying:
"There is no contradiction between this and what has been narrated about the benefit of
the Qur'an and the Noble Word, since the benefit of the Qur'an and the Noble Word are
general and were meant for the entire community, while this is a special. And there is no
contradiction between them since he (may Allah bless him and give him peace) used to
transmit the general rulings to the entire community during his lifetime. I mean that
when He would forbid something, he would forbid it for everyone; and when he would
enjoin something, he would enjoin it upon everyone. And the same went for the rest of
the external verdicts of the Sacred Law. But at the same time, he would (may Allah
bless him and give him peace) transmit the special verdicts to the elite. And he would
choose for some matters some of his companions apart from others. This is widespread
and apparent in his reports (may Allah bless him and give him peace).
Then when he was transferred to the Abode Hereafter- and he is in that just as he was
in life (may Allah bless him and give him peace)- he began to only transmit to his
Community the special commands to the elite. And it is not possible to transmit general
commands to the entire Community. That was cut off by his passing away (may Allah
bless him and give him peace). But his outpouring of the special commands to the elite
remains. Whoever assumes that all of his benefit for his Community (may Allah bless
him and give him peace) ended with his passing away- just like all other dead people,
he is ignorant of the degree of the Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace)
and has bad conduct with him. And it is feared that he will die a disbeliever if he does
not repent from that belief.
248
I asked our Master (may Allah bless him and give him peace) if the Master of Existence
(may Allah bless him and give him peace) had known in his time about this grace that
would come later. He replied, “Yes. He knew about it.” I then asked, “If it has
indescribable benefit is in it, why then did he not mention it to his companions (may
Allah be pleased with them all)?
He replied:
Two things prevented him. The first is that he knew that its time would only come later
and that at that time, there was no one at that time upon whose hand Allah could
manifest it. The second is that if he had mentioned to them this great benefit through
such small deeds, they would have asked him to explain it to them, due to the strength
of their avidness for all that was good. But its manifestation was not possible at that
time. For that reason, he did not mention it to them.
Yet another angle is that since Allah (Blessed and Exalted) knew the weakness of the
people of this time, and their condition of negligence and corruption, He had mercy
upon them and was generous with them (by giving them) a lot of benefit in exchange for
few actions. He chooses for His mercy whom He wills at the time that He wills. And it
should not be said, “His traditions after his death is not the same as his traditions during
his life. Rather they are the same in everything that he was related (may Allah bless him
and give him peace), except in the aforementioned division of general rules to all people
and the special rules for the elite.
Then he said (may Allah be pleased with him):
The aforementioned benefit is with regards actions that are not obligatory. As for those
that are obligatory, it does not apply, due to the hadith:
249
“What action is best, O Messenger of Allah?” He replied (may Allah bless him and
give him peace), “Prayer at the beginning of its time.”
26
I said to our Master (may Allah bless him and give him peace):
“It can be understood from what has preceded that the reciter of the aforementioned
prayer upon the Prophet has a greater benefit than all of the believing, worshipers of
Allah that preceded him, since Salat al-Fatihi is worth the multiplied reward of all of their
prayer upon the Prophets upon the Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace),
and all of their remembrances and litanies; except for in one case, which is the
recitation of Da’irah al-Ihatah. There is no mention of that here, and the multiplication of
reward does not apply to it.

Testing the Shaykh:
Testing the Shaykh
As for your question about putting the Shaykh to the test and evaluating his actions and
states, that is not proper, and no one follows that path and succeed at all, since that is a
Cause for the closing of the doors of God, the Exalted. And whoever desires that and
follows that with all people, God, the Exalted, will show him the attribute of deficiency of
all people, so that he will not trust anyone. As for belief in the Shaykh, it is a Divine
command which God places in the heart I so that the one who possesses it is not
capable of separating from him, even if he should see, from him, one thousand acts of
disobedience. However, if he is a sincere disciple, the reward for his sincerity is that he
will not see from the Shaykh anything, except what causes his heart to be at ease
regarding him. And that only happens with a true Shaykh. But whoever's inner is impure,
and Seeks defects, he will only see what causes him to deny him and attribute
deficiency to him, and what requires turning away from him and Showing him enmity.
---
He also said (may Allah be pleased with him)::
He also said (may Allah be pleased with him):
You should know that the Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace) during his
life, used to transmit general verdicts to all, meaning if he prohibited something, he
prohibited it to everyone. And if he made something obligatory, he made it obligatory on
everyone. Likewise, with all of the verdicts of the outward law. However, he (may Allah
bless him and give him peace) used to transmit the special commands to the special ones. 
And he used to choose some matters for some of his companions apart from
others. This is widespread and well-known in his traditional reports (may Allah bless him
and give him peace. Then, when he had been transported to the abode of the Hereafter- and he is, there,
alive just as he was in the world, he began to transmit to his nation the special matters
to the special ones. But, there is no entrance to the general matters here, since that was
cut off by his death (may Allah bless him and give him peace. However, his outpouring
of the special matters to the special ones remains. Whoever assumes that all of his
support for his community (may Allah bless him and give him peace) was cut off, just as
is the case with all other dead people, is ignorant of his station (may Allah bless him and
give him peace) and has bad manners towards him. And it is feared for him that he will
have a bad ending. We ask God for safety, sufficiency and to die with the best of
endings.

He said (may Allah be pleased with him)::
He said (may Allah be pleased with him):

“You should know that God, Blessed and Exalted, decreed, in His pre-eternal will, that
the support that reaches His creation, from the outpouring of His mercy- in every era,
should circulate among the Elect Exalted people among His creation, from among the
Prophets and the Siddiqs. So whoever takes refuge with the living Elect Exalted people
of his era, keeps their company, follows them and seeks assistance from them, will
succeed at attaining the support that outpours from God. But whoever rejects the
People of his era, sufficing himself with the words of those who preceded him among
the saints who had passed on, he is stamped with the stamp of deprivation. His likeness
is that of those who rejected the Prophet of their time and his legislation, sufficing
themselves with the legislations of the Prophets who came before him, so they were
recorded with the stamp of disbelief. We seek refuge in God from that.”

The proof that companionship is only to the living is his saying (may Allah bless him and
give him peace) to Abi Juhayfah:

“Ask the scholars [ulama’], mix with the wise [hukama’] and keep the company of
the Great Saints [kubara’].” [Narrated by al-Tabarani]

The guidance of the scholar (al-‘alim) is in general matters, commanding and
prohibiting, according to what brings about praise from God and prevents the suffering
of the slave. The end of that is Paradise.

The guidance of the wise person (al-hakim) is towards drawing near to God, the
Exalted, by purifying oneself from the passions of the ego and from following one’s
desires. The end of that is the different levels of nearness.

The guidance of the Great one (al-Kabir) is to God, the Exalted, by way of erasure of
the ego and becoming free from self-direction in all that brings about its rectification in
this world and the next, and all that distances from it harm in this world and the next.
The end of that is God.

What is taken from this is that companionship is only to the living since the dead do not
keep company, do not speak and do not mix with others."


---
On the Abrogation of the Paths:
On the Abrogation of the Paths 

The Shaykh [al-Tijani] said, may God the Exalted be well pleased with him: “All the paths are included in the path of ash-Shādhilī, may God the Exalted be well pleased with him, except this Muḥammadan lbrahīmī Ḥanīfī path of ours, for it is self-sufficient.”

He [Sheikh Tijani] also said, may God the Exalted be well pleased with him: “all the paths will be incorporated into ours, so they will be rendered obsolete. Our stamp will be imprinted on every stamp, and our stamp will carry no other.”
---
On Afiya:
On Afiya 

Sīdī ʿAlī Ḥarāzim says in Jawāhir al-Maʿānī vol. 2, p. 136:
He [i.e. the author] asked him (may God be pleased with him) about well-being (ʿāfiyah) and its reality.
He replied:
“Know that the reality of well-being is to stand with God (taʿālā) in perfect conformity to His will, with complete acceptance (riḍā), submission (taslīm), delegation (tafwīḍ), and surrender (istislām), with no personal maneuvering or self-importance. It is [to remain in] perpetual renunciation of all personal considerations, attachments, alliances, and self-serving desires, so that one has nothing besides God at every moment—unceasingly and forever. The measure and verification of this is that nothing other than God ever crosses his heart, at any time, always. That is well-being. And if you ask God for well-being, do it from the vantage by which He knows it to be [true] well-being for you, not from what you want or choose.”
---
Stamp of Deprivation:
Stamp of Deprivation 

“The stamp of deprivation is on whoever rejects people of his age and adheres to the words of the dead friends [of Allah] before him.”

Kitab al-Jami, 77 
---
Sheikh Tijani on the Unknowability of the Essence of the Essence…:
Sheikh Tijani on the Unknowability of the Essence of the Essence 

Shaikh at Tijani on the Unknowability of the Essence of the Essence:

All those of experiential knowledge, may God be pleased with them, know, without exception know it is the essence of the level (ayn al martaba) not the essence of the Essence (ayn al dhat) as the Truth’s level (martaba), glorified is He, is the Divnity (uluhiya). The Essence is in utter hiddenness. No one other than Him knows It, glorified is He. Nothing has appeared in existence but the level (martaba). The Essence is hidden. None can perceive it. It is in utter hiddenness. The level (martaba) is the epitome of manifestation. Whatever you hear of the words of the experiential knowers, may God be pleased with them, [say] that He is the Manifest (ath thaahir) and that nothing has existence but He, they only intend the level in that [expression], not the manifestation of the Essence. 

[Kitaab al jaami 346]

---
Kitab al-Jami On “You did not see anything Wonderous”:
Kitab al-Jami On “You did not see anything Wonderous” 

Al-Mishry documented Shaikh al-Tijānī’s having mentioned the following verses attributed to some of the Seniors (al-akābir) and the Shaikh’s commentary on them:

A Reality whose ability has manifested in the universe/existence (al-kawn).
	Thus, It manifested these beings (al-akwān) and veils.
The essences of the worlds disguised it just as it is
	Known by the hearts of the Erudite Knowers (al-ʿurrafa al-udabāʿ).
All creatures are the veils of Its appearance.
	Most of the affair (jumlat l’amr) became Its leaders (al-nuqabāʿ).
There is nothing wondrous hidden in existent things,
	Rather, their being Its essence [is wondrous] thus you have not seen anything amazing.

———————————
Our master said (ra) regarding their meaning:

‘The ‘Reality’ here is Absolute Existence (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) termed the Essence of Obliteration (ʿayn al-ṭams) and the Cloud (al-ʿamā). There is nothing relative to it, it is unimaginable nor intellected. It has no location, how, trace, or fantasy (wahm). All relationships with it have been annihilated. The ability that the Reality manifests is the first veil of Obliteration and the Cloud. The Attributes and Names are completely inconceivable there. It is primary in the treasured veil wherein He said: ‘I was an unknown hidden treasure, and I loved to be known.’ He meant that He loved to appear to other than Himself. ‘Thus, I created the creation and made Myself known to them, thus, they knew Me through Me.’ This ability is what He expanded in the existent things since He caused the existent things to appear through this ability. (pg.213)

‘[The essences of the world] disguised it,’ etc., The act of disguising here is to be veiled from the other, for in the essence of its existence, it is in the zenith of appearance and clarity because when it manifested ‘other’ and ‘otherness’ is obliterated. The one who sees It has no doubt nor delusion regarding It. It is in the epitome of manifestation in that [case]. It is then disguised by the appearance of existent entities (al-mawjūdāt). This is the meaning of ‘It was disguised’ after having been in the zenith of experiential knowledge, it was then obliterated in ‘other’ and ‘otherness.’ It was disguised by existence when the latter manifested. In other words, It was veiled by existence through the forms of existent things.

His words ‘the essences of the world’s entities disguised it’ here means that the ʿayn of something is its essence. It is called an ʿayn due to its specification from the Lordly Cloud (al-ʿamā al-rabbānī). They are called essences here and are the essences of existent entities.

His words:  ‘…just as it is Known by the hearts of the Erudite Knowers’ means: experiential knowers (al-ʿurrāf) is the plural of experential knower ʿ(ārif). The term here implies those experiential knowers who have become acquainted with the etiquettes of the Divine Presence (al-ḥadra al-ilāhiyya), and as a result, the Reality acquainted Itself with their hearts. The veil of the universe has been lifted from the hearts of the experiential knowers. Thus, they can designate the Holy Presence (al-ḥaḍra al-qudsiyya) directly, just as one drowned in the ocean does not require someone else to inform them about it.

His words: All creatures are the veils of Its appearance means they appropriate them. In other words, Absolute Existence through the forms of the existential events (al-akwān) and all of creation are the veils of Its appearance.

His words: ‘The bulk of the affair,’ etc., Linguistically, leaders means those who bear a responsibility. As the Prophet (s.a.w.s.) took the allegiance of the Helpers in Makkah and they pledged their allegiance to him to carry out all of his provisions with a condition that anyone who refused to do so would be in a state of dishonor and degradation, he was not convinced until he had taken some leaders. Leaders were responsible for making sure any tribe member who refused would be dishonored, incapable of rebelling or fighting and to assist his enemies against him. He appointed leaders amongst them due to this burden. They are those who bear the responsibility placed upon them in this issue. He said (s.w.t.) to the Children of Israil after having taken their oath from them: ‘and We delegated twelve leaders amongst them.’ (5:12)

His words: ‘The bulk of the affair,’ etc., here are all the forms of existent things. Each of them, one by one have become Its leaders. Their purpose is that they all bear the burden of the weight of their experiential knowledge. This is the heaviest of affairs. They bear the burden of their glorification, worship, and prostration to It, meaning the Absolute Essence. Each individual existent thing is a leader in this sense. All of them praise Him. Thus, the Truth is an Essence and a Level. The Essence is unseen and inconceivable. He has not manifested in His Existence but through a level. This level is Divinity (al-ulūhiyya). (pg.215) The meaning of the verses, then is that all of existence is focused on Him with submssive worship, abasement, experiential knowledge, glorification, and prostration. No atom is outside of this place.

His words: ‘There is nothing wondrous hidden in existent things’, etc, refers to it being nothing wondrous to be hidden in them. His words: ‘Rather, their being Its Essence, meaning the Essence of Absolute Existence. The meaning of ‘His being their Essence’ is that the universe has a mirror that they appear in only some people’s light is strong so they witness the mirror and the One manifesting in it. Whoever’s light is weak sees the One manifesting in the mirror but the Existence of the One who manifests veils them from the mirror. Thus, they don't see other than Him, meaning other than the Truth, may He be glorified. One in this state says: “The entire universe is Allah (t.w.t.) there is nothing in it but Him” due to the weakness of his light. 

The poet says:

So none remains but Allah, nothing other than Him
	There is no arrival nor one who arrives

The one whose light is strong witnesses the mirror and the One who manifests therein. He gives every level its right of reality (ḥaqiyya) and creation (khalqiyya). One does not veil him from the other.

As for His words ‘thus you have not seen anything amazing,’ the word mā here means  ‘that which’ (al-ladhī). When Ibn ʿArabī al-Ḥatimī met Aaron (a.s.s.) he said that he said to him, ‘O Prophet of Allah! Your words: ‘...so let not the enemies rejoice over me…’ (7:150) where are the enemies (pg.216)  that you indicate? Is there anything outside of Allah?’ or however it was that he said it. ‘We Knowers see that everything is Allah. How can one imagine there be enemies? Our master Aaron (a.s.s.) said: ‘All that you see is Him simultaneously.'  He said: ‘No.’ Aaron said to him: ‘To the extent that you do not know this experientially is the degree to which you have failed to witness of Him.’1 (Al Mishry N.d, Vo1.  213-217)

The Ta’ifa:
The Ta’ifa 
طائفة من صحبه لو اجتمع
أقطاب أمة النبي المتبع
ما وزنوا شعرة من فرد
منهم فكيف بالامام الفرد

A group of his companions, if they gathered,

The Poles of the Prophet’s following nation,

Would not weigh the weight of a hair from a single one of them,

So how then could they compare to the unique Imam?”

(Munyat al Murid)

Varying experiences of the Arifeen:
Varying experiences of the Arifeen 

“Every one of the Awliya (friends of Allah) is truthful in what he claimed, since each one of them is given in His presence what others were not given. And he hears an address in his presence—an address particular to him.

Allah outpours on every Wali in His presence abundant good and great bestowal whose worth is known only to the one on who it is bestowed. And each of the Arifin has a presence specific to him. Perhaps it is possible that some of them share a single presence as a group. But, they would differ in their experience of it according to the Divine distribution. 
- Sidi Ahmad Tijani (ra)

Scale of the Sharia:
Scale of the Sharia 
Shaikh al-Tijani (ra) said:
“If you hear something from me, weigh it against the scale of the law; take what conforms and leave what does not.”

Allah’s Deception/Scheme:
Allah’s Deception/Scheme 

Shaikh Al-Tijani (ra) said: 
"Everything I mentioned to you on this path is real, if we are spared from the deception of God. The Messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, despite their esteemed rank and high position, did not feel secure from the deception of God ('none feel secure from the deception of God, except the losing people')."
